# Adversarial Audit — 2026-07-16 QA Session (39-agent fleet, full findings)

**Auditor:** Claude Fable 5 orchestrating 14 probes + 24 adversarial verifiers + 1 completeness critic (~4M tokens).
**Subject:** QA_SESSION_REPORT_2026-07-16.md — commits lexa-hub e0864c9/29e9552, csip-tls-test fbcaca0/3e907f2, findings A–E, soak evidence.
**Method:** every claim treated as hypothesis; every critical/high finding independently re-verified by a second agent instructed to refute it. Verdicts: CONFIRMED / PARTLY (real, but root cause or fix corrected) / REFUTED.

---

## Probe: commit-e0864c9-export-cap

**Probe summary:** Deep-reviewed lexa-hub e0864c9 ("cap plan-followed discharge under an active export limit"): read the full diff, the current optimizer.go plan-rule/export-rule/import-rule/safety region (lines 387-606, 700-874, 944-1250, 2235-2445), cmd/hub/state.go's meter staleness/frozen handling, constraint/economics.go + constraint/shadow.go for shadow parity, the 3 added tests, and the prior session's raw mayhem logs. The core design is sound and its documented properties check out numerically: the signed (unfloored) base-export correctly credits local load on a net-importing site, the measured-discharge subtraction makes the absolute cap stable through a discharge ramp-down, NaN passthrough keeps plans byte-identical with no cap, and multi-battery distribution plus rule ordering cannot overshoot the capped aggregate or produce duplicate commands. However I found one real correctness bug the tests miss: a CHARGING battery is excluded from the discharge sum (optimizer.go:750 `b.PowerW > 0`), so its draw is miscredited as local load and the cap is inflated by the full charge magnitude — empirically confirmed (4800 W returned where true headroom is 1800 W), causing a 1-2 tick kW-scale export breach at every charge->discharge plan transition under an active cap (the canonical daily peak-onset pattern). Second, the admitted shadow-parity gap is confirmed and is worse than the report's framing: constraint/economics.go applyPlan has no cap, the diff is candidate-scoped with the candidate expressing an opinion, so every binding-cap tick counts a divergence — post-commit soak data cannot pass the export flip's ~0-diff gate. Third, a frozen (still-publishing) meter turns the cap into a self-inflating value that silently fails open to pre-fix behavior, and the frozen-meter exclusion can never engage at night because worldMoving is derived from inverters only — exactly the peak-discharge window. The bench PASS claims are corroborated by the raw rerun log. Overall judgment: a good, well-documented fix for the scenario it targeted, with an unpinned charging-transient bug, an inherited frozen-meter blind spot, and a soak-gate poisoning that needs the economics.go port plus a soak-clock restart.

### EXPCAP-1 [high/bug/confidence=high] — **verifier: CONFIRMED**
**planExportDischargeCapW ignores a CHARGING battery, inflating the cap by the full charge magnitude at every charge->discharge plan transition under an active export limit**

**Evidence:** optimizer.go:748-754 sums only POSITIVE battery power: `measuredDischargeW := 0.0; for _, b := range state.Batteries { if b.Connected && b.PowerW > 0 { measuredDischargeW += b.PowerW } }; baseExportW = signedNetExportW - measuredDischargeW`. A charging pack (PowerW < 0) is excluded, so its draw is silently credited as permanent local load. Since netExport = trueBase + batterySigned, with charge the computed baseExport = trueBase - |charge|, so cap = conservative - baseExport is OVERSTATED by |charge|. Empirically demonstrated with a throwaway unit test against the real function (removed after run): solar 0, load 1000 W, battery charging 3000 W (NetW=+4000), export limit 1000 W -> planExportDischargeCapW returned 4800 W where the true headroom is 1800 W (conservative 800 + load 1000). Commanding a 4800 W discharge (the plan wants 5000) lands the meter at 4800-1000 = 3800 W export against a 1000 W cap for ~1-2 ticks until the recomputed cap self-corrects (next tick: base = 3800-4800 = -1000, cap = 1800). The canonical daily plan flips charge->discharge exactly at peak-hour onset, so under a standing export cap this transient can recur daily. The commit message and doc comment (optimizer.go:722, 739) only describe 'signed net export minus the discharge now flowing' and never consider the charging case; none of the 3 added tests exercise PowerW < 0 with an armed cap.

**Root cause:** baseExport is meant to be 'export attributable to everything BUT the battery', which requires subtracting the SIGNED battery power (discharge positive, charge negative). The code floors the subtraction at discharge-only, mirroring applyImportLimitRule's measuredDischargeW pattern (optimizer.go:2272-2277) where discharge-only is correct, but here it misclassifies battery charging as immovable site load.

**Proposed fix:** Subtract signed battery power: `if b.Connected && !math.IsNaN(b.PowerW) { measuredBatterySignedW += b.PowerW }; baseExportW = signedNetExportW - measuredBatterySignedW`. This leaves all three pinned cases (net-export steady, net-import load credit, discharge ramp-down) numerically identical and fixes the charging case (cap 1800 W in the example above). Add a regression test with PowerW < 0.

**Blast radius:** Transient (one to two engine ticks, 15-30 s at stock cadence, plus device ramp) meter over-export past an active CSIP/OpenADR export cap, magnitude up to the pack's charge rate (kW-scale). Self-correcting; bounded by the plan's own setW. Occurs at plan charge->discharge boundaries and whenever an export cap arrives mid-charge with a discharge plan pending. Could re-degrade the very mayhem scenarios this commit closed if the sim ever starts the episode with the pack charging.

**Verifier reasoning:** Read the function myself: internal/orchestrator/optimizer.go:745-756 sums only b.PowerW > 0 (discharge) and computes baseExportW = signedNetExportW - measuredDischargeW, so a charging pack (PowerW < 0 = charging, pinned by convergence_test.go:84 and optimizer_test.go:542) is credited as immovable site load. Hand-recomputed the claimed example against the real code (NetW=+4000 with load 1000 + charge 3000, exportLimitW=1000, default margin 0.20 at optimizer.go:733-737): base = -4000, cap = max(0, 800-(-4000)) = 4800 W vs true headroom 1800 W — inflated by exactly the 3000 W charge magnitude, matching the finding. No same-tick backstop exists: applyPlanRule fires at optimizer.go:436 before applyExportLimitRule at :441, which (per commit e0864c9's own message) never reduces a battery discharge and reacts only to measured NetW, which that tick still shows import; self-correction occurs on the next tick when the recomputed base subtracts the now-flowing discharge. Test gap confirmed: the three tests added by e0864c9 (optimizer_rules_test.go:1364-1462) use ruleBat with PowerW=5000 or 0 only; grep shows no PowerW<0 case under an armed cap. The proposed signed-subtraction fix is correct: it is numerically identical on all three pinned cases (signed sum == discharge-only sum when no pack is charging), semantically right because applyPlanRule distributes the plan setpoint across ALL connected batteries (a charging pack is re-commanded on discharge, not immovable), and the NaN guard preserves the existing filter's implicit NaN exclusion. Root-cause attribution to the applyImportLimitRule discharge-only template (optimizer.go:2271-2277) is plausible and the cited pattern exists verbatim; discharge-only is correct there for its import-conservation identity. Severity=high is appropriate: transient over-export bounded to ~1 engine tick + device ramp, self-correcting, but recurs at every charge→discharge plan transition (daily peak onset) under a standing cap and can spuriously open a CannotComply episode under a CSIP obligation — real but transient wrong control behavior, no safety guard defeated.

**Verifier corrections:** None needed. Minor precision note: the finding's "1-2 ticks" duration is right for the recompute path; actual meter exposure additionally includes battery ramp latency, same as the physical ramp-down transient the commit already accepts. The fix as proposed (signed sum over Connected, NaN-guarded packs) is complete; the regression test should pin the exact example (NetW=+4000, PowerW=-3000, limit 1000 → cap 1800).

### EXPCAP-2 [medium/design-flaw/confidence=high]
**Shadow candidate (constraint/economics.go applyPlan) was not given the cap: every binding-cap tick is a counted shadow divergence, poisoning the >=1-week 0-diff gate for the export active flip**

**Evidence:** Verified in code: constraint/economics.go:285-337 `applyPlan` distributes `setW := target.BattSetpointW` with NO planDischargeCapW parameter or clamp (only device limits + SOC clamps, lines 313-323), while the live path clamps at optimizer.go:782-787. The shadow diff IS candidate-scoped but the candidate expresses an opinion here (economics.go:325 `e.setBattery(b.Name, share)`), so shadow.go:834-872 diffBattery compares live capped share (e.g. 1050 W) vs candidate uncapped share (5000 W) — far outside the tolerance band (shadow.go:107-114: max(150 W, 5%)) — and compare() increments w.count + the battery-setpoint axis tally every such tick (shadow.go:544-554). These divergences are NOT filtered by FIX-F attributeAndFilter because their author is the economics constraint, not an active one. The QA report itself admits this at line 90 ('Follow-up noted, NOT done'). Consequence: with `constraint_shadow:true` on the bench, every tick where an export cap binds a plan discharge (exactly the openadr-limit-adopt / openadr-csip-precedence scenarios now in the regression rotation) inflates lexa_constraint_shadow_divergence_total, so soak data collected after e0864c9 cannot pass the ~0-diff gate CLAUDE.md requires before the `export: active` flip — and worse, a reviewer triaging the soak could waste days chasing 'economics' divergences that are really this known parity gap.

**Root cause:** The fix was applied to the authoritative cascade only; the ported constraint-package twin (the P5 migration candidate) was left behind, breaking the both-sides-or-neither discipline CLAUDE.md's defensive-fault-handling section mandates for ported logic.

**Proposed fix:** Port planExportDischargeCapW into EconomicsConstraint.applyPlan (it already has effectiveExportLimitW at economics.go:146 and st.Grid.NetW/st.Batteries available) in the same change that fixes EXPCAP-1, then restart the shadow soak clock. Until then, annotate the soak dashboard that battery-setpoint divergences coinciding with export caps are expected.

**Blast radius:** No live control impact (candidate plans are discarded, shadow.go:396-404). Process impact: the export-flip soak gate is silently invalidated from 2026-07-15 onward; divergence metrics/logs are noisy on every export-cap scenario.

### EXPCAP-3 [medium/design-flaw/confidence=high]
**Frozen (not silent) meter makes the cap self-inflate each tick — the new guard fails open to pre-fix behavior, and frozen-meter exclusion cannot engage at night because worldMoving is inverter-only**

**Evidence:** Cap arithmetic: cap_n = conservative - (frozenNetExport - measuredDischarge_{n-1}) (optimizer.go:745-756). With NetW frozen (meter still publishing an unchanged value) but battery telemetry fresh, each tick's actuated discharge is added back into the next tick's cap: cap_{n} = conservative - frozenExport + cap_{n-1} — a positive feedback that grows until setW = min(planSetW, cap) saturates at the full uncapped plan value. So the guard this commit adds silently evaporates under a frozen meter (it never commands MORE than the plan, so it degrades exactly to the pre-fix breach, sustained rather than transient). The convergence backstop is blind to it: checkExportLimitConvergence (optimizer.go:443, 1494) reads the same frozen netW. The frozen-meter defense exists (cmd/hub/state.go:671-691 excludes a frozen meter -> NetW=NaN) but is gated on worldMoving, which state.go:614-623 sets ONLY from `dc.Role == "inverter"` W changes within solarMovingWindow=20s (state.go:39-43). At night — precisely when peak-TOU plan discharge runs — solar W is flat, worldMoving stays false, and a stuck meter is never excluded even while the battery it is supposed to measure ramps by kilowatts. A truly SILENT meter is handled correctly (measStaleAfter=60s -> NetW=NaN, state.go:682).

**Root cause:** The measured-discharge subtraction that makes the cap ramp-stable assumes the meter co-moves with the battery; a frozen meter breaks that assumption into a per-tick additive error. The pre-existing worldMoving gate never anticipated battery movement as evidence the world is moving.

**Proposed fix:** (a) Extend worldMoving in cmd/hub/state.go to also consider battery W changes (a discharging pack is the strongest possible evidence a flat meter is stuck); (b) optionally clamp the cap's tick-over-tick growth (e.g. cap may not grow faster than the measured export headroom shrinks) so a frozen meter degrades to a stable, not inflating, cap.

**Blast radius:** Under a single frozen-meter fault with an active export cap and a discharge plan: sustained export past the cap up to the plan's full setW, undetected by every export oracle in the hub (all read the same frozen NetW). Not a regression vs pre-commit (which had no cap at all), but the new guard gives false confidence — the mayhem meter-freeze fault class combined with openadr-limit scenarios would expose it.

### EXPCAP-5 [medium/test-blindspot/confidence=high]
**Added tests pin the happy paths but none of the failure modes above; ev_storage discharge is not covered by the cap at all**

**Evidence:** The 3 added tests (optimizer_rules_test.go:1364-1462, verified passing with `go test -run 'TestPlanExportDischargeCapW|TestPlanRule_Discharge|TestOptimize_PlanDischargeRespectsExportCap'`) pin: net-exporting steady/mid-ramp-down cap arithmetic (discharging 5000 W capped to 1050 — this single point IS the ramp-down stability case), net-importing load credit under a 0 W cap (idle pack, NetW=+250 -> 250 W), NaN-limit => NaN cap, NaN cap => full passthrough, charge plan (-3000 W) untouched, and the full-Optimize path with both over- and under-cap assertions (>1100 fails, <=0 fails). NOT pinned: (1) a CHARGING pack when the cap is computed (EXPCAP-1 — my throwaway test fails today: 4800 W vs true 1800 W); (2) NetW=NaN fallback value (EXPCAP-4); (3) any multi-tick sequence (frozen-meter inflation, EXPCAP-3, needs one); (4) multi-battery distribution under a binding cap with device/SOC clamps; (5) shadow parity (no test asserts constraint economics.applyPlan matches — EXPCAP-2 would have been caught by a Wrap()-based test with an export cap + plan target). Also unpinned and un-capped: a WP-14 ev_storage plan EV-discharge (target.EVSetpointW > 0, optimizer.go:858-862) is grid export the cap never bounds — dormant while ev_storage defaults false, but the same class of hole this commit fixed for batteries.

**Root cause:** Tests were written from the fix's own mental model (discharge-only, meter present) rather than adversarially against the estimator's inputs.

**Proposed fix:** Add: charging-pack cap test (fails today — fix EXPCAP-1 first), NetW=NaN cap-value test, a 3-tick frozen-meter sequence test, a two-pack proportional-distribution-under-cap test, and a shadow Wrapper parity test with export cap + plan discharge. Note the ev_storage gap in the WP-14 task file.

**Blast radius:** Regression protection only covers the exact bench scenario shape that failed; the estimator's wrong-input behaviors are unguarded.

### EXPCAP-4 [low/design-flaw/confidence=high]
**NetW=NaN fallback (base=0 => cap=conservative limit) is more permissive than the sibling autonomous rule's no-meter fallback**

**Evidence:** planExportDischargeCapW: `baseExportW := 0.0; if !math.IsNaN(state.Grid.NetW) {...}` (optimizer.go:745-746) — no meter => cap = conservativeW regardless of solar. The autonomous TOU cap right below uses `exportNowW = math.Max(0, surplusW)` when NetW is NaN (optimizer.go:509-511), where surplusW=solarW meterless (computePowerBalance, optimizer.go:708-709) — i.e. it debits solar generation from the headroom; the plan cap does not. A meterless site with solar producing near the limit can thus be commanded conservativeW of plan discharge on top of unmetered solar export. Partially mitigated: Rule 3's own meterless fallback reconstructs signedNetExport from device telemetry (optimizer.go:974-983) and will curtail solar to hold the cap — an economically inverted outcome (curtail PV to make room for battery discharge) rather than an uncorrected breach.

**Root cause:** The fallback comment (optimizer.go:742-744) reasons only about the battery's own contribution ('a pure-discharge bound that can never itself exceed the cap') and ignores concurrent unmetered solar export, unlike the sibling rule two screens down.

**Proposed fix:** Mirror the autonomous rule: meterless base = max(0, surplusW) (or reconstruct from device telemetry as Rule 3 does), i.e. cap = max(0, conservativeW - solar-derived export estimate).

**Blast radius:** Meterless or meter-stale (>60 s) sites only; Rule 3's solar curtailment mostly converts the error into wrong economics rather than a compliance breach.

### EXPCAP-OK-1 [info/ok-verified/confidence=high]
**Sign conventions and steady-state/ramp-down arithmetic of the cap are correct for net-exporting sites, net-importing load credit, and discharge mid-ramp**

**Evidence:** Grid.NetW convention pinned at optimizer.go:691-696 (>0 import, <0 export); signedNetExportW := -state.Grid.NetW (optimizer.go:747) is consistent. Worked numerically against the code: (a) net-exporting: NetW=-4750 with 5000 W measured discharge, limit 1000 => base = 4750-5000 = -250 (250 W load), cap = 800-(-250) = 1050; actuating 1050 lands export at 1050-250 = 800 = conservative limit, and re-evaluating with the settled meter (NetW=-800, discharge 1050) reproduces base=-250, cap=1050 — stable. (b) net-importing idle: NetW=+250, 0 W cap => base=-250, cap=250 = discharge exactly up to local load, exporting nothing (signed, unfloored base is what makes this work — the comment at optimizer.go:740-742 is accurate). (c) discharge mid-ramp-down (commanded 1050, meter still shows the old 5000 W flowing): base = 4750-5000 = -250, cap unchanged at 1050 — no oscillation, exactly the claimed absolute-bound property. Final math.Max(0,...) (optimizer.go:756) prevents a negative cap from ever flipping a discharge plan into a forced value. The one direction NOT handled is charge (EXPCAP-1).

### EXPCAP-OK-2 [info/ok-verified/confidence=high]
**Multi-battery redistribution cannot overshoot the capped aggregate, and rule ordering has no duplicate-command/last-writer hazard**

**Evidence:** Distribution (optimizer.go:806-834): share = setW*cap/totalCap with per-device clamps `math.Max(-b.MaxChargeW, math.Min(b.MaxDischargeW, share))` and SOC clamps that only reduce toward 0 — shares sum to <= capped setW, so device-level clamping can only UNDER-deliver, never overshoot the cap (headroom lost to a clamped pack is not redistributed — conservative). Ordering: the cap is computed and applied in Rule 2.5 (optimizer.go:433-436) BEFORE Rule 3 (line 441); Rule 3's battery-absorb lever explicitly skips plan-commanded packs (`hasBatteryCommand(plan.BatteryCommands, b.Name)`, optimizer.go:1086) so it never re-commands them; Rule 3.5 deliberately MAY raise a plan discharge to defend an import cap but does so by in-place overwrite via batteryCommandIndex (optimizer.go:2400-2411), as does checkBatterySafety's forced disconnect (optimizer.go:1879-1888). Every battery therefore carries at most ONE BatteryCommand per plan — there is no duplicate for the desired-doc actuator to dedupe/mis-order. Rule 3.5 raising the discharge above planDischargeCapW is only reachable while the site is importing over an import cap, where extra discharge reduces import and cannot breach the export cap.

### EXPCAP-OK-3 [info/ok-verified/confidence=medium]
**Commit's bench claims corroborated: both OpenADR scenarios PASS in the raw rerun log, and the 3 added tests pass**

**Evidence:** Raw artifact /tmp/.../7cbd4a28.../scratchpad/mayhem-openadr-rerun.log lines 6-13: 'PASS exportCap <= 1000 W held, correctly attributed (an OpenADR-only bind (no CSIP control active))', 'PASS exportCap <= 0 W held, correctly attributed (a CSIP control (mRID DERC-SP-AD...) ... binding tighter than the injected OpenADR cap)', 'PASS 2 DEGRADED 0 FAIL 0 BLIND 0 INCONCLUSIVE 0' — matching the commit message and QA report line 86 (including the CannotComply attribution claims, which I did not independently re-derive from hub journals — that part is corroborated-by-log, not code-verified). `go test ./internal/orchestrator/ -run 'TestPlanExportDischargeCapW|TestPlanRule_Discharge|TestOptimize_PlanDischargeRespectsExportCap'` => ok. Confidence medium only because the log is the prior session's own artifact (same provenance as the report), not an independent re-run.

## Probe: commit-29e9552-fixed-pf

**Probe summary:** Deep-reviewed lexa-hub commit 29e9552 (fixed-PF convergence two-sided). Read cmd/modbus/reconcile_adv.go in full (1878 lines: synthesizeLocked, all axes, executeLocked/recordMeasuredWriteLocked, transitionLocked), internal/reconcile/reconcile.go (backoff/episode core), the vendored lexa-proto sunspec/derbase PF read+write paths (Parse701, L701 layout, SetFixedPF/write704), the updated test, the QA report §2.2 claim, and the prior session's raw bench artifacts. The fix itself is correct and verified: the two-sided |measured−commanded| ≤ 0.02 check replaces a genuinely wrong one-sided ceiling, matches fixed_var's setpoint discipline, and the report's live-bench claim is corroborated by artifacts (pf-alone-capture.log shows fixed_pf pending→diverged→NonConvergedBegin under the injected 0.90 command; mayhem-pf-alone.log line 16 PASS). However the check compares magnitudes only: the commanded excitation (over/under-excited, carried as sign on the target and as 704 PFWInj_Ext on the wire) is verified nowhere — model 701 PF is unsigned (Tuint16) so measured PF carries no direction, the signed model-701 Var (which the adjacent fixed_var axis already uses) is not consulted, and PFWInj_Ext is never read back — so an inverter delivering rated VARs in the WRONG direction is judged adopted. Secondary issues: the two-sided band adds a second undamped decision boundary with no hysteresis (a converged sample resets the backoff cursor, so band-edge dither yields an immediate corrective 704 RMW write per divergence onset — the exact boundary-dither class the same session's report flags as open findings B/D); the fixed 0.02 PF-unit band is degenerate near unity (commanded ≥0.98 admits PF=1.0, i.e. zero VARs, so accept-but-ignore is still undetectable there); and the commit's test swap removed the only assertion of the far-side (shortfall) divergence direction, leaving two-sidedness half-pinned. Low-power hold behavior is verified correct with no false-clear path.

### PF-1 [high/bug/confidence=high] — **verifier: CONFIRMED**
**Fixed-PF convergence verifies magnitude only — wrong-excitation (leading vs lagging) VARs at the right |PF| are judged adopted**

**Evidence:** VERIFIED IN CODE. cmd/modbus/reconcile_adv.go:1230-1247 (synthesizeLocked, AdvAxisFixedPF): `target := rn.target.fields[reconcile.FixedPF] // signed` … `want := math.Abs(target); got := math.Abs(m.PF)` … `if math.Abs(got-want) <= advPFBand { … advVerdictConverged }` — the sign carrying excitation (advAxisTargets reconcile_adv.go:857-867: `signed := rm.FixedPF.PF; if !rm.FixedPF.OverExcited { signed = -signed }`) is stripped before comparison, and the diverged synthesis `math.Copysign(got, target)` (line 1247) stamps the TARGET's sign onto the measured magnitude so the core's FixedPF tolerance check can never see a sign mismatch either. Measured PF from SunSpec model 701 is unsigned by transcription — vendor/lexa-proto/sunspec/derlayout.go:27 `FS("PF", Tuint16, "PF_SF")`, decoded via View.Float's Tuint16 branch (layout.go) and Parse701 (der1547.go:74) — so |PF| carries no direction on the wire; the ONLY measured direction signal is the signed Var point (derlayout.go: `FS("Var", Tint16, "Var_SF")`, der1547.go:73), which is present in the same device.Measurements and already used by the fixed_var axis (reconcile_adv.go:1259 `math.Abs(m.Var-targetVar)` — signed, so fixed_var DOES catch wrong-direction vars) but is never consulted in the fixed_pf case. Excitation is also never verified at the provisioning layer: the write sets 704 PFWInj_Ext (vendor/lexa-proto/derbase/derbase.go:371-386 SetFixedPF), but the only 704 readback the shell does is the Ena point for releases (ReadFuncEnabled, reconcile_adv.go:389-406) — grep for OverExcited/Ext in reconcile_adv.go shows only write-side uses (860, 1414, 1416, 1845). Net: a device commanded 0.90 over-excited that runs 0.90 under-excited (absorbing instead of injecting VARs — e.g. aggravating an over-voltage event instead of relieving it) reports adopt_state=adopted; a re-issued doc that only flips OverExcited transitions to pending and re-adopts on the next in-band |PF| sample without the excitation change ever being verified.

**Root cause:** The convergence check was designed around the unsigned model-701 PF point and never widened to a direction check; the natural direction oracle (sign of measured Var, or a 704 Ext readback) exists in the same code paths but is unused for this axis.

**Proposed fix:** In synthesizeLocked's FixedPF case, when |W| ≥ advPFAssessMinW and |PF| is in-band, additionally require sign(m.Var) to agree with the commanded excitation (over-excited ⇒ Var injection ⇒ m.Var > 0 under the 701 sign convention) with a small dead-band around Var≈0 (where direction is meaningless because commanded PF≈1); alternatively/additionally read back PFWInj_Ext during the slow reassert. Add a regression test: commanded 0.90 over-excited, measured PF 0.90 with m.Var < 0 ⇒ diverged.

**Blast radius:** Any device under fixed-PF advanced control with reconciler.adv="active" (7xx via 704, 12x via M123 where the sign convention mirrors Ext — reconcile_adv.go:481-486). Gated today: configs ship reconciler.adv="off", so product default is unaffected; on a commissioned CSIP/CSIP-AUS site with adv active, wrong-direction reactive support from a faulty device passes silently and no CannotComply is raised.

**Verifier reasoning:** Every cited code location verified by direct read. (1) cmd/modbus/reconcile_adv.go:1231-1247: fixed-PF convergence compares want:=math.Abs(target) vs got:=math.Abs(m.PF) — magnitude only; the diverged synthesis math.Copysign(got, target) (line 1247) stamps the TARGET's sign onto the measurement and the converged branch returns target verbatim (1245), so the core reconciler's signed tolerance check (internal/reconcile/reconcile.go:462, math.Abs(read[f]-want) > tolerance — which WOULD catch -0.90 vs +0.90) can never see a sign mismatch. (2) Signed target built at reconcile_adv.go:858-866 (signed := rm.FixedPF.PF; if !rm.FixedPF.OverExcited { signed = -signed }). (3) Measured 701 PF is unsigned on the wire: vendor/lexa-proto/sunspec/derlayout.go:27 FS("PF", Tuint16, "PF_SF"), der1547.go:74. (4) The direction oracle exists and is unused: m.Var is signed (derlayout.go:26 Tint16; derbase.go:139 documents "positive = capacitive", consistent with over-excited=injection) and is consulted signed by the adjacent fixed_var case (reconcile_adv.go:1259) but never in the fixed_pf case (1230-1247 reads only m.PF/m.W); the 704 PFWInjExt point is parsed (der1547.go:184) but the shell's only 704 readback is the Ena register (reconcile_adv.go:380-381, 389-406); grep confirms OverExcited appears only at write/format sites (860, 1414, 1416, 1845). (5) No compensating check elsewhere: zero non-test OverExcited hits in cmd/hub, internal/reconcile, internal/orchestrator; FixedPF uses the scalar field, not the AdvContent fingerprint. (6) No test coverage: TestAdvShell_FixedPFMeasuredConvergence (reconcile_adv_test.go:578-628) never sets m.Var or tests excitation mismatch. Failure scenario, root cause, and proposed fix (sign(m.Var) agreement with commanded excitation under a near-unity Var dead-band, plus optional 704 Ext readback on the slow reassert; regression test commanded 0.90 over-excited with in-band |PF| but m.Var<0 => diverged) are all correct and consistent with the codebase's own documented conventions.

**Verifier corrections:** Only a minor precision nit, not affecting the verdict: the claim "measured PF is unsigned by transcription" is exactly true for the 701 path (Tuint16), but the legacy 10x path DOES decode a signed PF (vendor/lexa-proto/derbase/derbase.go:229, ApplyScaleSigned(...)/100.0) — irrelevant in practice because synthesizeLocked's math.Abs(m.PF) strips any sign on every path. Severity=high is defensible (the initial write does command the correct excitation; the defect is the verification oracle certifying an accept-but-ignore device), though one could argue critical since wrong-direction reactive power judged "adopted" can aggravate a voltage event on a real site with no alarm.

### PF-2 [medium/design-flaw/confidence=high]
**Two-sided band adds a second undamped decision boundary: band-edge dither produces immediate corrective 704 writes plus retained-report/log churn (the report's own §8 boundary-dither class)**

**Evidence:** VERIFIED IN CODE (mechanics), inferred (occurrence rate). Converge band == diverge band, no hysteresis: reconcile_adv.go:1244 `if math.Abs(got-want) <= advPFBand`. Each verdict flips adoptState via transitionLocked (reconcile_adv.go:1180-1186), which publishes a RETAINED report per transition (1741-1758) and logs each edge. Write pacing: internal/reconcile/reconcile.go:325-327 — a converged sample resets `r.divergentSince = time.Time{}; r.writeAttempts = 0`; the next diverged sample (Observe lines 339-346) sets divergentSince and calls backoffReady, and reconcile.go:417-419 `if r.writeAttempts == 0 { return true }` makes the FIRST write of every new divergence episode immediate. So a measured PF alternating across a band edge poll-to-poll defeats the advMinRetryBackoff (15 s) entirely: one 704 whole-block RMW write (derbase.go write704 — full-model read+write) per 2 polls, indefinitely (every ~20 s at the default poll_interval_s 10, cmd/modbus/config.go:157-158), plus an adopt_state flap log line and retained MQTT publish per poll. Pre-commit, one such boundary existed (want−band); the commit adds the second (want+band) — and near-unity commands sit close to it (PF-3). The same session's report explicitly names this defect shape as its top open theme (QA_SESSION_REPORT_2026-07-16.md §8: guards "chatter or breach when a value straddles a decision boundary… They should hold-bias at the line", findings B/D) yet the landed fix introduces a new instance without hysteresis or a mention.

**Root cause:** No hysteresis/debounce between the converge and diverge verdicts, combined with the reconcile core's episode-reset semantics (converged sample zeroes the backoff cursor).

**Proposed fix:** Either (a) hysteresis: diverge at |got−want| > band but re-converge only at |got−want| ≤ band·0.5 (or require N consecutive in-band samples), or (b) do not reset writeAttempts to 0 on a single converged sample (require sustained convergence before re-arming the immediate first write). Same treatment applies to fixed_var, which shares the shape.

**Blast radius:** Bounded (poll-cadence-limited, ≥10 s between writes in practice) but indefinite: Modbus write churn on the inverter's 704 block, retained-report churn on lexa/reconcile/adv/+/report, journald volume (FLASH_BUDGET discipline), and adopt_state flapping visible to the hub's breach-episode machinery.

### PF-3 [medium/design-flaw/confidence=high]
**advPFBand=0.02 in PF units is degenerate near unity: commanded PF ≥ 0.98 still cannot detect accept-but-ignore (unity/zero-VARs is in-band)**

**Evidence:** VERIFIED IN CODE (math from the quoted check, reconcile_adv.go:1244). For commanded PF w, the in-band set is [w−0.02, min(w+0.02, 1)]. At w=0.98: measured PF 1.0 (zero VARs delivered) satisfies |1.0−0.98| ≤ 0.02 ⇒ adopted, while the requested reactive power was Q/S = sqrt(1−0.98²) ≈ 19.9% of VA — a ~20%-of-nameplate reactive shortfall passes as converged. The PF-unit band is nonlinear in reactive terms: d(Q/S)/dPF = PF/sqrt(1−PF²), so ±0.02 PF ≈ ±2.7% S at PF 0.80, ±4.1% at 0.90, ±6.1% at 0.95, ±9.8% at 0.98. Against IEEE 1547-2018's steady-state reactive-power measurement accuracy (±5% of VA rating, the basis 1547.1 evaluation uses), the band is defensible only mid-range (0.85–0.92); it is looser than the accuracy floor above 0.93 and collapses entirely as w+band crosses 1. The commit's own rationale ("an inverter left near unity while commanded 0.90 is NOT providing the requested VARs") therefore still fails for near-unity commands, which CSIP-AUS programs commonly issue (0.95–0.98 lagging). The adjacent fixed_var axis already does the principled thing: a Q-domain band as a fraction of the reactive rating (advVarBandFrac=0.05·VarRatingVar, reconcile_adv.go:1259), and the rating plumbing (advCaps.VarRatingVar via 702, reconcile_adv.go:251-268) already exists.

**Root cause:** Tolerance chosen in PF units rather than reactive-power units; PF is a nonlinear, saturating measure of Q.

**Proposed fix:** Judge fixed-PF convergence in the Q domain: expected Q = |W|·tan(acos(w)); diverge when |measured Var − expected Q| exceeds max(advVarBandFrac·VarRatingVar, k·|W|), falling back to the PF-unit band only when Var/rating are unavailable. This also naturally carries the excitation sign check from PF-1.

**Blast radius:** Fixed-PF advanced control with near-unity commanded values — the accept-but-ignore fault class the commit was written to close remains open for that command range.

### PF-4 [medium/test-blindspot/confidence=high]
**Test swap removed the only far-side (shortfall) divergence assertion — two-sidedness is now half-pinned**

**Evidence:** VERIFIED IN CODE. The commit's diff replaces the shortfall case instead of adding the near-unity case: old test asserted `m.PF = 0.7` diverges; new test (cmd/modbus/reconcile_adv_test.go:615-627) asserts only `m.PF = 0.99` under a 0.95 command diverges, with the far side demoted to a comment: "A shortfall on the FAR side (e.g. 0.7) diverges identically." — no assertion executes it. Consequence: a regression that flips the check to the OPPOSITE one-sided rule (diverge only when got > want+band, e.g. someone 'simplifying' `math.Abs(got-want) <= advPFBand` to `got-want <= advPFBand`) passes the entire suite — 0.96 still converges, 0.99 still diverges, and the original ceiling behavior (catching a device delivering too FEW VARs, protected since the axis was written) is silently lost. The corrective-write assertion (line 620-626) covers only the near-unity episode.

**Root cause:** The fix edited the existing test case in place rather than adding a second case; both directions of a two-sided contract need independent pins.

**Proposed fix:** Add one observe() step asserting PF 0.7 (and ideally exactly-at-band-edge 0.93/0.97 boundary values) under the 0.95 command ⇒ diverged + corrective write; keep the 0.99 case.

**Blast radius:** Regression protection only; no runtime behavior.

### PF-7 [low/process/confidence=high]
**Stale doc comments: file-header and synthesizeLocked docs still describe the measured axes as "one-sided"**

**Evidence:** VERIFIED IN CODE. reconcile_adv.go:26-28 (file doc, Fixed PF / fixed var bullet): "Convergence is judged from MEASURED PF/Var in the poll-loop observe() feed, one-sided/toleranced (bands below)" — wrong for BOTH fixed_pf (this commit) and fixed_var (always two-sided). reconcile_adv.go:1223-1227 (synthesizeLocked doc): "builds the one-sided/toleranced readback … mirrors the solar shell's one-sided synthesis" — now accurate only for the energize axis. The commit updated the advPFBand const doc and the inline case comment but missed these two. In a codebase whose CLAUDE.md leans heavily on doc-comments as normative contracts, a future refactorer could 're-align' the code to the stale header.

**Root cause:** Partial doc sweep in the commit.

**Proposed fix:** Update both comments to: fixed_pf/fixed_var two-sided (setpoints), energize one-sided.

**Blast radius:** Documentation only.

### PF-8 [low/design-flaw/confidence=medium]
**Pre-existing context: absorb-side fixed-PF is folded onto the inject group and assessed regardless of W sign; assessment floor is absolute (100 W), not nameplate-relative**

**Evidence:** VERIFIED IN CODE (mechanics), inferred (field impact) — pre-existing, NOT introduced by 29e9552; recorded so the orchestrator knows it was examined. (a) The driver only ever writes the 704 PFWInj group: reconcile_adv.go:357-361 hardcodes `b.SetFixedPF(true, pf, overExcited, tag)` (inject=true), and cmd/hub/adv.go:342-353 maps an absorb-only CSIP control (opModFixedPFAbsorbW) into the same fixed_pf doc (documented as deliberate in internal/bus/desired_adv.go:110-115 "the author keeps the inject half"). Convergence, however, assesses whenever |W| ≥ advPFAssessMinW in EITHER direction (reconcile_adv.go:1232 uses math.Abs(m.W)) — so a battery ABSORBING power, whose reactive behavior is governed by the never-written PFWAbs group, is judged against the inject setpoint: a spec-compliant device can read as diverged while charging, driving paced corrective writes and CannotComply evidence. (b) advPFAssessMinW=100.0 (reconcile_adv.go:114) is absolute watts; on a large (e.g. 250 kW) inverter, PF at 0.04% output is noise yet passes the floor and can generate verdicts.

**Root cause:** WP-9/WP-10 simplification scoped to inject-context devices; floor sized for bench-scale sims.

**Proposed fix:** Assess fixed_pf only when sign(W) matches the written group's context (W>0 for PFWInj), holding otherwise; consider scaling the assess floor to a fraction of WMax when known.

**Blast radius:** Batteries under advanced fixed-PF control while charging; large inverters at trickle output. Gated behind reconciler.adv (default off).

### PF-5 [info/ok-verified/confidence=high]
**Low-power hold verified correct: under advPFAssessMinW the axis holds its prior adopt_state, and no path clears a diverged verdict without measured convergence**

**Evidence:** VERIFIED IN CODE + TEST. Hold: reconcile_adv.go:1232-1234 `if math.IsNaN(m.PF) || math.IsNaN(m.W) || math.Abs(m.W) < advPFAssessMinW { return nil, advVerdictHold }`; observe() line 1170-1172 `if read == nil { continue }` — no Observe is fed to the core, no transition fires; pinned by reconcile_adv_test.go:598-602 (W=20 sample holds pending). Exhaustive clear-path check: fixed_pf reaches AdoptStateAdopted ONLY via advVerdictConverged in observe (line 1182). A successful corrective/reassert write explicitly KEEPS diverged (recordMeasuredWriteLocked, reconcile_adv.go:1458-1464: "the divergence EVIDENCE stands until a measurement clears it"); reconnect-reassert goes through the same recordMeasuredWriteLocked; a re-published heartbeat doc with identical fields does not transition (setDesired line 1122 gates on !fieldsEq); only a genuinely NEW target resets to pending, which is a new command, not a false clear. One deliberate behavior worth knowing: while held (e.g. dusk) a previously-diverged axis keeps issuing corrective writes on the Tick retry path (reconcile.go:391-393) at the backoff cadence (15/30/60/120 s repeating) — paced, by design, not a storm.

### PF-6 [info/ok-verified/confidence=high]
**The two-sided fix itself is correct and its bench-verification claim is corroborated by session artifacts**

**Evidence:** VERIFIED IN CODE + ARTIFACTS. The pre-fix rule `if got >= want-advPFBand` (git show 29e9552) genuinely passed the accept-but-ignore fault (measured 0.981 under commanded 0.90: 0.981 ≥ 0.88) — the QA report §2.2 root-cause claim is accurate, and the fixed_var precedent it cites is real (reconcile_adv.go:115-120 "Two-sided by design — fixed var is a SETPOINT, not a limit"). The new check `math.Abs(got-want) <= advPFBand` (reconcile_adv.go:1244) is consistent with that discipline. The report's "verified live at the report topic" claim is corroborated by the prior session's raw captures, not just the self-report: scratchpad/pf-alone-capture.log lines 1-3 show the retained lexa/reconcile/adv/inverter-0/report sequence axis:"fixed_pf" adopt_state pending → diverged → NonConvergedBegin under mrid "mayhem-pf-ignore-…", and scratchpad/mayhem-pf-alone.log line 16 records "[PASS] Fixed-PF write ACKs but measured PF never moves (accept-but-ignore) · pf-var-measured-convergence". The sim fault exists (csip-tls-test/sim/southbound/sim.go:170 FaultPFAckIgnore, solar_adv.go). Caveats to this OK are PF-1/PF-3 (the fix closes the magnitude dimension only, mid-range commands only).

## Probe: oracle-fbcaca0-aus-loadcap

**Probe summary:** Deep-reviewed csip-tls-test commit fbcaca0 (aus-load-cap CannotComply→PASS oracle change): read the full diff, the current diagnoseAusCap (cmd/dashboard/mayhem_adv.go:1112-1272) including both AUS scenario definitions and Expected texts, the sample plumbing (mayhem.go:799-804, cannotComplyCount at 2417), the hub-side checkAusLoadConvergence/applyAusLoadLimitRule (lexa-hub internal/orchestrator/auslimits.go), the comparison oracles diagnoseOpenADRBind (mayhem_ocpp_openadr.go:796-873) and diagnoseCannotComplyVocab/diagnoseConstraint (mayhem_reporting.go:686-731, mayhem.go:1139-1148), the new/existing unit tests, and the live recheck artifact. Answers to the probe: (1) YES — a lazy hub passes: the acceptance condition is literally `case reportedCannot && cannotComplyLegit: PASS` with reportedCannot a presence-only bool; no lever-engagement or residual-magnitude check exists, and hub-side the CannotComply is emitted by measurement alone, so a hub with the entire lever rule deleted still PASSes. (2) NO magnitude check — 6500W untouched plus EV at full rate plus CannotComply PASSes identically to best effort; the data to check an irreducible floor (injected 6500/300, EvCurrentA/BatterySimW per sample) is available and unused. (3) YES — silent sustained breach remains FAIL for both families (default branch, pinned by test); verified as ok. (4) The report's inconsistency claim is misdiagnosed: diagnoseOpenADRBind DEGRADEs (not PASSes) an unresolved breach with attributed CannotComply — its live PASS was a converged run — so the suite has TWO standards, not three, and the genuine outlier pair is aus-load-cap (PASS) vs cannotcomply-table27 (pinned DEGRADED) for an honest admission of a genuinely-unresolvable breach. Overall judgment: the reclassification is defensible in principle (the pre-existing Expected text supports it) but the implementation is a de-facto oracle weakening — it removed the suite's only signal distinguishing best-effort from lazy on the ONLY load-cap scenario, which is unmeetable by design, leaving the WP-11 opModLoadLimW lever path with zero verdict coverage; the commit message's 'the hub pulled its sheddable levers' was never verified by the oracle or evidenced in the run log.

### AUSCAP-1 [high/test-blindspot/confidence=high] — **verifier: CONFIRMED**
**fbcaca0's aus-load-cap PASS condition is presence-only: a hub that sheds NOTHING sheddable passes by merely posting CannotComply**

**Evidence:** The exact acceptance condition, csip-tls-test cmd/dashboard/mayhem_adv.go:1200-1207: `case reportedCannot && cannotComplyLegit:` → `f.Verdict = "PASS"` / headline "exceeded the %.0fW cap by more than the sheddable levers can remove; hub correctly admitted CannotComply". `reportedCannot` (mayhem_adv.go:1190-1195) is only `for _, smp := range s { if smp.CannotComply { reportedCannot = true } }` — smp.CannotComply is a presence bool from gridsim's alert count for the control's mRID (mayhem.go:799-804). NOTHING in the branch inspects magnitude or lever engagement: `peak` and `lastBreach` are computed at mayhem_adv.go:1152-1166 but the PASS branch ignores both; the headline's "by more than the sheddable levers can remove" is asserted, not measured. Hub-side, the CannotComply is emitted by checkAusLoadConvergence purely from measured gross load vs cap (lexa-hub internal/orchestrator/auslimits.go:489-507: `if grossLoadW > loadLimitW+complianceBreachW { breachTicks++ } ... o.recordBreach(...)`) — it fires whether or not applyAusLoadLimitRule's levers (battery-charge shed, sticky EVSE ceiling) ever actuated. Even the oracle's `ausDecisionEngaged` gate (mayhem_adv.go:1143) is satisfied by checkAusLoadConvergence's own AddDecision("csip-aus/load-limit", ...) at auslimits.go:504, so a hub with applyAusLoadLimitRule entirely deleted would still: log the decision, breach, post CannotComply, and PASS. Compounding it: aus-load-cap is the ONLY scenario exercising opModLoadLimW (grep shows postAusCap("load") only at mayhem_adv.go:1250) and its injection is unmeetable BY DESIGN (injectEnv(300, 6500) vs 3000W cap, mayhem_adv.go:1246), so the converged-PASS branch (line 1197) is unreachable live — post-fbcaca0 the load-limit lever path has zero verdict coverage anywhere in the suite. The live recheck log confirms the PASS carried no lever evidence: scratchpad/mayhem-ausload-recheck.log line 18 shows `peak 0 W · out-of-limit 0 s · adopted=False reacted=False cannot_comply=False` on the PASS finding (Metrics never populated by diagnoseAusCap).

**Root cause:** cannotComplyLegit was threaded as a bool that converts DEGRADED→PASS wholesale, instead of PASS-conditional-on-best-effort. The oracle has the data to do better: maySample carries EvCurrentA/EvMaxA/EvW/BatterySimW (mayhem.go:780-786) and the scenario knows its injected home load (6500W) and solar (300W), so an irreducible-floor check (tail gross ≤ ~6500W + complianceTolW) or a lever check (EV current reduced, BatterySimW ≤ 0 in tail) was feasible and omitted.

**Proposed fix:** Two complementary fixes: (1) make the legit-CannotComply PASS conditional on residual magnitude — pass an irreducibleFloorW from the scenario (injected home load + tol) and require the tail-window gross load ≤ floor; a CannotComply with tail gross still carrying sheddable EV/battery-charge load → DEGRADED with a 'admitted but did not shed sheddable load' diagnosis. (2) Add a second, MEETABLE load-cap scenario (e.g. home 1500W + EV session vs 3000W cap — over only because of the EV) where the converged-PASS bar applies, restoring real coverage of applyAusLoadLimitRule's two levers.

**Blast radius:** aus-load-cap is the suite's sole certification of the WP-11 opModLoadLimW cascade (CSIP-AUS load limit). Any regression in applyAusLoadLimitRule — levers never actuated, EVSE ceiling broken, charge-shed dropped — now ships green as long as checkAusLoadConvergence still posts CannotComply. On a real CSIP-AUS site that means an EV charging at full rate straight through a utility load cap, with the suite reporting PASS.

**Verifier reasoning:** Every evidence claim checks out against code I read. (1) PASS-on-presence: csip-tls-test/cmd/dashboard/mayhem_adv.go:1200-1207 — `case reportedCannot && cannotComplyLegit: f.Verdict = "PASS"` with headline asserting "exceeded the cap by more than the sheddable levers can remove"; the branch reads neither `peak`/`lastBreach` (computed 1152-1166, unused here) nor any lever signal, though maySample carries EvCurrentA/EvMaxA/EvW (mayhem.go:782-785) and BatterySimW (mayhem.go:771-773). (2) reportedCannot is presence-only: mayhem_adv.go:1190-1195 loops `if smp.CannotComply { reportedCannot = true }`; mayhem.go:799-805 sets `s.CannotComply = n > 0` from gridsim's per-mRID alert count. (3) Engagement gate defeated by the backstop itself: ausDecisionEngaged (mayhem_adv.go:1065-1075) is a "[csip-aus/load-limit]" prefix-presence check, and lexa-hub/internal/orchestrator/auslimits.go:504 — inside checkAusLoadConvergence, which fires purely from measured `grossLoadW > loadLimitW+complianceBreachW` (lines 489-496) — emits that exact decision rule; its own doc comment (mayhem_adv.go:1060-1064) admits AddDecision fires regardless of breach state. So a hub with applyAusLoadLimitRule deleted would still gate-pass, breach, post CannotComply, and PASS (well-grounded inference from code, not a live experiment). (4) Sole + unmeetable scenario: grep shows postAusCap("load") only at mayhem_adv.go:1250; injectEnv(300, 6500) (mayhem.go:2759-2762 = solar 300 W, home load 6500 W) vs ausLoadCapLimW=3000.0 (mayhem_adv.go:991) makes baseload alone 2.17x the cap, so the converged-PASS branch (line 1197) is unreachable and the load-limit levers (auslimits.go:337 charge-shed, :428/:440 sticky EVSE ceiling) have zero verdict coverage suite-wide. (5) Log confirms evidence-free PASS: scratchpad mayhem-ausload-recheck.log shows PASS with "peak 0 W · out-of-limit 0 s · adopted=False reacted=False cannot_comply=False" — diagnoseAusCap sets only Metrics.HubBlind (mayhem_adv.go:1169), never the evidence fields. Root cause claim matches code structure exactly (1208-1211 DEGRADED differs from 1200 PASS only by the cannotComplyLegit bool). Both proposed fixes are feasible with data already collected and are the right shape. Severity=high (QA oracle can certify a hub whose load-shed levers are broken or deleted) is appropriate.

### AUSCAP-2 [high/test-blindspot/confidence=high] — **verifier: CONFIRMED**
**Answer to Q2 verified: 6500W untouched + CannotComply PASSes; no irreducible-overage check exists**

**Evidence:** Same code path as AUSCAP-1, stated per the probe's concrete example. With home 6500W, cap 3000W, sheddable 2000W: the oracle never computes 'irreducible overage'. mayhem_adv.go:1160 computes `over := gross - (limW + complianceTolW)` only to track peak/lastBreach for headlines; the `reportedCannot && cannotComplyLegit` branch (1200) is entered whenever the tail is not clean and any CannotComply landed, regardless of whether tail gross is 6500W (best effort) or 14000W (EV at full rate + battery charging, nothing shed). The unit test the commit adds pins only the best-effort-shaped fixture (mayhem_adv_test.go:444-455: RealGridW=6000, BatterySimW=0, no EV load — genuinely irreducible) — there is no companion test pinning that a sheddable-load-still-present fixture must NOT pass, so the blindspot is not even documented as accepted.

**Root cause:** Verified in code (not inferred): the only inputs to the PASS branch are the boolean pair (reportedCannot, cannotComplyLegit) and the negation of tail-clean.

**Proposed fix:** See AUSCAP-1 fix (1); additionally add TestDiagnoseAusLoadCap_Degraded_SheddableLoadRemains with an EV-load-in-tail fixture pinning the non-PASS verdict.

**Blast radius:** Same as AUSCAP-1.

**Verifier reasoning:** All claimed evidence verified by direct read. (1) csip-tls-test/cmd/dashboard/mayhem_adv.go:1160 — `over := gross - (limW + complianceTolW)` feeds only peak/lastBreach for headlines. (2) mayhem_adv.go:1196-1207 — the verdict switch's PASS branch is `case reportedCannot && cannotComplyLegit:` (line 1200), entered whenever the tail is not clean and ANY sample carried CannotComply; cannotComplyLegit is hardwired true for the load cap (line 1225). No code in diagnoseAusCap reads EvSimW/EvSimA/negative BatterySimW, though maySample (mayhem.go:98-107) carries all three as ground truth — the irreducible-overage check is absent AND computable. (3) mayhem_adv_test.go:444-456 — the only new pin, TestDiagnoseAusLoadCap_Pass_CannotComplyUnmeetable, uses RealGridW=6000/BatterySimW=0/no EV (genuinely irreducible); grep confirms zero EV/sheddable references anywhere in the test file, so no companion non-PASS pin exists. (4) Stronger than the probe stated: ausLoadCapScenario (mayhem_adv.go:1244-1246) actively starts an EV charging session and injects home 6500W > cap 3000W, so even a perfect hub's tail is unclean; hub-side checkAusLoadConvergence (lexa-hub/internal/orchestrator/auslimits.go:449-507) posts CannotComply on sustained measured breach regardless of lever success. A hub whose EVSE-curtail lever (auslimits.go:236-243) is completely broken therefore PASSes identically to a working one in the shipped scenario — the blindspot is active, not hypothetical. QA report §2.3 (docs/QA_SESSION_REPORT_2026-07-16.md:110-114) matches: the fix only threaded the cannotComplyLegit bool.

**Verifier corrections:** Root cause and fix are correct as stated. Two refinements: (a) trivial line-number nit — the test spans mayhem_adv_test.go:444-456 (fixture body 445-451), not 444-455; (b) the finding understates severity context: the blindspot is not merely undocumented-as-accepted, it is exercised by the shipped scenario itself, which starts a live EV session (mayhem_adv.go:1244-1246) whose curtailment the verdict never checks — so every green aus-load-cap run to date says nothing about whether the EVSE lever works. Proposed fix stands: gate the legit-CannotComply PASS on tail sheddable-load ≈ 0 (EvSimW/EvSimA at curtailed floor, battery not charging) or gross − sheddable ≤ limW + tol, plus TestDiagnoseAusLoadCap_Degraded_SheddableLoadRemains with an EV-load-in-tail fixture.

### AUSCAP-4 [medium/process/confidence=high]
**Session report mischaracterizes diagnoseOpenADRBind: it DEGRADEs (not PASSes) the forced-breach+CannotComply shape — the claimed three-way oracle inconsistency is misdiagnosed**

**Evidence:** QA_SESSION_REPORT_2026-07-16.md:262 claims: "openadr-csip-precedence's oracle PASSes the *same* forced-breach+correct-CannotComply shape — the two oracles are inconsistent". The code says otherwise: cmd/dashboard/mayhem_ocpp_openadr.go:837 defines `settled := m.BreachSeconds == 0 || (m.TailClean && m.ConvergedAtS >= 0 && m.ConvergedAtS <= mayConvergeDeadlineS)` and lines 850-857 give `if !settled && attributed > 0 { f.Verdict = "DEGRADED"; f.Headline = ... "breached but the hub admitted CannotComply against %s" }` — an UNRESOLVED breach + attributed CannotComply is DEGRADED there, exactly like cannotcomply-table27's base verdict (mayhem.go:1139-1148 `case m.ReportedCannot: f.Verdict = "DEGRADED"` and diagnoseConverge mayhem.go:1221-1225). openadr-csip-precedence's live PASS (report line 86, "6s physical ramp-down transient") was earned via the settled/converged branch — its site (battery full, PV curtailable, export cap 0) is always meetable — not via the CannotComply branch. The precise post-fbcaca0 rule set is therefore TWO standards, not three: (a) unresolved breach + honest CannotComply = DEGRADED (aus-gen-cap, openadr-csip-precedence, cannotcomply-table27, and every diagnoseConstraint/diagnoseConverge consumer); (b) unresolved breach + honest CannotComply = PASS (aus-load-cap alone, unconditional). The residual REAL inconsistency is aus-load-cap vs cannotcomply-table27: table27's breach is also genuinely unresolvable by design (ack_before_effect blocks the only lever, battery pinned full — mayhem_reporting.go:656,661-665) yet its honest admission stays DEGRADED (deliberately pinned), while aus-load-cap's honest admission is now full PASS. That pair is documented as deliberate in the commit message and report §9, so it is a design-call gap rather than a cheat — but the report's supporting argument (the openadr comparison) is factually wrong, which matters because it was used to frame table27's DEGRADED as an arbitrary outlier.

**Root cause:** The report author read openadr-csip-precedence's live PASS (a converged run) as an oracle rule about the breach+CannotComply shape without reading diagnoseOpenADRBind's DEGRADED branch.

**Proposed fix:** Correct the report's §9 parenthetical. If harmonization is ever done, the coherent rule is: honest CannotComply on a PROVABLY-unmeetable obligation with best-effort verified = PASS; honest CannotComply otherwise = DEGRADED — which is also what AUSCAP-1's fix implements for aus-load-cap.

**Blast radius:** Report-trust: an orchestrator or reviewer acting on §9's 'harmonize the oracles' suggestion in the PASS direction would weaken diagnoseOpenADRBind/table27 based on a false premise.

### AUSCAP-5 [medium/process/confidence=high]
**Process: DEGRADED→PASS without a compensating best-effort check is a de-facto oracle weakening, and the commit message overclaims what was verified live**

**Evidence:** The governing directive was 'never weaken an oracle to force a pass'. The commit's justification is real and pre-existing — the scenario's Expected text (mayhem_adv.go:1236, unchanged by fbcaca0) already said "CannotComply is a legitimate, correct outcome here, not just an acceptable one" — so this is not a fabricated rationale. But the implementation converts the suite's only distinguishing signal (DEGRADED, which at least drew operator eyes) into unconditional green without adding the check that would keep the PASS honest (AUSCAP-1). The commit message further asserts as fact: "Live: aus-load-cap ... now PASS — the hub pulled its sheddable levers and honestly admitted CannotComply for the irreducible baseload" — the oracle never verified lever engagement, and the live artifact (scratchpad/mayhem-ausload-recheck.log:18) contains no lever evidence at all (all Metrics zero, no EVSE-ceiling or charge-shed decision quoted). 'The hub pulled its sheddable levers' is inferred, not verified. QA_SESSION_REPORT §2.3:116 repeats "Verified: aus-load-cap PASS live" — what was verified is only that the verdict flipped.

**Root cause:** Verdict-flip verified; behavior claim carried over from the hypothesis without evidence.

**Proposed fix:** Treat fbcaca0 as half-done: keep the reclassification but land the best-effort condition (AUSCAP-1) before merging feat/dashboard-v2; re-run aus-load-cap and capture the hub's [csip-aus/load-limit] EVSE-ceiling/charge-shed decisions in the finding's Diagnosis as lever evidence.

**Blast radius:** Precedent: this is the exact pattern ('the Expected text lets me pass it') that a future session could reuse on cannotcomply-table27 or the openadr oracles.

### AUSCAP-6 [low/test-blindspot/confidence=high]
**Pre-existing: diagnoseAusCap's converged-PASS branch treats sensor-blind tail samples as clean**

**Evidence:** mayhem_adv.go:1181-1189: the tail loop sets `sawTail = true` for any sample in the last mayConvergeHoldS seconds but only dirties `tailClean` when `grossOf(smp)` returns ok — `if gross, ok := grossOf(smp); ok && gross-(limW+complianceTolW) > 0 { tailClean = false }`. A hub whose judging sensors (solar/grid) go absent for just the tail window while still breaching earns PASS "breached briefly ... then converged and held" (line 1197-1199), because the BLIND gate (line 1167, `okCount < len(s)/2`) is computed over the WHOLE window, not the tail. Not introduced by fbcaca0 (present in the pre-image, per `git show fbcaca0` context) and shared with the gen cap; noted for completeness since this branch sits above the new PASS branch in the same switch.

**Root cause:** Tail-clean uses skip-on-blind instead of blind-dirties or blind-in-tail→BLIND.

**Proposed fix:** Require ≥1 ok sample in the tail AND treat a majority-blind tail as BLIND rather than clean.

**Blast radius:** A device sim or meter dropout in the final 10s can convert a live FAIL/DEGRADED into PASS for both AUS cap scenarios.

### AUSCAP-7 [low/bug/confidence=high]
**Cosmetic: the new PASS finding's metrics line contradicts its own headline (cannot_comply=False, peak 0 W)**

**Evidence:** diagnoseAusCap never populates f.Metrics (baseFinding leaves it zero; peak is a local var, mayhem_adv.go:1153; only the BLIND branch touches Metrics.HubBlind at 1169). The runner prints the zero struct: scratchpad/mayhem-ausload-recheck.log:18 shows `peak 0 W · out-of-limit 0 s · adopted=False reacted=False cannot_comply=False` directly under a headline asserting the cap was exceeded and CannotComply was admitted. An operator (or a downstream auditor) reading the metrics line would conclude no breach happened — the artifact is self-contradictory.

**Root cause:** diagnoseAusCap deliberately avoids scanSamples (its Typ vocabulary limitation, doc at mayhem_adv.go:1112-1117) but never backfills the display metrics it does compute (peak, breach presence, CannotComply).

**Proposed fix:** Set f.Metrics.PeakBreachW, BreachSeconds (derivable from lastBreach walk), and ReportedCannot inside diagnoseAusCap.

**Blast radius:** Report readability/auditability only.

### AUSCAP-3 [info/ok-verified/confidence=high]
**Verified: silent sustained breach remains FAIL for both AUS cap families (the invariant the commit claimed to preserve)**

**Evidence:** mayhem_adv.go:1212-1215: `default: f.Verdict = "FAIL"; f.Headline = fmt.Sprintf("%s stayed over the %.0fW CSIP-AUS cap (peak +%.0fW) with no CannotComply admission", ...)`. The switch order means FAIL is reached exactly when tail is dirty AND reportedCannot is false — for BOTH gen (cannotComplyLegit=false) and load (true). Pinned by TestDiagnoseAusLoadCap_Fail_SustainedBreach (mayhem_adv_test.go:424-436, RealGridW=6000 no CannotComply → FAIL) and gen-cap DEGRADED-on-CannotComply remains pinned by TestDiagnoseAusGenCap_Degraded_CannotComplyReported (mayhem_adv_test.go:371-382). Also verified: CannotComply attribution cannot leak across scenarios — postAusCap gets a fresh mRID per postControl (mayhem_adv.go:568-572) and cannotComplyCount filters /admin/alerts by that subject (mayhem.go:2417-2433), returning -1 (not 0) on probe failure.

## Probe: evsim-3e907f2-clearprofile

**Probe summary:** Deep-reviewed csip-tls-test commit 3e907f2 (evsim ClearChargingProfile => ResumeNative). Read the full commit diff plus sim/evsim/battery.go, state.go, session.go, the clear handlers in ocpp16.go:279-281 and ocpp201.go:387-389, the updated ocpp16_test.go, the hub-side release path (lexa-hub cmd/ocpp/reconcile_shell.go, main.go, bridge16.go, internal/bus/desired.go), the mayhem oracle (cmd/dashboard/mayhem_ocpp_openadr.go), and the QA report's section 2.4. The core fix is correct and well-scoped: 0 was genuinely overloaded (Tick reads commandedA<=0 as do-not-charge at battery.go:118; StopCharging uses 0 for session end), both OCPP stacks route clears through the one shared handleClearChargingProfile, and no other SetCommandedA(0)-as-unrestricted call sites exist (exhaustive grep: session.go:120 sets 6.0 at session start, state.go:155/161 apply real limits, StopCharging at session.go:142 legitimately means stop). Session-end safety holds: Tick only runs inside runChargingLoop (session-scoped), and every new session resets commandedA to 6.0 A, so a clear arriving after session end sets commandedA=MaxCurrentA harmlessly — no charging resumes and no stale value leaks into the next session. The hub's 2.0.1/1.6 release path never puts the 1e6 RestoreCurrentA sentinel on the wire (releaseLimit maps >=1e6 or >=ratedMaxA to ClearChargingProfile), and even a numeric over-limit would be clamped by Tick's min(commandedA, MaxCurrentA); post-clear the sim reports 32 A, which passes the hub's implausibleCurrent gate (32 <= 32*1.25) with hub configs and evsim default both at 32 A. Residual defects are minor: the commit left the function's own header comment describing the OLD SetCommandedA(0)/suspend behavior (directly contradicting the code two lines below), the model has no vehicle-side current limit (the EV always resumes to the EVSE hardware max, an assumption the mayhem oracle's 0.6*EvMaxA threshold also hard-codes), and the new semantics are unit-tested only on the 1.6 handler. The QA report's section 2.4 claims about this commit are accurate, including its honest note that the two scenarios remain OPEN for an independent plan-vs-reactive reason.

### EVSIM-CLEAR-4 [low/bug/confidence=high]
**Commit left the handleClearChargingProfile header comment describing the OLD SetCommandedA(0)/suspend behavior, contradicting the code two lines below**

**Evidence:** Verified in code. state.go:176-179 (untouched by the 3e907f2 diff hunk, which starts at line 181): '// handleClearChargingProfile clears the limit back to whatever "unrestricted" // means for this sim: SetCommandedA(0), matching the pre-existing 2.0.1 // behaviour exactly (a cleared TxDefaultProfile means no active limit, and // this sim treats "no limit" as "not charging" — see evBattery.Tick).' The body at state.go:184-186 now calls h.batt.ResumeNative() with an inline comment saying the opposite ('Release to the native rate, not suspend'). The stale header documents the exact bug the commit fixes as if it were current behavior.

**Root cause:** The fix edited only the call line inside the function; the function-level doc comment above the diff hunk's context window was not updated.

**Proposed fix:** Rewrite the state.go:176-179 doc comment to describe ResumeNative semantics (0 = stop/session-end, MaxCurrentA = unrestricted/clear), mirroring battery.go:58-63.

**Blast radius:** Documentation only, but it re-plants the exact 0-overload misconception in the highest-traffic place a future editor will read.

### EVSIM-CLEAR-5 [low/test-blindspot/confidence=high]
**No vehicle-side current limit in the EV model: the sim's EV always resumes to the EVSE hardware max, and the mayhem release oracle hard-codes that same assumption**

**Evidence:** Verified in code. battery.go:29 'MaxCurrentA float64 // EVSE hardware max current (A)' is the ONLY ceiling in the model — Tick (battery.go:123) draws min(commandedA, MaxCurrentA) with no vehicle/onboard-charger pilot limit anywhere in evBattery, so ResumeNative models an EV that instantly steps to the full station rate. Real EVs resume at min(EVSE limit, vehicle limit) and ramp over seconds. Consequences: (a) the hub's one-sided EVSE convergence branch ('an EV under its limit is compliant', reconcile_shell.go:115-118 evseCurrentTolerance) is only ever exercised via CV taper or the min_current_floor fault, never by a vehicle that structurally draws less than commanded; (b) the mayhem oracle cmd/dashboard/mayhem_ocpp_openadr.go:139 'ocpp16ReleaseRecoverFrac = 0.6' with mayhem_ocpp_openadr.go:386 'smp.EvSimA >= ocpp16ReleaseRecoverFrac*maxA' encodes 'recovery reaches >=60% of station max' — true for this sim by construction, but would false-FAIL a correctly-functioning hub driving a real EV whose onboard charger caps below 0.6x the station rating (e.g. a 16 A vehicle on a 32 A station). Inferred impact (bench-only today, so low): the oracle certifies the sim's model, not release semantics in general.

**Proposed fix:** Add an optional vehicle-side limit field to evBattery (e.g. VehicleMaxA, min-ed into Tick's limit and into ResumeNative), default equal to MaxCurrentA to preserve current behavior; have the release oracle judge recovery against min(EvMaxA, vehicle limit) or against the pre-curtailment steady draw instead of a fraction of station max.

**Blast radius:** Bench QA fidelity only; no product control path involved.

### EVSIM-CLEAR-1 [info/ok-verified/confidence=high]
**ResumeNative fix is semantically correct; 0-overload disambiguated; both OCPP stacks covered**

**Evidence:** Verified in code. battery.go:118 'if b.SOC >= 100.0 || b.commandedA <= 0 { b.actualA = 0; return 0, ... }' — commandedA<=0 is do-not-charge, so the old SetCommandedA(0) on clear really did suspend a released charger. New ResumeNative (battery.go:64-68) sets 'b.commandedA = b.MaxCurrentA'; handleClearChargingProfile (state.go:186) calls it; both adapters route through that one function: ocpp201.go:387-389 'o.h.handleClearChargingProfile()' and ocpp16.go:279-281 identically. Tick clamps at battery.go:123 'limit := math.Min(b.commandedA, b.MaxCurrentA)' so the value is physically bounded. ocpp16_test.go:372-373 now asserts commandedA==MaxCurrentA after clear (the old test asserted the bug: commandedA==0).

**Root cause:** Pre-fix, the value 0 was overloaded between 'unrestricted' (clear handler intent) and 'stop' (battery model reading).

**Blast radius:** Test bench only (sim); the fix un-blinds mayhem clear-profile-release / ocpp16-smart-charge on the actuation half.

### EVSIM-CLEAR-2 [info/ok-verified/confidence=high]
**No other SetCommandedA(0)-as-unrestricted call sites; session end still forces 0 and a post-session clear cannot resume charging**

**Evidence:** Verified in code via exhaustive grep of sim/ for SetCommandedA/commandedA/ResumeNative/StopCharging. Writers: session.go:120 'h.batt.SetCommandedA(6.0)' (session start, IEC 61851 minimum — deliberate, not unrestricted); state.go:155 (apply_delayed fault) and state.go:161 (normal profile apply) — real limits; session.go:142 'h.batt.StopCharging()' (battery.go:105-110 zeros commandedA AND actualA) — legitimately means stop. A ClearChargingProfile AFTER session end calls ResumeNative unconditionally, but Tick only runs inside runChargingLoop (session.go:164-194), which has already exited, so nothing charges; actualA stays 0 so Snapshot/MeterValues report 0; and the next startSession resets commandedA to 6.0 (session.go:115-120), so the stale MaxCurrentA never leaks into a new session.

**Blast radius:** None — behavior verified safe across session lifecycle.

### EVSIM-CLEAR-3 [info/ok-verified/confidence=high]
**Hub 2.0.1/1.6 release path interacts sanely: the 1e6 RestoreCurrentA sentinel never reaches the wire, and the post-clear 32 A resume passes the hub's plausibility gate**

**Evidence:** Verified in code. lexa-hub internal/bus/desired.go:88 'const RestoreCurrentA = 1e6' is a bus-level sentinel only: cmd/ocpp/reconcile_shell.go:427-432 releaseLimit() maps 'limitA >= bus.RestoreCurrentA' OR 'ratedMaxA > 0 && limitA >= s.ratedMaxA' to driver.ApplyClear (applyActionLocked, reconcile_shell.go:399-409) — an OCPP ClearChargingProfile, never a numeric SetChargingProfile of 1000000 A. So evsim sees a Clear and resumes at its OWN MaxCurrentA (32 A default, main.go:83 '-max-current 32.0'), never reporting a bogus 1000000 A; even a hypothetical numeric over-limit is clamped by battery.go:123's min(). Post-release convergence on the hub is trivially satisfied by the one-sided rule (reconcile_shell.go:381-390 comment: release has no measurable target). The resumed 32 A passes cmd/ocpp/main.go:1025-1032 implausibleCurrent (32 <= 32*1.25=40; configs/ocpp.json:21 and hub.json:83 both 'max_current_a: 32.0', matching evsim's default). The QA report §2.4 claim ('reconciler issues ClearChargingProfile + MaxCurrentA=1000000 = the RestoreCurrentA release sentinel') is consistent with this code: 1e6 is the desired-doc value, Clear is the wire verb.

**Blast radius:** None — hub/sim release interaction verified coherent.

### EVSIM-CLEAR-6 [info/test-blindspot/confidence=high]
**New clear semantics unit-tested only on the 1.6 handler; no 2.0.1-side test and no criteria matching on clear**

**Evidence:** Verified in code. The commit updated only ocpp16_test.go (TestOCPP16_ClearChargingProfileRestoresUnrestricted, lines 355-374); grep of main_test.go/faults_test.go/lifecycle_fault_test.go finds no ClearChargingProfile test on the 2.0.1 handler path. Mitigated because ocpp201.go:387-389 and ocpp16.go:279-281 both delegate to the identical shared handleClearChargingProfile, so a shared-path regression is caught — but a 2.0.1 wrapper regression (e.g. dropping the delegation) would not be. Related sim simplification: handleClearChargingProfile (state.go:180-187) ignores the request's clear criteria entirely (the hub sets ChargingProfileCriteria at cmd/ocpp/main.go:847), acceptable for a one-profile sim but means criteria-mismatch bugs on the hub side are invisible to the bench.

**Proposed fix:** Add a mirror TestOCPP201_ClearChargingProfile asserting commandedA==MaxCurrentA through ocpp201Handlers.OnClearChargingProfile.

**Blast radius:** Test coverage completeness only.
