## Probe: qa-oracle-blindspots

**Probe summary:** Audited the mayhem QA suite itself (csip-tls-test cmd/dashboard/mayhem.go 3147 lines read across engine/run-loop/diagnosers/sampling/bench-IO, invariants.go in full, mayhem_pagination.go and mayhem_csipedge.go in full, targeted reads of mayhem_adv.go, mayhem_world.go, mayhem_ocpp_openadr.go, scripts/mayhem.py in full, docs/QA_COMPLETENESS_AUDIT.md excerpts) plus the prior session's raw run logs and the QA_SESSION_REPORT. The admitted csip-pagination-walk false-PASS is confirmed to be an AGGREGATION failure, not an oracle failure: the engine scored it INCONCLUSIVE ('arm pagination: gridsim/admin/paginate: HTTP 404', mayhem-batch2.log:96) and the session report's '15/15 PASS' tally simply absorbed it — enabled by mayhem.py's exit code counting only fail+blind, with INCONCLUSIVE invisible and no finished/total integrity check (a dashboard restart mid-run even yields exit 0 with an empty report). The systematic classes found, ranked by leverage: (1) make INCONCLUSIVE and incomplete runs machine-visible failures in mayhem.py (MAY-1); (2) add injection-efficacy assertions — diagnoseStale literally returns PASS when the fault 'did not take', the pagination oracle never verifies the list was served paged, and all environment-pressure posts are fire-and-forget so a dead solar sim yields vacuous cap-held PASSes (MAY-2); (3) bind the adv retained-report oracles to THIS run's injected mrid/timestamp — today they match axis only, so retained cross-scenario pollution can certify a broken reconciler (MAY-3); (4) close the lying-hub hole where diagnosePaginationWalk PASSes purely on hub-reported mRID while the safety audit deliberately excludes INV-EXPORT (MAY-4); (5) stop folding a gridsim alerts-probe failure into CannotComply=false, which turns honest hub admissions into FAILs (MAY-5); (6) engine-level per-scenario bench health gates with infra-cause annotation on FAILs (MAY-6); (7) first-class repeat/flake support — iterations currently exists only for chaos mode, so finding-D's ~25% intermittents are structurally invisible to any standard run (MAY-7); (8) runner robustness: SIGTERM→abort, scenario id on live findings, 409 takeover, SSH command deadlines (MAY-8). Core verdict machinery (setup-fail→INCONCLUSIVE, abort→INCONCLUSIVE, panic recovery, WS-3 probe gates, ground-truth dither oracles, safety-audit escalation, the fbcaca0 oracle fix) verified correct (MAY-OK-1). All findings carry file:line evidence read directly; nothing was taken from the session report on faith.

### MAY-1 [high/test-blindspot/confidence=high] — **verifier: CONFIRMED**
**mayhem.py exit code and completion check make INCONCLUSIVE (and truncated/dead runs) indistinguishable from success — the exact enabler of the admitted csip-pagination-walk false PASS**

**Evidence:** mayhem.py:193-195: `s = status.get("summary") or {}; bad = s.get("fail", 0) + s.get("blind", 0); return 1 if bad else 0` — INCONCLUSIVE never affects the exit code. Nothing in the script reads `status["finished"]` (grep for `finished` in mayhem.py returns nothing). The engine correctly produced INCONCLUSIVE for the stale-gridsim run — scratchpad mayhem-batch2.log:96 shows `[INCONCLUSIVE] … csip-pagination-walk` with `Setup failed: arm pagination: gridsim/admin/paginate: HTTP 404` — yet the session report §5 claimed "15/15 PASS"; the machine signal (exit 0, no FAIL section) offered nothing to contradict that mis-tally. Additionally: the dashboard engine keeps status only in process memory (mayhem.go:203-230, d.status), so a dashboard restart mid-run answers /api/qa/status with a zero-value `{running:false}`; mayhem.py's poll loop (lines 152-185) breaks on `not status.get("running")`, prints an empty report, computes bad=0, and exits 0 — a full false-green with zero scenarios judged.

**Root cause:** The runner defines success as 'no FAIL/BLIND in whatever summary I last saw' instead of 'the run finished, judged every selected scenario, and every verdict was PASS/DEGRADED'.

**Proposed fix:** In mayhem.py run(): (1) exit non-zero (new code 3 or fold into 1) when summary.inconclusive > 0 unless an explicit --allow-inconclusive is passed; (2) require status.finished==true AND len(findings)==status.total, else exit 2 with 'run did not complete'; (3) print an explicit 'N INCONCLUSIVE — these scenarios were NOT judged; re-run them' banner above the summary. Optionally persist run state server-side (the writeReport .md already exists) so a restarted dashboard can answer 'a run was in progress and died'.

**Blast radius:** Every CI/agent-driven campaign: any scenario whose precondition silently failed (sim down, endpoint 404, stale build) is scored as if it never existed. This is the systematic class behind the report's one admitted false-PASS.

**Verifier reasoning:** All load-bearing claims verified by direct read. (1) Exit-code blindness: csip-tls-test/scripts/mayhem.py:193-195 is verbatim as cited — `s = status.get("summary") or {}; bad = s.get("fail", 0) + s.get("blind", 0); return 1 if bad else 0`. INCONCLUSIVE (and aborted/last_error/finished) never affect the exit code; the docstring line 19 even documents this as the design ("0 if no FAIL/BLIND"). `grep -n finished scripts/mayhem.py` returns nothing — confirmed the script never reads it, even though the server EXPOSES it: cmd/dashboard/mayhem.go:184 `Finished bool json:"finished"`, set at mayhem.go:2266 `d.status.Finished = !aborted && errMsg == ""`, and mayhem.go:177 has `Inconclusive int json:"inconclusive"` — so both halves of the proposed fix are directly implementable against existing API fields. (2) Dashboard-restart false-green: verified in code (not observed in logs). d.status is a plain in-process field (mayhem.go:207 `status mayhemStatus` inside mayhemDriver, no persistence of status itself); handleStatus (mayhem.go:419-427) returns a copy of d.status, so a restarted dashboard answers the zero value `{"running":false,"finished":false,...}`. mayhem.py's poll loop breaks on `if not status.get("running"): break` (lines 169-170), _print_report's state expression (line 216) renders that zero value as "Run complete. Bench restored." (not aborted, no last_error), summary empty → bad=0 → exit 0. Full false-green with zero scenarios judged, and it even prints "complete". (3) Log/report evidence: scratchpad mayhem-batch2.log line 96 shows `[INCONCLUSIVE] Hub pages a multi-page DERControlList... csip-pagination-walk` with "Setup failed: arm pagination: gridsim/admin/paginate: HTTP 404"; the session report (docs/QA_SESSION_REPORT_2026-07-16.md) claims "Batch 2/3 new seams **15/15 PASS**" at lines 41 and 168 while its own footnote at line 175 admits csip-pagination-walk "PASSed here only because it was actually INCONCLUSIVE under the then-stale gridsim" — and mayhem-batch2-retry.log confirms only 2 scenarios (cancelled-superseded, randomize) were re-run after the gridsim rebuild (summary "PASS 2 ... INCONCLUSIVE 0", exit 0), pagination never re-judged. Strengthening evidence the original auditor missed: runGuarded's panic recovery (mayhem.go:404-414) sets Aborted=true/LastError/Finished=false — mayhem.py prints "Run FAILED: <err>" (line 216) yet still exits 0 if no FAIL/BLIND findings landed before the panic, so even a server-side crash mid-run is exit-0.

**Verifier corrections:** Root cause and fix are correct as stated; one narrative detail needs precision: the batch2 run itself did NOT exit 0 — it had FAIL 1 (csip-event-delay, mayhem-batch2.log line 22 "PASS 4 DEGRADED 0 FAIL 1 BLIND 0 INCONCLUSIVE 2"), so it exited 1. The exit-0 machine signal that "offered nothing to contradict the mis-tally" was the RETRY run (mayhem-batch2-retry.log: 2/2 PASS, exit 0) that re-ran only cancelled-superseded and randomize — the enabling mechanism is that neither run's exit code (nor any completeness check) ever forced csip-pagination-walk's INCONCLUSIVE to be re-judged, which is exactly the claimed root cause. Fix additions: (a) the finished check should be `status.get("finished") is True` — this also correctly fails the panic-abort path (Finished=false, mayhem.go:409) and Ctrl-C abort; (b) note the docstring at mayhem.py:19 must be updated too since it documents the current exit contract; (c) the optional server-side persistence half is genuinely optional — writeReport already persists a markdown report per run (status.report_path), so a restarted dashboard has an artifact trail even today, just not one the runner consults.

### MAY-2 [high/test-blindspot/confidence=high] — **verifier: CONFIRMED**
**No injection-efficacy verification: a fault that never armed, or environment pressure that never materialized, can score PASS**

**Evidence:** Three verified instances. (a) diagnoseStale, mayhem.go:1286-1290: when the meter freeze did not engage, `f.Verdict = "PASS"; f.Headline = "meter kept updating; sensor-freeze fault did not take"` — the diagnosis text says "this run does not test staleness … re-run" but the VERDICT is PASS and counts in the pass column. (b) csip-pagination-walk (mayhem_pagination.go:86-94): setup arms `/admin/paginate` and only checks the POST status; the oracle (lines 111-196) judges solely which mRID the hub adopted — nothing ever probes that gridsim actually served /derp/0/derc paged (all=2/results=1). A gridsim that accepts the POST but doesn't paginate lets the hub see both controls in one page and PASS without the pagination code path ever executing. (c) Environment pressure is fire-and-forget: `injectEnv` (mayhem.go:2759-2762) and nearly all setup device posts discard errors (`_ = d.post("battery", "/inject", …)` at mayhem.go:1526, malformScenario; mayhem_pagination.go:61). If the solar sim is broken (finding E's HTTP-500 mode) an export-cap scenario has no PV to export, the cap is trivially met, GridOK stays true so the WS-3 probe gate never fires, and the scenario PASSes vacuously — 'hub held the cap' is indistinguishable from 'there was never anything to curtail'.

**Root cause:** Oracles assert the hub's response but never assert the scenario's premise (fault armed, pressure present) from an independent readback.

**Proposed fix:** Add a premise assertion to each oracle: (1) diagnoseStale's not-frozen branch → INCONCLUSIVE, not PASS; (2) pagination setup does a direct probe GET of /derp/0/derc (or /admin readback) asserting results<all before the hold, else INCONCLUSIVE; (3) constraint scenarios record the injected PV/load and require SolarPossibleW (already sampled) ≈ pvHighW on ≥80% of the window — else INCONCLUSIVE 'injection never took'; (4) make setup/perTick injection errors at least counted and folded into the verdict.

**Blast radius:** Every export/gen/import-cap scenario and every fault-injection scenario; this is the general form of both the pagination false-PASS and the modsim-500 spurious results.

**Verifier reasoning:** All three claimed instances verified in code, plus the supporting machinery. (a) VERIFIED: cmd/dashboard/mayhem.go:1286-1290 reads exactly `if !frozen { f.Verdict = "PASS"; f.Headline = "meter kept updating; sensor-freeze fault did not take"` with diagnosis text "...the freeze did not engage, so this run does not test staleness. Confirm the meter sim honoured pause and re-run." — and appendFinding (mayhem.go:2227-2229) increments Summary.Pass for verdict "PASS", so it does count in the pass column, contradicting its own diagnosis. (b) VERIFIED: mayhem_pagination.go:86-90 arms `/admin/paginate` checking only the POST error; the oracle diagnosePaginationWalk (111-196) judges solely tail AdoptedMRID (sawWinner/sawLoser, lines 134-146) — no readback that gridsim served results<all. Because within-program supersede makes CTRL-PAGE2 win even in a single-page response (the file's own header comment, lines 22-25, says supersede picks PAGE2), a gridsim that 200s the arm POST but doesn't actually paginate (stale deployed binary predating sim/gridsim/paginate.go, or a path-match regression) lets a hub with a BROKEN paging loop adopt PAGE2 and PASS — the paging code path never executes and the verdict cannot distinguish it. (c) VERIFIED: injectEnv (mayhem.go:2759-2762) discards both post errors; d.post DOES return real errors on transport failure and any >=300 status (mayhem.go:2350-2357), so signal exists and is dropped. Same discard pattern at malformScenario setup (mayhem.go:1526), perfect-storm setup (3064-3067) and its delayed meter pause (3077-3079), and pagination setup (mayhem_pagination.go:61-62). diagnoseConstraint gives PASS purely on m.BreachSeconds==0 (mayhem.go:1122-1129) with no premise check that pressure existed; the WS-3 gate forceBlindOnProbeGap (mayhem.go:897-933) fires only when the JUDGING probe is unavailable — for exportCap the judging sensor is the grid meter (judgingProbeLabel, 886-889) — so a dead/erroring solar sim leaves GridOK true and the vacuous PASS stands, exactly as claimed. Fix feasibility confirmed: SolarPossibleW is already sampled (maySample field mayhem.go:82, populated at :763). Sim /inject endpoints really can return non-2xx (sim/simapi/server.go:130-139: 400/501), so discarded errors are a realistic loss, independent of whether finding E's specific HTTP-500 mode exists (that cross-reference is the one part I did not verify; the mechanism does not depend on it).

**Verifier corrections:** Root cause is accurate as stated. Two refinements: (1) Instance (a) is narrower than "a fault that never armed": the stale-meter scenario's arm POST IS error-checked at setup (mayhem.go:3005-3007) and any setup error already yields INCONCLUSIVE via the runner (mayhem.go:511-525), so the PASS blindspot is specifically the accepted-but-ineffective arm (sim returns 200 but doesn't freeze) — which is still real, and note perfect-storm's meter pause at :3078 discards even the HTTP error. (2) Proposed fix #2's "direct probe GET of /derp/0/derc" option is likely infeasible from the dashboard: the CSIP endpoint requires ECDHE-ECDSA-AES128-CCM-8 mTLS (product invariant), and Go's crypto/tls has no AES-CCM suites — use the /admin readback variant instead, ideally a gridsim counter asserting it actually SERVED a paged response (results<all) to the hub during the window, which is stronger than asserting the arm state. Fixes #1, #3 (SolarPossibleW is already in maySample), and #4 are feasible as proposed.

### MAY-3 [high/test-blindspot/confidence=high] — **verifier: PARTLY**
**Advanced-DER oracles judge a retained per-device report matched only by AXIS — no mrid/timestamp binding to this scenario's injection, so cross-scenario retained pollution can mint a false PASS (or FAIL)**

**Evidence:** advReportMsg (mayhem_adv.go:424-432) carries Kind/DeviceClass/DeviceID/Axis/AdoptState/CurveHash/Ts — no mrid field at all, even though every injected desired doc stamps a unique mrid (`mayhem-pf-ignore-%d`, mayhem_adv.go setup) and bus.ReconcileReport rides a retained topic per DEVICE, not per axis or per command. diagnosePFVarMeasuredConvergence gates only on `report.Axis != "fixed_pf"` then switches on report.AdoptState; report.Ts is never compared to the injection time. A retained `{axis:fixed_pf, adopt_state:diverged}` left over from a previous run would PASS a hub whose reconciler is now broken (or whose write never happened). The session report §10 itself recommends "make the adv oracle match the report's mrid" — confirmed unimplemented. resetForScenario (mayhem.go:2727-2744) clears device faults/controls but never clears lexa/desired/adv/+ or lexa/reconcile/adv/+/report retained topics; the report's operational workaround is a manual mosquitto clear between runs.

**Root cause:** The retained report is treated as 'the outcome of my injection' when it is actually 'the last transition anyone caused on this device'.

**Proposed fix:** Two-sided: (1) lexa-hub: echo the desired doc's mrid (and issued_at/seq) into bus.ReconcileReport's adv extension; (2) oracle: match report mrid == injected mrid (interim: require report.Ts >= injection wall time), else INCONCLUSIVE; (3) resetForScenario publishes empty retained payloads on the adv desired/report topics for configured adv devices.

**Blast radius:** curve-adopt-readback-divergence, pf-var-measured-convergence, adv-shadow-no-writes — the WP-10 safety-verification oracles; exactly the scenarios the report says must be run 'individually with a manual topic clear', i.e. the suite depends on operator discipline where it should depend on the oracle.

**Verifier reasoning:** The blindspot itself is CONFIRMED with code evidence; one leg of the proposed fix is wrong because it is already implemented in the hub.

Confirmed claims (all read directly):
1. Oracle struct has no mrid binding: csip-tls-test/cmd/dashboard/mayhem_adv.go:424-432 — advReportMsg carries only Kind/DeviceClass/DeviceID/Axis/AdoptState/CurveHash/Ts. No mrid, seq, or issued_at.
2. Injections stamp unique mrids the oracle never checks: mayhem_adv.go:877 `mrid := fmt.Sprintf("mayhem-pf-ignore-%d", time.Now().UnixNano())` and :744 `"mayhem-curve-lies-%d"`; both payload builders embed `"mrid":%q` (mayhem_adv.go:390, :402).
3. Axis-only gating, no time binding: diagnosePFVarMeasuredConvergence gates only `if report.Axis != "fixed_pf"` (mayhem_adv.go:929) then switches on report.AdoptState (:944); diagnoseCurveAdoptDivergence likewise gates only `report.Axis != wantAxis` (:786). `grep '\.Ts' mayhem_adv.go` returns nothing — Ts is decoded but never compared to injection time anywhere in the file.
4. resetForScenario never clears adv retained topics: csip-tls-test/cmd/dashboard/mayhem.go:2727-2744 clears controls/faults/clock and idles devices only; no publish to lexa/desired/adv/+ or lexa/reconcile/adv/+/report.
5. The session report itself concedes the gap operationally: QA_SESSION_REPORT_2026-07-16.md line 275 — "run individually with a clear of lexa/{desired,reconcile}/adv/inverter-0[/report] between them (retained-report cross-scenario pollution)... Recommended future hardening: make the adv oracle match the report's mrid" — recommended, verified unimplemented in the oracle.
6. False-PASS path is real but requires two coincident conditions (assessment, not just quote): the retained topic is per DEVICE and the pf teardown reads the report BEFORE publishing the release (mayhem_adv.go:888-899), so a clean run ends with the release transition's report retained (adopt_state "", via transitionLocked(rn, "", now), lexa-hub/cmd/modbus/reconcile_adv.go:1503) — which the pf oracle actually judges FAIL (case "adopted", "": mayhem_adv.go:945). The false PASS needs a prior run that left {axis:fixed_pf, adopt_state:diverged} retained (teardown mqttInject errors are discarded, `_ =` at :899, or an aborted run) followed by a run where the new injection is never processed. So the more common pollution symptom is false FAIL/INCONCLUSIVE; false PASS is reachable but narrower. Severity=high still fits the rubric ("a QA oracle that can certify a broken hub").

Refuted part — fix leg (1) is already done: bus.ReconcileReport ALREADY carries `MRID string json:"mrid,omitempty"`, Seq, and IssuedAt (lexa-hub/internal/bus/messages.go:182-184), and the adv shell already stamps the held doc's identity on EVERY published report including AdoptState transitions: publishReportLocked sets `MRID: s.docMRID, Seq: s.docSeq, IssuedAt: s.docIssuedAt` (reconcile_adv.go:1798-1800; docMRID captured from doc.MRID at :1109), and handleReportLocked sets `MRID: rep.MRID` (:1776). The injected mrid is therefore already on the wire in the retained report; the oracle simply fails to decode and compare it.

**Verifier corrections:** Root cause stands ("last transition anyone caused" treated as "outcome of my injection"), but the fix is one-sided, not two-sided: (1) NO lexa-hub change is needed — bus.ReconcileReport already carries mrid/seq/issued_at (internal/bus/messages.go:182-184) and cmd/modbus/reconcile_adv.go:1776/1798 already populates them from the held desired doc, including for shell-authored AdoptState transition reports. (2) The real fix is oracle-only: add `MRID string json:"mrid"` (and optionally issued_at/seq) to advReportMsg (mayhem_adv.go:424-432) and require report.MRID == the injected mrid in diagnoseCurveAdoptDivergence/diagnosePFVarMeasuredConvergence, else INCONCLUSIVE. One caveat for the implementer: after the teardown release, subsequent retained reports carry the RELEASE doc's identity (empty mrid), so the mrid match must happen against the report read in teardown before the release publish — which is already the read the oracles use. The Ts >= injection-time interim check is valid but weaker (release/other-axis transitions also bump Ts). (3) The resetForScenario addition (publish empty retained payloads on adv desired/report topics for adv devices) is correct and matches the session report's own manual workaround (§10/§13); note also that per-axis reports share ONE retained slot per device, so even mrid matching leaves multi-axis last-writer-wins ambiguity — mrid match downgrades it safely to INCONCLUSIVE rather than a wrong verdict.

### MAY-4 [high/test-blindspot/confidence=high]
**Hub-reported-state-only PASSes: pagination PASS ignores measured enforcement, and the safety audit deliberately excludes INV-EXPORT, so nothing escalates it — a lying or half-fixed hub passes**

**Evidence:** diagnosePaginationWalk, mayhem_pagination.go:152-161: `case sawWinner > 0 && sawLoser == 0: f.Verdict = "PASS"` — the verdict is decided entirely from /status's AdoptedMRID; `breaches := invExport(cons, s)` is computed (line 149) but only rendered into diagnosis text, never gated on. safetyAudit (invariants.go:294-302) intentionally omits INV-EXPORT/INV-CONVERGE ("those are the scenario's primary oracle") — but for this oracle they are NOT the primary oracle, so a hub that reports adopting the 1000 W page-2 cap while physically exporting 4+ kW scores PASS. Same class, weaker instances: diagnoseRandomizeDuration judges only hub-reported validUntil (inherent to the property — acceptable, but a hub misreporting validUntil passes); the adv oracles (MAY-3) judge the reconciler's self-reported adopt_state, with sim ground-truth PF captured but used only as a diagnosis note (diagnosePFVarMeasuredConvergence: groundTruthNote never affects the verdict). By contrast diagnoseConstraint/diagnoseSOC/dither oracles correctly judge sim/meter ground truth.

**Root cause:** The 'safety audit escalates what the targeted oracle missed' contract has a hole: oracles whose primary signal is hub-reported state have no ground-truth backstop because the audit skips the constraint invariants for everyone.

**Proposed fix:** In diagnosePaginationWalk's winner branch, require `len(breaches)==0 || f.Metrics.TailClean` for PASS (else DEGRADED/FAIL); in diagnosePFVarMeasuredConvergence, when havePF is true and measured PF DID move to the commanded value (fault failed to arm) treat 'diverged' as suspicious → INCONCLUSIVE rather than PASS. General rule: any oracle whose verdict source is hub self-report must either gate on the measured invariant or be listed as self-report-only in the scenario's Expected text.

**Blast radius:** csip-pagination-walk (the finding-C scenario — when the hub's pagination fix lands, this oracle would certify it even if enforcement of the adopted cap were broken), randomize-duration-honored, all adv report scenarios.

### MAY-5 [medium/bug/confidence=high]
**gridsim probe failure is folded into CannotComply=false: a correctly-admitting hub scores FAIL instead of DEGRADED when /admin/alerts is unreachable, with no INCONCLUSIVE path**

**Evidence:** cannotComplyCount (mayhem.go:2417-2433) deliberately returns -1 when gridsim is unreachable ("a caller … must not treat a probe failure as a clean reading"), but sample() (mayhem.go:800-805) does `if n := d.cannotComplyCount(cons.MRID); n >= 0 { s.CannotComply = n > 0 … }` — on -1 the sample silently keeps CannotComply=false and records no probe-failure marker. scanSamples then reports m.ReportedCannot=false and diagnoseConstraint's first switch arm (`case m.ReportedCannot:` → DEGRADED, mayhem.go:1139-1148) is skipped, so a sustained physical-limit breach the hub honestly admitted lands in the FAIL branches ('no admission of failure'). The -1 discipline is honored only by the WS-4.5 duplicate-count consumers, not by the presence-bool path every constraint diagnoser uses.

**Root cause:** The probe-failure sentinel exists but the per-sample fold discards it; maySample has no CannotComplyProbeOK field, so no diagnoser can distinguish 'confirmed no admission' from 'could not check'.

**Proposed fix:** Add `CannotComplyProbeOK bool` to maySample (set from n>=0); in scanSamples, track the fraction of probe-OK samples; when a would-be FAIL rests on ReportedCannot=false and the alerts probe was down for most of the window, emit INCONCLUSIVE ('cannot verify admission — gridsim alerts unreachable') — the symmetric twin of the WS-3 probe gate, on the FAIL side.

**Blast radius:** Every constraint/converge/SOC scenario during any gridsim outage or net-partition scenario window — false-red (hub blamed) rather than false-green, but it burns trust and triage time, and in a net-partition scenario the probe outage is guaranteed.

### MAY-6 [medium/infra/confidence=high]
**No per-scenario bench health gate and no mid-run sim-death detection: a sim-broken run is distinguishable from a hub-broken run only for setup failures and PASS-side probe gaps, not for FAIL verdicts**

**Evidence:** baseline() runs once per RUN (mayhem.go:479-482) and even there half the posts ignore errors (`_ = d.post("battery", …)`, mayhem.go:2664-2671). resetForScenario ignores every error (mayhem.go:2727-2744). Nothing re-probes sims between or during scenarios; finding E (modsim serving HTTP 500 while systemd shows 'active') required the operator to notice and adopt manual `curl /state` checks + preventive restarts (report §10). The WS-3 forceBlindOnProbeGap only ever tightens PASS→BLIND (mayhem.go:908-918, by design); a FAIL produced while a sim was broken (e.g. hub cannot curtail a dead modsim, export stays high) is reported as a hub control failure with no infra annotation. The adv scenarios show the right pattern — requireAdvSolarSim/requireModbusReconcilerAdvMode fail setup → INCONCLUSIVE — but only the adv family uses it.

**Root cause:** Precondition checking is per-family convention (adv only), not an engine-level contract; probe health is consulted only to protect PASS, never to contextualize FAIL.

**Proposed fix:** Engine-level: before each scenario, probe every backend the scenario's setup/oracle touches (/state 200 for sims, hub /healthz, gridsim /admin/status); any failure → INCONCLUSIVE with a machine-readable `infra_cause` field. After a FAIL verdict, re-probe the same set and append a 'bench health at verdict time' line; a sim that died mid-window flags the finding `suspect_infra=true` so aggregation can separate hub-red from bench-red.

**Blast radius:** All 100+ scenarios during long campaigns; directly addresses the report's finding-E spurious FAIL/BLIND class and the 'check the sims at every review' operator burden.

### MAY-7 [medium/test-blindspot/confidence=high]
**Single-run verdicts with no repeat/flake support: ~25% intermittents (finding D) are invisible to any standard run; the soak that found them was ad-hoc shell looping**

**Evidence:** handleStart (mayhem.go:338-349): `req.Iterations` is consumed only by `d.chaosScenarios(chaosSeed, req.Iterations)`; curated and matrix modes run each scenario exactly once (run loop, mayhem.go:484-579, no repeat plumbing). mayhem.py exposes --iterations "chaos iteration count" only. csip-event-delay PASSed its single Batch-2 run and was later measured ~25% FAIL over 8 soak repetitions (report §7.4) — a verdict distribution no single run can express. The soak itself was external bash loops writing to scratchpad logs, with scenario↔verdict pairing done by hand (which produced the §5 mis-tally).

**Root cause:** The engine's unit of result is one verdict per scenario; flakiness is not a representable outcome.

**Proposed fix:** Add `repeat: N` to mayhemStartReq (applies to curated/--only runs): run each selected scenario N times, report per-scenario verdict distribution (e.g. `6 PASS / 2 FAIL`) and a computed verdict FLAKY when mixed; mayhem.py --repeat N surfaces it and exits non-zero on FLAKY. This turns finding-D-class intermittents into a first-class, machine-detected outcome instead of an 11-hour-soak-plus-human-diffing discovery.

**Blast radius:** All boundary/timing scenarios — precisely the §8 dither/hunt class the report calls the campaign's most valuable synthesis.

### MAY-8 [medium/infra/confidence=high]
**Runner/engine robustness gaps behind report §10's 'operator must know' rules: SIGTERM strands the engine (the 409), live findings print without scenario id (the mispairing), and hubSSHOutput has no command timeout (an abort-proof wedge)**

**Evidence:** (a) mayhem.py handles only KeyboardInterrupt (lines 171-185); grep for signal/SIGTERM/atexit returns nothing — `timeout`'s default SIGTERM kills the client without POSTing /api/qa/abort, so the server-side engine keeps running and the next start hits handleStart's 409 (mayhem.go:375-378), whose body carries no run age/current-scenario and offers no takeover. (b) _print_new_findings (mayhem.py:201-208) prints `verdict + headline` with no f['id'] — while start-lines print the CURRENT scenario, findings land after `current` has advanced, so live-log scenario↔verdict pairing is unreliable (the report's admitted early mis-read); only the final report is keyed. (c) hubSSHOutput (mayhem_world.go:136-150) sets ConnectTimeout=4 but uses exec.Command + cmd.Output() with no overall deadline; a hung remote command in a setup/teardown (teardown runs unconditionally AFTER ctx cancel, mayhem.go:544-548) wedges the run goroutine where even /api/qa/abort cannot reach it — the 409 is then permanent until a dashboard restart.

**Root cause:** Client lifetime and engine lifetime are decoupled by design (runs survive tab close) but the failure paths of that decoupling are handled by playbook prose instead of code.

**Proposed fix:** (a) mayhem.py: install signal handlers for SIGTERM/SIGHUP that POST /abort before exit; (b) print `f['id']` in _print_new_findings (one line); (c) handleStart's 409 body includes started_at/current/idx and accepts {"takeover":true} to abort-then-start; (d) hubSSHOutput uses exec.CommandContext with a ~15s deadline derived from the scenario context.

**Blast radius:** Campaign operability: every one of §10's four 'learned the hard way' rules becomes unnecessary; prevents the stranded-409 and mispairing classes structurally.

### MAY-9 [low/design-flaw/confidence=high]
**scanSamples 'adopted' matches constraint TYPE only, never mRID — with the ever-present bench-default 5 kW export cap, HubAdopted is vacuous for exportCap scenarios and diagnoseConstraint misattributes the broken link**

**Evidence:** mayhem.go:984: `if smp.HubAdopted && smp.AdoptedTyp == cons.Typ { adopted++ }` — AdoptedMRID is sampled (mayhem.go:794) but never compared to cons.MRID. armAfterCapAdopted's own doc (mayhem.go:713-720) acknowledges the problem for fault ARMING ("hubState() reports ctrlActive=true for the default from the outset") but the metric side was never given the same treatment. Consequence: for any exportCap scenario the `!m.HubAdopted → FAIL 'never adopted'` branch (mayhem.go:1149-1154) can never fire while the bench default is served, so an adoption failure is instead reported as "adopted but did not converge" — wrong Fix pointer (actuation path instead of discovery/scheduler), costing triage time.

**Root cause:** Adoption is judged as 'some control of this type is active' rather than 'THIS scenario's control is active'.

**Proposed fix:** When cons.MRID != "", count adopted only on AdoptedMRID == cons.MRID (keep the type-only fallback for scenarios with server-assigned mRIDs unavailable at setup); surface both counts in diagnosis (`adopted_this_mrid` vs `adopted_any_of_type`).

**Blast radius:** Diagnostic accuracy of every exportCap scenario's FAIL story; no false-green (the breach math is unaffected).

### MAY-OK-1 [info/ok-verified/confidence=high]
**Verified correct: the engine's core verdict-integrity machinery does what the report relies on**

**Evidence:** Checked and confirmed in code: (1) setup failure → INCONCLUSIVE, never PASS (mayhem.go:512-529, and the stale-gridsim run really did score INCONCLUSIVE — mayhem-batch2.log:96); (2) abort mid-scenario forces INCONCLUSIVE over any partial-window verdict (mayhem.go:556-571, WS-3); (3) runGuarded's recover keeps the dashboard alive and restoreBench still fires on panic unwind (mayhem.go:403-417, 475-477); (4) unknown verdict strings fall into the Inconclusive counter, not Pass (appendFinding default arm, mayhem.go:2236-2237); (5) forceBlindOnProbeGap only ever tightens PASS→BLIND and never downgrades a data-backed FAIL (mayhem.go:908-918), with constraint-aware judging-probe selection mirrored off breachOver's own switch (mayhem.go:874-883); (6) the dither oracles judge simulator ground truth (BatterySimW/BatSimSOC — mayhem_world.go:1734-1749, 1813-1854) and the export-dither/soc-dither FAIL logic matches the report's findings B/D usage; (7) safety-audit escalation rules (INV-CONNECT any occurrence → FAIL; INV-SOC/INV-EVMAX sustained ≥3 samples → FAIL; never downgrades) are as documented (invariants.go:328-359); (8) the reported oracle fix fbcaca0 (aus-load-cap cannotComplyLegit) is real, threaded as described, and gen-cap keeps DEGRADED (mayhem_adv.go:1118-1200); (9) mayhem.py exit code does correctly count BLIND as failure (line 194).

**Blast radius:** Confidence baseline: the suite's verdict machinery is fundamentally sound; the gaps above are at its edges (aggregation, premise-verification, self-report binding), not its core.

## Probe: soak-evidence-verification

**Probe summary:** Evidence audit of the 2026-07-15/16 QA session self-report (docs/QA_SESSION_REPORT_2026-07-16.md) against the raw artifacts in /tmp/claude-1000/-home-dmitri-projects-lexa-hub/7cbd4a28-d4ad-4ec1-b53e-cddd53b7a131/scratchpad/. I read QA_CAMPAIGN_SUMMARY.md, QA_CAMPAIGN_FINDINGS.md, all 20 qa-run-*.log soak logs' verdict sections, every mayhem-*.log per-scenario log, the health-logger files, the hub journal captures (hub-openadr-rerun.log, hub-evrule-capture.log), the MQTT report captures (adv-report-capture*.log, pf-alone-capture.log), and cross-checked commits e0864c9/29e9552/fbcaca0/3e907f2 in git. Overall the report is substantially honest and unusually well-evidenced: claims (a) deferred 12/15, (c) regression 0-FAIL, (e) 108 clean health snapshots, (f) event-delay 6P/2F, (g) soc-dither 4/4 with the literal '4700 W at SoC 19%' string, and (h) live verification of both hub fixes are all directly supported by raw artifacts, several verbatim. However, three headline statements overstate the record: (b) 'Batch 2/3 15/15 PASS' is false for csip-pagination-walk (INCONCLUSIVE in the only batch-2 run, never PASSed anywhere, later a confirmed FAIL — the report's own footnote contradicts its table); '§6 Batch aa was 16 PASS / 4 DEGRADED every single cycle' is contradicted by qa-run-12-aa.log (14P/5D/1F); and the report omits a 09:39 recheck in which openadr-limit-adopt — the scenario used to certify flagship fix e0864c9 — FAILED again with a healthy sim on a spurious no-mRID CannotComply, while the report says the fix was 'confirmed fine'. Secondary omissions: the 'full-suite baseline (101)' was truncated at 82/101, batch ad got only 2 valid cycles, run #20 (the promised cycle-4 disambiguation re-run) was aborted after 2/20 scenarios, and csip-pagination-walk was excluded from the soak the report credits with proving it a 'reliable FAIL' (actual evidence: one isolated FAIL run + one unreliable truncated-run attribution).

### EV-9 [high/test-blindspot/confidence=high] — **verifier: PARTLY**
**OMITTED: post-fix openadr-limit-adopt FAILed again at 09:39 with a healthy sim (spurious CannotComply with no CSIP mRID) — report says the fix was 'confirmed fine'**

**Evidence:** qa-adfail-recheck.log:34-40 (09:39, run immediately after the modsim restart, sims healthy): '[FAIL] OpenADR-only export cap binds with no CSIP control active … 1 CannotComply alert(s) posted with no CSIP mRID to attribute them to … posting one for a limit that only OpenADR ever asserted is a protocol violation'. Only after this did the isolated qa-openadr-recheck.log (09:41) PASS. Neither QA_CAMPAIGN_FINDINGS.md, QA_CAMPAIGN_SUMMARY.md, nor the repo report mentions this FAIL — the findings log (run #15 entry) says only 're-run with a healthy+settled sim, openadr-limit-adopt → PASS … Export-cap fix confirmed fine', and report §7.5 repeats 'the export-cap fix is solid'. Two hypotheses the record cannot distinguish: (1) cross-scenario pollution — mqtt-storm ran first in the same 2-scenario run and legitimately posted a CannotComply (qa-adfail-recheck.log:24) that the openadr window may have counted, i.e. an oracle isolation gap; (2) a real intermittent spurious-CannotComply under an OpenADR-only bind (D9 violation, exactly what the scenario exists to catch). Either way, the verification story for the flagship fix has an undisclosed contrary data point, and post-fix the scenario's artifact record is PASS/PASS/PASS/FAIL(run15, sim-attributed)/FAIL(09:39)/PASS — intermittent, not 'solid'.

**Root cause:** The 09:39 recheck paired two scenarios whose oracles share gridsim's /admin/alerts window; the session re-ran the target alone, got PASS, and reported only that.

**Proposed fix:** Re-run openadr-limit-adopt ~10× alone and once paired after mqtt-storm; check gridsim /admin/alerts timestamps vs scenario windows; document the 09:39 FAIL in the report either way.

**Blast radius:** If (2) is real, the hub can emit a protocol-violating 2030.5 Response the utility head-end cannot interpret, and the report steers the next agent away from looking. If (1), the mayhem oracle can FAIL a correct hub when scenarios are batched — an oracle-isolation defect worth fixing before trusting batched CannotComply attribution scenarios.

**Verifier reasoning:** Core claim CONFIRMED: (1) qa-adfail-recheck.log:4-7,34-42 and csip-tls-test/logs/qa/qa-mayhem-20260716-093941.md:3,25-37 prove a 09:37-09:39 paired run (mqtt-storm → openadr-limit-adopt) where openadr-limit-adopt FAILed post-fix ("1 CannotComply alert(s) posted with no CSIP mRID to attribute them to"); qa-openadr-recheck.log:5 (09:41, isolated) then PASSed. (2) The omission is real: QA_CAMPAIGN_FINDINGS.md:78 ("re-run with a healthy+settled sim → PASS … Export-cap fix confirmed fine"), QA_SESSION_REPORT_2026-07-16.md:234 ("the export-cap fix is solid"), and QA_CAMPAIGN_SUMMARY.md (zero openadr mentions) all omit the 09:39 FAIL. (3) "Healthy sim" holds on in-run evidence: errs=0/80 and 0/75, solar responded to 4800W injections (4400W peak export), cap converged in 5s, meter/hub agreed at 0W (qa-adfail-recheck.log:20,27,36) — a 500-ing modsim cannot produce that; and the 09:39 mode (cap HELD, alert misattributed) differs from run 15's "cap never held" mode (qa-run-15-ad.log:203-214), so the run-15 sim-induced attribution cannot cover it. However: the finding's root cause is imprecise and its "intermittent, not solid" implication over-reads. The oracles do not share a window — openadr snapshots /admin/alerts in its own setup/teardown (mayhem_ocpp_openadr.go:714-716,730-732). Verified mechanism: mqtt-storm's armCap posts a 0W CSIP cap with duration_s=90+20=110s (mqtt_scenarios.go:518-522; mayhem.go:2792) at ~09:37:00 so the event ends ~09:38:50 INSIDE openadr's window; deleteControls/resetForScenario delete at gridsim only, never waiting for hub-side release (mayhem.go:2401-2409,2727-2744); the storm episode saw a breach (cannot_comply=true), so at event end the hub's tracker completeActive posts an end-of-event Table 27 code 8/10 (lexa-hub internal/northbound/responses/tracker.go:407-449) which gridsim classifies as an /admin/alerts entry (sim/gridsim/server.go:1089-1105); and openadr-limit-adopt's oracle treats ANY new alert as FAIL since cons.MRID=="" (mayhem_ocpp_openadr.go:783-834). So the FAIL is a near-deterministic oracle-isolation artifact whenever openadr-limit-adopt directly follows a breach-seeing cap scenario — not hub flakiness. Hypothesis (2), a real D9 violation, is refuted at code level: cmd/hub/main.go:781-787 gates plan-breach evidence on OpenADRBoundAxis, cmd/hub/breach.go:260-262 drops empty-MRID device evidence, and every ComplianceAlert carries a non-empty MRID (breach.go:301-311) — a no-mRID CannotComply is not constructible in the hub. Residual uncertainty: the alert's actual subject/received_at live only in gridsim's /admin/alerts (bench, unreachable read-only), so hypothesis (1) is code-proven-plausible rather than log-proven.

**Verifier corrections:** Root cause corrected: not "oracles share gridsim's /admin/alerts window" — each scenario takes its own before/after count. The pollution enters because (a) gridsim's alert list is global and append-only and the openadr oracle counts ANY delta as misattribution (cons.MRID=="" ⇒ attributed always 0, mayhem_ocpp_openadr.go:818-825); (b) the hub's WP-7 end-of-event Response (code 8 or 10 after a breach-seeing event, tracker.go endOfEventCode) for mqtt-storm's 110s-duration cap necessarily POSTs after mqtt-storm's 80s hold ends — i.e. inside the next scenario's window — and gridsim classifies 8/10 as alerts (server.go:1089-1105); (c) a fresh onset-8 re-breach against the still-live-in-hub 0W storm cap (gridsim-side deletion is not hub-side release; resetForScenario uncurtails solar and openadr setup re-injects 4800W PV) is a second path. Consequence: the 09:39 FAIL is a QA scenario-isolation defect that FAILs a correctly-behaving hub, not evidence the export-cap fix is intermittent — but the session never established that; it silently dropped the contrary run. Fix corrected/extended: (1) document the 09:39 FAIL in the report and findings log; (2) make diagnoseOpenADRBind inspect /admin/alerts subjects+received_at (cannotComplyCount at mayhem.go:2417 already parses subjects) and exclude alerts whose subject is a prior scenario's mRID or whose status is an end-of-event code for an already-ended event; (3) alternatively have openadr-limit-adopt's setup wait out the prior event's ValidUntil (+ one walk interval) or verify via hub /status that no CSIP control is active before snapshotting alertsBefore; (4) the proposed 10x-alone + paired-after-mqtt-storm reruns remain a good confirmation matrix — expect alone=PASS, paired-after-breach-seeing-scenario=deterministic FAIL.

## Probe: finding-B-soc-reserve

**Probe summary:** Probed finding B (soc-dither-at-reserve) end to end: read the QA report §7.2/§8, the mayhem scenario+oracle (csip-tls-test cmd/dashboard/mayhem_world.go), the raw soak logs (qa-run-06/11/16, QA_CAMPAIGN_FINDINGS.md — 4/4 FAILs, 56-62 violating samples, "discharging 4700-5000W at SoC 19%" confirmed verbatim), and every reserve-relevant path in lexa-hub: all four discharge authors, checkBatterySafety/EvaluateSafety/criticalBatteryInversion, the constraint-package shadow port, the Tier-0 modbus interlock, and GAP-08's paper trail. The report's finding B is real and its severity is justified, but its suspected root cause is slightly off: the scenario arms an importCap 0 (5000W load / 300W PV), so the discharging author is applyImportLimitRule, and every author DOES check SOCReserve — the defect is that the check is memoryless (raw `b.SOC <= socReserve` per tick, zero hysteresis), so each 21% read re-authorizes a fresh ~4700W discharge and each 19% read merely idles, producing a 4.7kW↔0W square wave that tracks the dither while the physical pack keeps discharging through the line. The guard side is mechanically defeated because battDrainTicks hard-resets to 0 on any single above-reserve or non-discharging sample and needs 3 consecutive qualifying economic ticks (~9s FAST) versus a 4s dither phase — it can never trip; the no-debounce critical path and the Tier-1 fast tick both require chargeCommanded (false here), and the Tier-0 interlock's trip condition also requires charge intent, so it is out of scope by design. The shadow port (constraint/batterysafety.go, importlimit.go, economics.go) reproduces all of this line-for-line, so the defect survives the P5 flip unless fixed on both sides. GAP-08 (csip-tls-test docs/refactor/07_QA_GAP_PLAN.md:121 + TASK-054) predicted exactly this — "leaky counters are believed hold-biased, but no one has swept the boundary" — and this soak was that deferred bench validation confirming the belief false (the counters are not even leaky; they hard-reset). One mitigating mechanic verified: overshoot depth is self-bounding at roughly the dither amplitude plus actuation latency (once true SoC falls below reserve−ε every read is ≤ reserve and all authors stop), so the pack degrades a few points below reserve rather than draining to empty — the 92-day-replay drain-to-0% failure mode is separately closed by applyRestoreRule's unconditional idle, which I verified correct. The CannotComply posting comes from applyImportLimitRule's headroom-breach path and is correct behavior that the fix must preserve. Root-cause fix specified in the findings: a single-owner hysteretic reserve-hold latch at command-authoring time (enter at SOC≤reserve, release only after SOC≥reserve+2pts for scaleTicks(3) ticks) consulted by all four authors, PLUS hold-biased (decay-not-reset) drain/wrong-dir counters with a latched trip, mirrored into the constraint package for shadow parity, with unit dither-trace tests and a bench re-run.

### B-1 [critical/design-flaw/confidence=high] — **verifier: CONFIRMED**
**Reserve gating at every discharge author is memoryless per-tick with zero hysteresis — ±1pt SoC dither re-authorizes full discharge across the reserve line**

**Evidence:** Verified in code. The scenario (csip-tls-test cmd/dashboard/mayhem_world.go:1160-1166) arms `d.postCap("importCap", 0, ...)` with injectEnv(300, 5000) — so the live discharge author is applyImportLimitRule, not dischargingAtReserve (which is a detector, not an author). internal/orchestrator/optimizer.go:2390-2392: `if !math.IsNaN(b.SOC) && b.SOC <= socReserve { continue }` — a raw threshold re-evaluated every tick; the tick after SoC reads 21% the rule ratchets discharge straight back up (optimizer.go:2318 `targetDischargeW := math.Max(0, unconstrainedImportW-conservativeLimitW)` with conservativeLimit=0 → ~4700W; :2403-2412 issues the setpoint). On a 19% tick the loop skips the pack, applyRestoreRule idles it (optimizer.go:2521-2539, `SetpointW: 0 // idle: clear any stale (e.g. discharge) setpoint`), and impGuard.dischargeW is cleared (:2423-2426). Net: the hub emits a 4700W↔0W square wave tracking the dither; with modbus poll (~2s) + desired-doc reconciler + device latency, the physical pack is measured discharging 4700-5000W on ~60 of ~260 one-second samples while reported SoC=19% (raw logs qa-run-06-ae.log:96, qa-run-11-ae.log:98; 4/4 consistent per QA_CAMPAIGN_FINDINGS.md runs #6b/#11/#16). The same memoryless pattern exists at the other three authors: applyPlanRule optimizer.go:822-828 (`if share > 0 && b.SOC <= socReserve { share = 0 }` — clamps to 0 but releases instantly at 20.01%), applyFixedDispatchRule :905-910, applyDemandResponseRule :2008-2013. The CannotComply the report saw comes from :2435-2442 (`importW > limits.importLimitW && remaining > complianceBreachW` → recordBreach with batteryHeadroomReason "battery at SOC reserve") and is correct. Depth of incursion is self-bounding: once true SoC < reserve−ε, every read is ≤20 and all authors skip — so ~1-2pt over-discharge plus latency drain, not a walk to empty.

**Root cause:** Reserve enforcement is a stateless comparison against the instantaneous measured SoC at each authoring site. Any telemetry noise straddling the line (±1pt BMS quantization is realistic on a real site) converts the reserve floor into a ~50%-duty-cycle discharge permit, and the release edge has no margin or dwell, so the hub coin-flips at the boundary exactly as GAP-08 hypothesized.

**Proposed fix:** Enforce the reserve at command-authoring time with a single-owner hysteretic latch, in ADDITION to hardening the guard (B-2): add to DefaultOptimizer a per-pack reserve-hold state (`battReserveHold map[string]bool`, `battReserveRecoverTicks map[string]int`) updated once per tick at the top of Optimize by a new `updateReserveHolds(state.Batteries)`: enter hold when `!IsNaN(SOC) && SOC <= SOCReserve`; while held count consecutive ticks with `SOC >= SOCReserve + reserveReleaseMarginPct` (2.0, above realistic noise) and release only at `scaleTicks(reserveReleaseTicks)` (3, wall-clock-preserving like every other threshold); prune on !Connected/NaN like battDrainTicks. Expose `dischargeBlocked(name)` and replace the four inline `SOC <= socReserve` author checks with it: applyImportLimitRule:2390, applyPlanRule:822 (share>0 → 0), applyFixedDispatchRule:905, applyDemandResponseRule:2008 (the three free functions take the predicate or become methods). Keep the raw comparison as belt-and-braces (hold is a superset). Do NOT touch the breach path :2435 / batteryHeadroomReason:2460 — CannotComply must keep posting, and with the latch it becomes a stable held episode instead of a flapping one (also kinder to breachEpisodes). EvaluateSafety needs no change (it never authors discharge). Tests: new optimizer_reserve_dither_test.go driving Optimize with importCap=0 and SOC sequences 21/19 and 20.5/19.5 alternating — assert (a) zero BatteryCommands with SetpointW>0 after the first ≤reserve sample, (b) plan.Breach non-nil throughout the unmeetable phase, (c) ≤1 discharge→idle sign transition; a release test (recovery to 21% never releases; 22% held 3 ticks does); per-author unit tests for the held-pack skip. Bench: re-run soc-dither-at-reserve expecting PASS on both the INV-SOC-RESERVE and batteryCommandFlaps arms, plus regression on battery-soc-refuse, import-cap family, and the 92-day replay.

**Blast radius:** Any real site whose BMS SoC telemetry is noisy/quantized at the reserve line: the pack is discharged 1-2+ points below the demand-response/backup reserve at ~50% duty, the contactor/inverter sees a 4.7kW↔0W command square wave every ~4s (wear), and CannotComply episodes flap. All four discharge authors affected; worst on import-cap defense where target discharge is largest.

**Verifier reasoning:** Every load-bearing citation verified by direct read. (1) All four discharge authors are stateless per-tick SOC comparisons: internal/orchestrator/optimizer.go:2390-2392 applyImportLimitRule ("if !math.IsNaN(b.SOC) && b.SOC <= socReserve { continue }"), :822-828 applyPlanRule ("if share > 0 && b.SOC <= socReserve { share = 0 }"), :905-910 applyFixedDispatchRule, :2008-2013 applyDemandResponseRule. (2) Square-wave mechanics confirmed and slightly WORSE than stated: the import rule's slew (optimizer.go:2320-2334) only damps ramp-DOWN, and when all packs sit at reserve it clears impGuard.dischargeW to NaN (:2423-2427), so each 21% tick re-fires full targetDischargeW = max(0, unconstrainedImportW-conservativeLimitW) (:2318, ≈4700 W at injectEnv(300,5000)/cap 0) with no slew memory; applyRestoreRule idles the pack at any SoC on 19% ticks (:2521-2539). (3) The backstop detector is defeated by the same statelessness: checkBatterySafety's battDrainTicks resets to 0 on any non-violating tick (:1843-1846) while dischargingAtReserve (:1841) alternates at the injected cadence (ditherHalfPeriodTicks=4, csip-tls-test cmd/dashboard/mayhem_world.go:1628), and criticalBatteryInversion (:1775-1777) requires chargeCommanded — absent here — so no force-disconnect fires. (4) Scenario confirmed at mayhem_world.go:1152-1173 (importCap 0, injectEnv(300,5000), SoC 21.0/19.0 from :1644-1645). (5) Raw-log claims confirmed: qa-run-06-ae.log:91-99 (60 samples, peak 6230 W, out-of-limit 211 s, "discharging 5000 W at SoC 19%", cannot_comply=True), qa-run-11-ae.log:93-101 (56 samples, 4700 W, 282 s), FAILs also in qa-run-06b-ae.log:92 and qa-run-16-ae.log:92 — 4/4. (6) Breach path :2435-2442/:2460-2471 correct as claimed; EvaluateSafety never authors discharge (:1811-1823). Severity=critical stands: real ±1pt BMS quantization at the reserve line converts the floor into a ~50%-duty discharge permit and the debounced safety detector cannot accumulate.

**Verifier corrections:** Root cause is correct. The proposed fix is sound in design (single-owner hysteretic latch at Optimize top, 2pt release margin, scaleTicks dwell, raw check kept as subset) but INCOMPLETE in scope: the identical stateless SOC<=reserve comparisons exist in the constraint-package shadow ports — internal/orchestrator/constraint/importlimit.go:248 ("if !math.IsNaN(b.SOC) && b.SOC <= importSOCReserve") and constraint/economics.go:257, 318, 429 — which the fix never touches. Patching only optimizer.go would make the constraint_shadow harness log persistent divergences during every reserve-boundary episode (polluting the 0-diff P5 flip gate) and would resurrect the flaw the moment those constraints flip active; the latch must be mirrored into the constraint package (or the divergence explicitly documented/accepted), per the CLAUDE.md "do not strip either side" parity discipline. Minor: the proposed prune-on-NaN releases the hold when the BMS drops SoC readings (pack exits hold with unknown SoC); holding through NaN would be safer, though NaN-never-blocks is pre-existing behavior at all four authors, not a regression of the fix.

### B-2 [high/bug/confidence=high] — **verifier: PARTLY**
**checkBatterySafety's drain counter hard-resets on any single compliant sample — the reserve-drain backstop mathematically cannot trip under boundary dither, and every no-debounce path requires charge intent**

**Evidence:** Verified in code. optimizer.go:1841-1846: `dischargingAtReserve := b.PowerW > complianceBreachW && b.SOC <= o.SOCReserve; if dischargingAtReserve { o.battDrainTicks[b.Name]++ } else { o.battDrainTicks[b.Name] = 0 }` — a HARD reset, not the "leaky"/hold-biased counter GAP-08's text believed ("leaky counters are believed hold-biased", csip-tls-test docs/refactor/07_QA_GAP_PLAN.md:121). Trip needs `o.battDrainTicks[b.Name] >= threshold` with threshold = scaleTicks(batteryReserveDrainTicks)=3 (optimizer.go:1754, :1869-1871; scaleTicks is a no-op at the bench FAST 3s cadence, :285-295 with tunedTickInterval=3s at :250) — i.e. 3 CONSECUTIVE economic ticks (~9s) of simultaneously SOC≤20 AND PowerW>100. The injected dither phase is 4s (ditherHalfPeriodTicks=4 @1s, mayhem_world.go:1625-1633), so the counter reaches at most 1-2 before an above-line read zeroes it — it can never fire, matching the observed zero disconnects across 4/4 runs. The escape hatches all require charge intent: criticalBatteryInversion (optimizer.go:1775-1778) `return chargeCommanded && powerW > complianceBreachW && ... soc <= socReserve+5` and EvaluateSafety (:1803-1824) only calls that predicate — under an import cap the commanded setpoint is positive (discharge) or 0, so chargeCommanded is always false. battWrongDirTicks (:1853-1858) likewise requires chargeCommanded. So under discharge-commanded boundary dither there is NO tripping guard anywhere in the hub. Same structural weakness against a real accept-but-ignore pack: a device ignoring its idle command while SoC quantization flickers 19/21 never accumulates 3 consecutive qualifying ticks and is never disconnected.

**Root cause:** The debounce was designed to ride out a single telemetry glitch during a SUSTAINED fault (audit: battery-wrong-sign) and encodes that as consecutive-tick counting with reset-to-zero; nobody swept the boundary case (GAP-08 was filed for exactly this and its bench validation was deferred — TASK-054 status "CODE COMPLETE, NOT YET BENCH-VALIDATED", csip-tls-test docs/QA_FINDINGS.md:284).

**Proposed fix:** Make the counters hold-biased and the trip latched. (1) Decay instead of reset: `else if o.battDrainTicks[b.Name] > 0 { o.battDrainTicks[b.Name]-- }` (same for battWrongDirTicks) so a ≥50%-duty dither accumulates two-forward-one-back and trips within a bounded window, while an isolated 1-in-N glitch still never trips — preserving the original glitch-tolerance contract. (2) Latch the trip: today the force-disconnect (:1878-1888) is re-decided per tick and the counters are deleted the moment the pack reads !Connected (:1834-1837); define release explicitly as sustained recovery (reuse B-1's release condition: SOC ≥ reserve+margin for scaleTicks(3) ticks with no qualifying discharge) before the hub may reconnect — and while designing this, pin down the currently under-specified reconnect path: applyRestoreRule:2521-2539 re-asserts Connect=1 on any pack still MEASURING Connected, so a device that ignores the disconnect write gets reconnect+idle re-commanded next tick and the counters restart from zero (another chatter seam the latch closes). Tests: alternating qualifying/non-qualifying tick tables asserting trip-within-N at ≥50% duty and no-trip for 1-in-10 glitches; a latch test asserting no reconnect until sustained recovery; keep the existing battery-wrong-sign pins green.

**Blast radius:** The measured-effect backstop for a pack that ACKs and ignores its setpoint (the defensive-fault-handling HARD preserve) is blind whenever SoC or power telemetry dithers at the threshold — on a real site that is the norm, not the exception, near the reserve floor.

**Verifier reasoning:** Core claim VERIFIED in code, adversarially: (1) hard reset confirmed at /home/dmitri/projects/lexa-hub/internal/orchestrator/optimizer.go:1841-1846 ('o.battDrainTicks[b.Name] = 0' on any non-qualifying sample) and :1854-1858 for battWrongDirTicks; trip needs >= scaleTicks(3) consecutive ticks (:1754, :1869-1872; scaleTicks no-op at tunedTickInterval=3s, :250/:285-295; floors at 2 even at STOCK 15s). (2) Dither math holds: ditherHalfPeriodTicks=4 @1s and socDither 19/21 (csip-tls-test/cmd/dashboard/mayhem_world.go:1628, :1644-1645) means a 4s qualifying phase spans at most 2 economic ticks at 3s cadence (1 at 15s) — the drain trip is unreachable under the injected dither. (3) Every no-debounce path requires charge intent: criticalBatteryInversion leads with 'chargeCommanded &&' (:1775-1778), EvaluateSafety only calls it (:1810-1811), wrongDirection requires it (:1853); chargeCommandedFor returns false for setpoints >= 0 (:1783-1793). I additionally verified the Tier-0 interlock the finding did not check — cmd/modbus/interlock.go:134 'if !(charge && discharging && nearReserve)' is also charge-gated — so 'no tripping guard anywhere' holds even including lexa-modbus, strengthening the finding. (4) Chatter seam confirmed: counters deleted on !Connected (:1834-1837), disconnect re-decided per tick (:1878-1888), applyRestoreRule re-asserts Conn=1+idle for any pack still MEASURING Connected (:2520-2541) and runs before checkBatterySafety (:1768). Doc citations verified: 07_QA_GAP_PLAN.md GAP-08 'leaky counters are believed hold-biased' (~:121-123); QA_FINDINGS.md:284 TASK-054 'code complete, bench validation pending'. Severity=high is fair (safety backstop defeatable at the boundary; Tier-0 also blind under discharge intent).

**Verifier corrections:** Three corrections. (a) Overstated sub-claim: a real accept-but-ignore pack is NOT 'never disconnected' — genuine drain >100W lowers true SOC, so 19/21 quantization flicker cannot persist; once readback sits <= reserve on both steps (18/19), 3 consecutive ticks accumulate and drainTrip fires. The real-hardware defect is bounded DELAYED detection (flicker-band transit, potentially tens of minutes at low drain), with permanent defeat only under sustained boundary-straddling telemetry (the injected case). (b) Evidence framing: 'zero disconnects across 4/4 runs' is consistent-with, not evidence-of — the mayhem batsim honors commands (with latency) and the scenario's own Expected (mayhem_world.go:1155) does not call for a disconnect; finding B's 4/4 over-discharge samples come mainly from the discharge-allocation/latency path at the boundary, which the proposed counter fix alone would NOT clear. (c) Fix incomplete: the identical hard reset exists in the TASK-062 shadow port at internal/orchestrator/constraint/batterysafety.go:168-179 ('sess.drainTicks[b.Name] = 0' / 'sess.wrongDirTicks[b.Name] = 0'); any decay/latch change must land in BOTH copies (CLAUDE.md: 'do not strip either side') or the constraint-shadow diff gate flags divergence and blocks the P5 flip. The latch design must also state its interaction with Tier-0 interlock seniority (interlock.go isTripped suppresses reconciler connect-restores; the interlock itself has no drain counter and stays charge-gated).

### B-3 [medium/design-flaw/confidence=high]
**Constraint-package shadow port reproduces both defects verbatim — fix must land on both sides or the P5 flip re-ships it**

**Evidence:** Verified in code. internal/orchestrator/constraint/batterysafety.go:167-171: `if b.PowerW > exportComplianceBreachW && b.SOC <= c.socReserve { sess.drainTicks[b.Name]++ } else { sess.drainTicks[b.Name] = 0 }` — the identical hard reset (the file's own comments say "Ported verbatim"); :183-186 same consecutive-threshold trip; :105-108 criticalBatteryInversion same chargeCommanded gate; EvaluateFast :244-257 same. constraint/importlimit.go:248: `if !math.IsNaN(b.SOC) && b.SOC <= importSOCReserve { continue }` — the identical memoryless author skip; constraint/economics.go:257 `if !math.IsNaN(b.SOC) && b.SOC <= c.socReserve { continue // protect reserve }` and :316 (plan-follow clamp) likewise. The QA report §2.1 already noted the same shadow-parity debt for the new planExportDischargeCapW — this finding widens it: B-1/B-2's fixes must be mirrored or the ≥1-week 0-diff shadow gate will actually ENFORCE keeping the bug (a hysteretic legacy side would diverge from an unfixed candidate side, or vice versa).

**Root cause:** TASK-060/061/062 are deliberate bit-faithful ports ("do not strip either side", CLAUDE.md), so they faithfully ported the boundary defect.

**Proposed fix:** Mirror B-1's reserve-hold into a session-owned struct (BatterySafetySession or a new ReserveHoldSession in constraint/session.go with reset semantics documented like the others) consulted by importlimit.go:248, economics.go:257/:316; mirror B-2's decay-not-reset into batterysafety.go evaluateTrips. Land legacy+candidate changes in the SAME commit and extend the shadow tests (batterysafety_shadow_test.go / shadow_active_test.go pattern) with the dither trace asserting 0 divergence, so the shadow gate proves parity of the FIXED behavior.

**Blast radius:** Shadow-only today (candidate plans are discarded), but becomes the live path at the per-axis `active` flips; also any shadow soak run across the fix window will log spurious divergences if the two sides are fixed asymmetrically.

### B-4 [info/ok-verified/confidence=high]
**Tier-0 interlock correctly does not cover this case — its trip is charge-intent-gated by design (sign-inversion only), so no interlock bug; optional hardening candidate**

**Evidence:** Verified in code. cmd/modbus/interlock.go:132-134: `discharging := ...m.W > interlockDischargeW; nearReserve := ...m.SOC <= reserve+interlockReserveMarginPct; if !(charge && discharging && nearReserve) { ... return false }` — reserve IS in its condition set, but the trip additionally requires `charge` = the hub's last command was a charge (noteControl :108-117: `charge := cmd.SetpointW != nil && *cmd.SetpointW < 0`). In the dither scenario the hub's commands alternate +4700W/0W, so charge is always false and the interlock never evaluates the reserve at all. This matches its documented scope (:37-43: "a pack the hub commanded to CHARGE is measured DISCHARGING while at/below its SOC reserve ... audit: battery-wrong-sign") — it is a sign-inversion reflex, not a reserve-floor enforcer, and cannot be, since it has no visibility into whether a discharge command was legitimately authored above the line. Not a defect.

**Root cause:** By design: the hub is the author of legitimate below-reserve-adjacent discharges, so the edge device cannot distinguish a dither-authored discharge from a valid one without the hysteresis state only the hub has.

**Proposed fix:** Optional defense-in-depth AFTER B-1 lands: since a hysteresis-held hub never commands discharge at/below reserve, the interlock could gain a second, generously-debounced condition (measured discharge >100W while SOC ≤ reserve−2pts sustained for N polls, regardless of command sign) as a last-ditch floor — but only with a wide margin so it can never fight a legitimate hub command (the guard-vs-guard oscillation the interlock doc explicitly exists to prevent). Not required to close finding B.

**Blast radius:** None (behavior is as designed).

### B-5 [info/ok-verified/confidence=high]
**GAP-08 verified: finding B is the live confirmation of a pre-identified, deliberately deferred bench validation — the 'hold-biased' belief was recorded and was false**

**Evidence:** Verified in docs. GAP-08 exists only in the bench repo (nothing in lexa-hub/docs matches): csip-tls-test/docs/refactor/07_QA_GAP_PLAN.md:121-127 — "GAP-08 Threshold dither (hold-biased leaky counters, unswept) → TASK-054. Why: SoC dithering exactly at reserve ... leaky counters are believed hold-biased, but no one has swept the boundary; INV-HUNT only catches sustained oscillation." csip-tls-test/docs/QA_FINDINGS.md:284+ records TASK-054 as "code complete, bench validation pending" with the 10× solo runs explicitly deferred to a later HIL session. The overnight soak was that deferred validation and it falsified the belief (the counters hard-reset, they are not leaky — see B-2). The QA report's §7.2 hedge ("likely confirms a known gap live") is accurate. One polish item: the scenario's committed Fix hint (mayhem_world.go:1840, "verify it re-evaluates every tick against the MEASURED SoC, not a stale or hysteresis-delayed read") points AWAY from the correct fix — the guard does re-evaluate measured SoC every tick, and the cure is precisely hysteresis; the hint should be rewritten alongside the fix so the next reader isn't steered wrong.

**Blast radius:** Process: none open — the gap tracking worked as intended; only the misleading oracle Fix text needs a one-line update when B-1/B-2 land.

### B-6 [info/ok-verified/confidence=high]
**QA report's finding-B claims verified against raw artifacts — consistent 4/4, magnitudes accurate, one phrasing nuance**

**Evidence:** Verified in logs. qa-run-06-ae.log:91-96: "[FAIL] Battery SoC dithers ±ε across the 20% reserve line ... INV-SOC-RESERVE violated on 60 samples (t=41–293s); first: discharging 5000 W at SoC 19%"; qa-run-11-ae.log:93-98: "56 samples (t=33–301s) ... 4700 W at SoC 19%"; QA_CAMPAIGN_FINDINGS.md:59 ("confirmed 2/2 ... 62 samples ... 4700W at SoC 19% ... Hub DID post CannotComply but still over-discharged"), :68 (3/3), :79 ("FAIL=soc-dither ... now 4/4"). The oracle predicate is sound for this claim: socReserveOverDischarge (mayhem_world.go:1726-1751) uses simulator ground-truth watts (BatterySimW) against the forced SoC, post-settling (T > mayConvergeDeadlineS), so it is not an artifact of hub-side staleness. Nuance: "hub keeps discharging below reserve" is duty-cycled rather than a standing setpoint — the hub never issues a discharge command on a tick where its own snapshot reads ≤20% (it idles via applyRestoreRule); it re-authorizes on every above-line read and the physical discharge persists through the below-line phases via actuation latency. The report's §8 synthesis (one hold-bias/hysteresis hardening effort covering B+D) is directionally correct; per B-1 the fix must ALSO include the authoring-side latch, not only the guard debounce that §7.2's "where to look" names.

**Blast radius:** None — report claims stand; next agent should just widen §7.2's fix scope from 'dischargingAtReserve debounce' to author-side hysteresis + guard hold-bias + shadow parity (B-1/B-2/B-3).

## Probe: finding-C-pagination

**Probe summary:** Probe of QA finding C (csip-pagination-walk reliable FAIL: hub adopts page-1 5000W cap, never sees page-2's superseding 1000W cap). I read commit cf5d2b7 in full, the hub's paging loop (internal/northbound/discovery/paginate.go), the walker wiring (walker.go steps 6b/6c and all four *Paged fetchers), the vendored csipmodel list types, the scheduler's supersession/tie-break logic, the gridsim side (sim/gridsim/paginate.go, admin.go control injection, server.go routing, tlsserver request parsing), and the mayhem scenario+oracle (cmd/dashboard/mayhem_pagination.go). I ran the hub and gridsim test suites fresh and built a byte-faithful gridsim-emulation reproduction (via go -overlay, repo untouched) that drives the hub's real fetchExtendedDERControlListPaged against gridsim's exact serving of the scenario: the current hub source pages correctly (GET /derp/0/derc then /derp/0/derc?s=1&l=1), assembles both controls, and the supersession winner is CTRL-PAGE2. DEFINITIVE ANSWER: none of the four offered hypotheses is the defect — not (a) termination logic, not (b) All/Results parse, not (c) gridsim (it honors ?s= correctly), not (d) scheduler supersession. The root cause is DEPLOYMENT STALENESS: cf5d2b7 touches only files compiled into the lexa-northbound binary, bin/arm64/lexa-northbound was last built 2026-07-14 20:28 (a day BEFORE the 2026-07-15 19:36 commit), `strings` on that binary shows zero pagination code while sibling walker strings are present, and the QA session's own report (§3, line 138) states only lexa-hub and lexa-modbus were deployed. The bench DUT ran a pre-fix single-GET walker; the rebuilt gridsim then correctly exposed it (the earlier INCONCLUSIVE→reliable-FAIL flip matches the gridsim rebuild). The QA report's claim that "cf5d2b7 is incomplete / covers DERProgramList but not DERControlList" is wrong in both directions: the fix covers DERControlList (walker.go:339), and malform-pagination's PASS proves nothing about paging (gridsim's MalformPagination serves all real entries on page 1 with a lying all=999, so a non-paging hub passes it too). Exact fix: rebuild lexa-northbound (make wolfssl-arm64 + make build-arm64 — the /tmp sysroot is wiped on reboot) and deploy it to 69.0.0.2, then re-run csip-pagination-walk (expect PASS). The step-6c bare ActiveDERControlList fetch is the same class in principle but ProgramState.ActiveControls has no consumer anywhere in the codebase, so its impact today is nil.

### PAG-4 [medium/test-blindspot/confidence=high]
**QA oracle asserts unobserved wire behavior and bench observability cannot distinguish page GETs — the diagnosis machinery that misled the session**

**Evidence:** cmd/dashboard/mayhem_pagination.go:166 hard-codes the FAIL diagnosis "it did a single GET of the list and silently missed every entry past page 1" — but diagnosePaginationWalk (:111-196) judges ONLY the adopted mRID from /status samples; it never observes GETs, so it cannot distinguish 'never fetched page 2' from 'fetched both but adopted page 1' (which would have implicated the scheduler instead). Compounding it, gridsim's request log strips the query string — server.go:255 `log.Printf("[gridsim] %s %s (peer=%s)", r.Method, path, ...)` with path=r.URL.Path — so "GET /derp/0/derc" and "GET /derp/0/derc?s=1&l=1" log identically and even manual log inspection cannot confirm paging. Additionally, malform-pagination cannot corroborate the paging loop at all: sim/gridsim/malform.go:34 defines it as a DERProgramList "whose all= count lies (999 across pages, one served, no next page)" — a pre-fix single-GET hub passes it trivially, so the QA report's inference "cf5d2b7 covers DERProgramList (malform-pagination PASSes)" was unsound.

**Root cause:** Oracle diagnosis strings written as narrative rather than derived from observations; gridsim logging drops RequestURI.

**Proposed fix:** (1) Log r.URL.RequestURI() (or path+RawQuery) in gridsim's request log. (2) Have the pagination scenario count offset GETs server-side (e.g. a per-scenario GET counter exposed on /admin, or parse gridsim logs for s= requests) and fold 'paged vs single-GET' into the verdict so the two failure modes are distinguishable. (3) Reword the canned FAIL diagnosis to state what was observed (adopted mRID) vs inferred.

**Blast radius:** Any pagination-adjacent regression will again produce a confidently-wrong root-cause narrative; QA certification of paging behavior currently rests on a single scenario whose failure text overclaims.

### PAG-6 [medium/process/confidence=high]
**QA session report finding C mis-root-causes a correct fix as 'incomplete' — hand-off would send the next agent to rewrite working code**

**Evidence:** docs/QA_SESSION_REPORT_2026-07-16.md:46 ("The P1-1 pagination fix cf5d2b7 is incomplete") and :213 ("covers the DERProgramList ... but not the DERControlList") are both false: cf5d2b7's diff wires DERControlList through fetchExtendedDERControlListPaged (walker.go:339, present in the commit and at HEAD), and my reproduction proves the code correct against the exact scenario payload. The report's §7.3 'Where to look' directs effort at paginate.go's fast-path, walker steps 6b/6c, and gridsim — none of which is broken. The actual defect (fix never deployed to the DUT) is absent from the report, which even documents the partial deploy itself at :138 without connecting it. The session had the no-code-change directive and did flag rather than fix (QA_CAMPAIGN_FINDINGS.md:37-38 lists the right suspects), but 'verify the DUT is running the code under test' was never performed despite the session having already been burned once by a stale gridsim on the same scenario (report :175).

**Root cause:** No build-provenance check in the QA loop: scenarios judge behavior with no assertion about WHICH build produced it, and per-service version stamping exists (Makefile:24 LDFLAGS -X lexa-hub/internal/buildinfo.Version) but is surfaced only by lexa-api (cmd/api/main.go:41-49 -version flag).

**Proposed fix:** Amend the report's §7.3 (or file the correction alongside it). Add a mayhem preflight that reads each service's build version from the DUT (extend /status or per-service metrics with buildinfo.Version for all six services, not just lexa-api) and refuses to run — or stamps every finding INCONCLUSIVE — when the DUT SHA doesn't match the checkout under test.

**Blast radius:** Every future mayhem verdict on a partially-deployed bench is suspect in both directions: real fixes read as broken (this case) and broken code can read as fixed if an old binary happens to pass.

### PAG-5 [low/design-flaw/confidence=high]
**Step 6c bare (unpaged) ActiveDERControlList fetch: same defect class in principle, but the fetched data has zero consumers today**

**Evidence:** walker.go:350 `act, err := w.fetchDERControlList(ctx, prog.ActiveDERControlListLink.Href)` is a bare single-page fetch (fetchDERControlList at walker.go:459-462 has no paging wrapper), so a spec-compliant server paging its ActiveDERControlList would silently truncate it — and gridsim's pageResource (paginate.go:111-115) WOULD page a scalar DERControlList at /derp/0/actderc if armed on that path. However, `grep -rn ActiveControls` across the whole lexa-hub repo shows ProgramState.ActiveControls (walker.go:100-103) is written at walker.go:354 and read NOWHERE — not by the scheduler (which evaluates ps.Controls, scheduler.go:533), not by publish/, not by cmd/. It is dead data; the QA report's note that 6c is 'bare by design' is accurate as to impact.

**Root cause:** ActiveDERControlList was discovered for completeness but never wired into evaluation; the P1-1 fix skipped it since nothing consumes it.

**Proposed fix:** Either wrap step 6c in fetchPagedList with DERControlList glue (four lines, mirrors walker.go:511-521) for class parity, or delete the ActiveControls field and the step-6c fetch until something needs it — carrying dead unpaged data invites a future consumer to trust a truncated list. Add a doc comment either way.

**Blast radius:** None today. Becomes a real truncation bug the day ActiveControls gains a consumer (e.g. cross-checking server-declared active events against the scheduler's own resolution).

### PAG-2 [info/ok-verified/confidence=high]
**Hub pagination code verified correct end-to-end: fetchPagedList termination, csipmodel All/Results parse, and scheduler supersession all behave as designed**

**Evidence:** paginate.go:85 fast-path `if uint32(len(acc)) >= all` correctly does NOT trigger on all=2/len=1; loop at :111-139 pages by offset with href dedupe (:122-131), empty-page break (:136), 256-page guard (:112), and fail-closed mid-pagination error propagation (:116-119). walker.go:339 wires step 6b to fetchExtendedDERControlListPaged, and walker.go:511-521 supplies correct all/results/href/install glue. vendor/lexa-proto/csipmodel/der.go:283-290 declares `All uint32 xml:"all,attr"` / `Results uint32 xml:"results,attr"` — parses gridsim's serialization (verified by reproduction: page-1 parsed all=2 results=1 entries=1). scheduler.go:550-563: potentiallySuperseded events are skipped only when actually superseded, and among overlapping active events "latest creationTime wins" with MRID tie-break — CTRL-PAGE2 (creationTime t0+1) beats CTRL-PAGE1 (t0-5) even with the ~1s POST-arrival start skew, verified in the reproduction. Existing tests TestWalker_AssemblesAllPages / TestWalker_SinglePageFetchMissesTail / TestFetchPagedList_LyingAllTerminates / TestFetchPagedList_MidPaginationErrorFailsClosed all pass fresh (-count=1). My additional gridsim-byte-faithful repro (scalar model.DERControlList storage, MarshalIndent + xml decl, applyPagination semantics including Atoi-default-0 and l-capping) passes: hub issues ?s=1&l=1 and assembles both entries.

**Root cause:** n/a — verified correct

**Proposed fix:** Optional: commit a gridsim-faithful variant of the reproduction (scalar DERControlList + 1s creation/start skew) into pagination_test.go for parity with the bench scenario's exact shape; incremental value is modest since existing coverage is strong.

**Blast radius:** n/a

### PAG-3 [info/ok-verified/confidence=high]
**Gridsim positive-pagination serving verified correct — hypothesis (c) is false**

**Evidence:** csip-tls-test sim/gridsim/paginate.go:59-76 applyPagination honors ?s=/?l= (parseUintQuery :143-148), path-scopes correctly against r.URL.Path (query already stripped — server.go:253 `path := r.URL.Path`, :266 passes r.URL.Query(); tlsserver/handlers.go:47 builds the request via http.ReadRequest, so URL.Path/Query are standard), pageSlice :80-91 clamps correctly, and pageResource :99-138 covers both *model.DERControlList and *model.ExtendedDERControlList with honest all=<full>/results=<slice>. admin.go:439 keys injected control hrefs by mRID ("/derp/%d/derc/%s") explicitly so href-deduping paged clients see distinct entries. The two mayhem controls land in /derp/0/derc via upsert (admin.go:472-481) and are correctly NOT added to /derp/0/actderc when posted with explicit mRIDs (replaceScalarInPlace no-op, admin.go:490-497/567-575). `go test ./sim/gridsim/` passes fresh.

**Root cause:** n/a — verified correct

**Proposed fix:** none

**Blast radius:** n/a
