## Probe: finding-D-delay-clockstep

**Probe summary:** Probed the two finding-D boundary/timing failures by reading the product code (internal/northbound/run+scheduler+discovery, internal/tlsclient, internal/utilitytime, cmd/hub/state.go, internal/orchestrator engine/planner), the mayhem harness (csip-tls-test cmd/dashboard/mayhem*.go, sim/gridsim/delay.go), and the prior session's raw run logs/reports. (1) csip-event-delay: the product's fail-closed path is verified correct — a 20s /dcap delay exceeds the 15s SO_RCVTIMEO, every walk fails (each burning ~30s via doGet's blind same-path retry), RunOnce publishes nothing on error, and the walker hard-fails partial trees — so nothing northbound-side can unseat the cap mid-fault. The FAIL runs are cross-run contamination: back-to-back runs are ~80s apart while each run's cap event lives holdS+20=95s, so run N's retained 0W cap expires ~11s into run N+1; armAfterCapAdopted matches only (typ, limW), which the leftover cap satisfies, so it arms the delay before run N+1's own cap is ever adopted; when no successful walk lands in the ~5s inter-run hole (the loop is usually stuck in a 30s failing walk), the hub — correctly — drops the leftover at its ValidUntil (debounced), applyRestoreRule un-curtails, and the window burns from t≈26 to the end, exactly matching the observed 42–50s breaches, breach onset ≈t=26–30, and cannot_comply=false. (2) local-clock-step-forward: TASK-037's residual gap is real and located — the utility-time anchor is composed from clock reads taken at different instants (walker.go:233 offset at /tm parse vs publish.go:330 Ts at publish vs run.go:360 anchor at walk end; also run.go:598-601's rewalk republish pairs a fresh Ts with a cached offset), so a wall step landing inside that window displaces utility time by the full step for up to one discovery interval; downstream, the northbound scheduler has NO debounce on controlExpired and its clock-regression guard is backward-only (scheduler.go:318-324, 374), so a forward-poisoned serverNow instantly replaces an active event with the DEFAULT (a genuine unseat), while on the hub a poisoned anchor shifts daily-plan slot selection (engine.go:983-984) with no debounce. The specific t=82–86s breach in the FAIL run was NOT an unseat — cannot_comply=true and the final plan line show the export-limit rule still active — it is consistent with a backward-poisoned anchor (or an EV-draw transient) making plan-follow discharge 1230–3600W over the active cap, i.e. the session report's "unseat" narrative contradicts its own evidence. Fixes and tests are itemized per finding.

### ED-1 [high/test-blindspot/confidence=high] — **verifier: CONFIRMED**
**csip-event-delay ~25% FAIL is a harness race (cross-run retained-cap contamination + identity-blind arm gate), not a product fail-closed defect**

**Evidence:** Product side verified: internal/northbound/run/run.go:309-327 walk error path publishes NOTHING (`slog.Warn("lexa-northbound: discovery error — holding last-published control (fail-closed)"...); return`); internal/northbound/discovery/walker.go:203-341 hard-fails every required sub-fetch (`return nil, fmt.Errorf("step 6 (DERControlList for %s): %w"...)`) so no partial tree can resolve the default; internal/tlsclient/fetcher.go:159-175 doGet closes the session on every error (no keep-alive desync possible). Harness side: mayhem_csipedge.go:421 arms `{"path": "/dcap", "delay_ms": 20000, "duration_s": 90}`; sim/gridsim/delay.go:72 is exact-path match; mayhem.go:51 `mayConvergeDeadlineS = 30` explains why counted violations start at t=30. Scratchpad qa-eventdelay-rate.txt: 6 PASS / 2 FAIL over 8 runs; qa-ed-3.log FAIL details as above; PASS runs qa-ed-1/4/5 show 4-9s out-of-limit WITH cannot_comply=true (settle ramp after a default interlude), qa-ed-2 shows 0s.

**Root cause:** Each run's cap event outlives the run: postCapProg sets duration_s = holdS+20 = 95s (csip-tls-test cmd/dashboard/mayhem.go:2792 `"duration_s": holdS + 20`), but the characterization runs were ~80s apart (report timestamps 032654/032814/032933, deltas 79-80s), so run N's retained 0W cap is still on lexa/csip/control and in the hub with ValidUntil ≈ run N+1 t+11s. armAfterCapAdopted arms the fault on ANY 0W exportCap: mayhem.go:743 `if h.ctrlActive && h.ctrlTyp == typ && h.ctrlLimW == limW` — it cannot distinguish run N's leftover from run N+1's new event even though /status exposes the MRID (mayhem.go:2555) and cons.MRID is in hand. If the leftover is still adopted at the first 2s poll, the /dcap delay arms ~t=2 and (20s delay > 15s DefaultReadTimeout, lexa-hub internal/tlsclient/config.go:19) seals every subsequent walk, so run N+1's fresh cap is never discovered; the hub then CORRECTLY drops the leftover at its ValidUntil (~t=11) after the 9s FAST debounce (cmd/hub/state.go:736-756, utilitytime.Expired), applyRestoreRule un-curtails PV, and the window breaches from t≈26 with no active control → no breach episode → cannot_comply=false — all matching qa-ed-3 (breach t=30–76, 50s total, cannot_comply=false). PASS runs are the interleavings where one successful walk lands in the ~5s hole between run N teardown's delay-clear and run N+1's arm (the walk loop is otherwise occupied ~30s per failing walk), republishing current truth first — explaining the observed trimodal outcomes (0s breach / 4-12s settle breach + CannotComply / permanent FAIL) and the ~25% rate.

**Proposed fix:** (a) armAfterCapAdopted: match the scenario's own control — compare /status csip_control.mrid against cons.MRID (both already available) instead of (typ, limW). (b) Inter-run hygiene: setup should first wait until the hub's active control is not a leftover 0W cap (or teardown should wait for the hub to return to default/none after deleteControls). (c) Size the event to the hold so it cannot straddle the next run. Test: harness unit test replaying two back-to-back scenario timelines asserting the arm gate never fires on the prior run's MRID.

**Blast radius:** QA trustworthiness: the oracle FAILs a correct hub ~25% of the time on this scenario, and the same contamination pattern can affect any back-to-back postCap scenario whose predecessor sealed the walk (e.g. following csip-pagination-walk in batch ab). It also mis-directed the session's triage toward RunOnce/tlsclient.

**Verifier reasoning:** Every load-bearing citation checks out on direct read. PRODUCT (verified in code): lexa-hub internal/northbound/run/run.go:309-326 walk-error path publishes NOTHING ("FAIL CLOSED on a walk error: publish NOTHING"... slog.Warn ...; return); internal/northbound/discovery/walker.go:209/227/242/256/303/315/327/341 hard-fails every required step and /dcap is step 1, so the 20s delay kills each walk at first fetch; internal/tlsclient/config.go:19 DefaultReadTimeout=15s < 20s delay, and fetcher.go doGet (~158-177) redials+retries once (two 15s timeouts ≈ the finding's ~30s per failing walk) and closes the session on error; cmd/hub/state.go:737-757 (utilitytime.Expired + r.expiry.Observe, Confirm=3 per utilitytime.go:10) correctly drops an adopted control at its OWN ValidUntil while walks are sealed — so dropping run N's leftover mid-window is correct behavior, not a defect. HARNESS (verified in code): csip-tls-test cmd/dashboard/mayhem_csipedge.go:421 arms /dcap delay 20000ms/90s; sim/gridsim/delay.go:71-73 exact-path match; mayhem.go:2792 duration_s=holdS+20 with HoldS=75 (mayhem_csipedge.go:460,465) ⇒ 95s cap lifetime; mayhem.go:743 arm gate is identity-blind (`h.ctrlActive && h.ctrlTyp == typ && h.ctrlLimW == limW`) even though MRID is parsed (mayhem.go:2555/2623, sample field AdoptedMRID at 794) and cons.MRID exists (2808); invariants.go:62 excuses samples T<=30 (mayConvergeDeadlineS, mayhem.go:51) explaining breach counting from t=30; teardown (mayhem_csipedge.go:474-477) deletes gridsim controls but never waits for the hub to relinquish the adopted/retained control. LOGS (verified): reports 032654/032814/032933 are 80/79s apart (qa-ed-2/qa-ed-1/qa-ed-3 respectively — temporal order differs from log numbering, deltas as claimed); qa-ed-3 FAIL breach t=30-76, 50s, peak 4400W, cannot_comply=False, adopted=True; PASS runs trimodal (0s / 4-9s settle with cannot_comply=True); 2/8 FAIL = 25% per qa-eventdelay-rate.txt. Arithmetic: leftover ValidUntil lands ≈ run N+1 t=13-17, +3-tick FAST debounce ⇒ drop ≈ t=22-26, PV ramp ⇒ 4400W by first counted sample t=30 — fits qa-ed-3 exactly. Caveat: no hub/northbound journal from the 03:28-03:29 window exists in the scratchpad (gridsim.log/dash.log are Jul-15 stubs), so the specific qa-ed-3 timeline is a strongly-supported inference from code+timing, not journal-proven; a sub-variant (an in-flight walk adopting the bench default 5kW after the leftover-triggered arm — export 4400W < 5000W default, hence no CannotComply) yields the identical FAIL signature and is equally harness contamination. Proposed fixes are sound: (a) MRID-match the arm gate (both values already in hand) is the real fix; (b) inter-run hygiene and (c) sizing duration to the hold are sensible hardening.

**Verifier corrections:** Two minor refinements, neither changing the verdict: (1) the leftover cap's ValidUntil lands at run N+1 t≈13-17s (cap posted ≈ report_N−78s, +95s; next run starts ≈ report_N+3-4s), not ~t+11s as claimed — same mechanism, slightly later; the observed t=30 breach onset then follows from expiry + 3-tick debounce + PV ramp. (2) Fix (a) as stated only repairs the arm gate at mayhem.go:743; scanSamples' adoption accounting at mayhem.go:984 (`smp.HubAdopted && smp.AdoptedTyp == cons.Typ`) is identity-blind in the same way — it is why the FAIL report shows adopted=True despite the new cap never being adopted — and should compare AdoptedMRID (already recorded per-sample at mayhem.go:794) against cons.MRID too, so the metric can't certify a leftover as adoption. Also note the FAIL signature is compatible with a second contamination sub-variant (post-arm in-flight walk adopting the bench default 5kW cap; 4400W export sits under 5000W so no CannotComply), which the MRID-gate fix also eliminates.

### ED-3 [high/design-flaw/confidence=high] — **verifier: PARTLY**
**On expiry during a discovery outage the hub reverts to UNCONSTRAINED instead of the last-known DefaultDERControl**

**Evidence:** cmd/hub/state.go:736-756 (expiry drop → `r.lastCSIP = nil`); run.go:309-319 comment: "the hub's own local clock discipline ... still releases it at ValidUntil if the outage outlives the control"; scheduler.go resolve() serves the default only on a SUCCESSFUL walk; bus.ActiveControl has no default-fallback fields.

**Root cause:** The retained lexa/csip/control doc carries only the ACTIVE control (publish.ToActiveControl, publish.go:325-337); the DefaultDERControl the walker has repeatedly observed is never retained as a fallback. When the hub's debounced expiry drops a control at ValidUntil while northbound is in a fail-closed walk hold (run.go:314-319 explicitly delegates release-at-ValidUntil to the hub), state.CSIPControl becomes nil and applyRestoreRule un-curtails to nameplate. IEEE 2030.5 event-end semantics revert the client to the default DER control; a site whose event expires mid-WAN-outage therefore runs uncapped (the bench default would be a 5kW export cap) until discovery recovers — potentially hours of wrong control on a real site. This is exactly the terminal state of the ED-1 FAIL runs: correct per the current documented design, wrong per spec intent.

**Proposed fix:** Carry the highest-priority program's DefaultDERControl on the retained bus doc (additive fields on bus.ActiveControl, or a second retained topic), and make the hub's expiry-drop path fall back to enforcing it (Source="default", ValidUntil=0) instead of nil. Test: hub reader test — adopt an event control with a default present, age past ValidUntil with no new message, assert enforcement degrades to the default limits rather than to nil.

**Blast radius:** Any deployment where a DERControl event ends during a WAN/head-end outage and a DefaultDERControl exists: export/import limits silently lift to unconstrained until discovery recovers.

**Verifier reasoning:** Design-flaw core CONFIRMED in code: (1) cmd/hub/state.go:737-755 — debounced expiry sets `r.lastCSIP = nil` with no fallback; lines 757-758 only populate state.CSIPControl when lastCSIP != nil, so the optimizer runs unconstrained and applyRestoreRule (internal/orchestrator/optimizer.go:551-560) un-curtails. (2) internal/northbound/run/run.go:309-326 — walk error publishes nothing ("holding last-published control (fail-closed)") and the comment at 314-317 explicitly delegates release-at-ValidUntil to the hub during an outage. (3) The default is only resolvable on a SUCCESSFUL walk: run.go:399 `d.sched.Evaluate(tree.Programs, serverNow)` is reached only after walker.Discover succeeds; scheduler.go:260-276 is the sole DefaultDERControl fallback. (4) bus.ActiveControl (internal/bus/messages.go:73-110) carries exactly one control (Source = event|default|none) with no default-fallback fields, and publish.ToActiveControl (publish.go:325-389) converts only the winning scheduler.ActiveControl (scheduler.go:49-114 — no default carried alongside an event). So an event expiring mid-outage degrades to unconstrained (modulo OpenADR limits merged at state.go:781), not to the last-known default — contrary to 2030.5 event-end revert-to-default intent. The proposed fix (carry default on the retained doc; hub expiry-drop falls back to Source="default", ValidUntil=0) is coherent and additive. HOWEVER the empirical anchor is wrong — see corrections.

**Verifier corrections:** The claim "this is exactly the terminal state of the ED-1 FAIL runs" is refuted. (a) qa-ed-1.log is a PASS run ("stayed up and kept enforcing the safe cap"); the FAILs were qa-ed-3.log (breach t=30-76s, 4400 W) and qa-eventdelay-2.log extra-run 3 (50 s out-of-limit). (b) Timing excludes the expiry mechanism: the scenario posts its 0 W export cap with duration_s = holdS+20 = 95 s (csip-tls-test cmd/dashboard/mayhem.go:2792; HoldS:75 at mayhem_csipedge.go:460), so ValidUntil ≈ t+93-95 while the FAIL breaches ran t=30/34 through 76 — entirely INSIDE the control's validity window; the hub's ValidUntil expiry drop cannot begin a breach at t≈30. Those FAILs are the campaign's separate, still-unexplained "csip-event-delay intermittent unseat" (QA_CAMPAIGN_FINDINGS.md FINDING #2), a different bug. (c) The bench-harm illustration is non-binding on this bench: default = 5 kW export cap but pvHighW=4800 W, load=250 W (mayhem.go:2675/2832) → unconstrained export ≈ 4550 W < 5 kW, so even a correct default fallback would curtail nothing there. Net: the finding stands as a LATENT design/conformance gap (high is defensible for real sites whose default is more restrictive than plant capability, e.g. CSIP-AUS export limits), but it is not demonstrated by any logged bench run, and its cited empirical evidence attributes the wrong root cause to the event-delay FAILs. The proposed fix and test are otherwise reasonable; the hub already handles Source="default"/ValidUntil=0 controls, so the fallback path composes with existing expiry logic.

### CS-1 [high/bug/confidence=high] — **verifier: CONFIRMED**
**TASK-037 residual gap: utility-time anchor is composed from clock reads taken at different instants, so a local wall step landing mid-walk (or mid-rewalk-republish) displaces utility time by the full step for one discovery interval**

**Evidence:** walker.go:233, publish.go:330, run.go:360 and 598-601, cmd/hub/state.go:394 and 820 (`state.ClockOffset = serverNow - now.Unix()`), engine.go:983-984 — all read in full. Observed FAIL (csip-tls-test logs/qa/qa-mayhem-20260716-084620.md:143-148): breach t=82–86s (5 samples ≈ one FAST discovery interval + ticks, first 1230W, peak 3600W) shortly after the −3600 restore step at tick 55, with cannot_comply=true and final plan `[csip/export-limit] holding generation ≤ 0W` — control ACTIVE throughout, battery=1630W discharge commanded — consistent with a backward-poisoned anchor flipping the plan slot, not an unseat. mayhem_world.go:1497-1537 confirms +3600 at tick 15, −3600 at tick 55.

**Root cause:** The anchor value is wall_now + offset with the two terms measured at different times: (a) walker.go:233 `tree.ClockOffset = tm.CurrentTime - time.Now().Unix()` at /tm parse; (b) publish.go:330 `Ts: time.Now().Unix()` at publish, ~0.2–2s later; (c) run.go:360 `d.clk.Anchor(utilitytime.ServerNowAt(time.Now(), tree.ClockOffset))` also at walk end; (d) run.go:598-601 rewalk republish pairs `refreshed.Ts = now.Unix()` with the CACHED message's old ClockOffset. A ±3600s local step landing between the offset measurement and the Ts/anchor stamp yields anchorServer = server ± 3600. The hub then anchors to that via state.go:394 `r.utclk.Anchor(msg.Ts + msg.ClockOffset)` and every serverNow reader is off by the step until the next coherent control message (~5s FAST, 20–60s STOCK). TASK-037's monotonic anchoring protects BETWEEN observations but is re-poisoned by the incoherent observation itself. Downstream: hub control-expiry is debounce-protected (rides out the ~5s excursion), but daily-plan slot selection has NO debounce — engine.go:983-984 `serverTime := state.Timestamp.Add(...ClockOffset...); state.DailyPlanTarget = dp.CurrentTarget(serverTime)` jumps ±1h and can select an interval whose BattSetpointW commands discharge under an active 0W export cap; TOU evaluation shifts identically. Straddle probability per step ≈ (offset→publish latency)/(discovery interval) ≈ 10–30% — matching the scenario's intermittency (INCONCLUSIVE→FAIL→PASS across cycles).

**Proposed fix:** Make the composition atomic: capture ONE time.Time (monotonic reading intact) at the /tm parse; derive both the published timestamp and the anchor from it — e.g. walker stores tmParsedAt; run.go anchors with `tm.CurrentTime + int64(time.Since(tmParsedAt).Seconds())`; publish a single server_ts field (server time at publish, computed the same way) that the hub anchors on directly instead of adding two independently-clocked fields; the rewalk republish must recompute server_ts from d.clk.ServerNow(), never fresh-wall+stale-offset. Tests: utilitytime/run tests with an injected Now stepping between the /tm capture and the publish stamp, asserting the anchor (and the hub's re-anchor from the message) is unchanged; hub test asserting CurrentTarget's interval index is stable across a ±3600 step injected between two control arrivals.

**Blast radius:** Every ServerNow consumer for one refresh interval after any NTP/RTC step that lands mid-walk: plan-follow dispatch, TOU pricing, northbound scheduler (CS-2), responses CreatedDateTime. At STOCK cadence the poisoned window is 20–60s. NTP steps at commissioning are a certainty, not an edge case (GAP-04's own motivation).

**Verifier reasoning:** Every cited code site verified by direct read: walker.go:233 measures ClockOffset against time.Now() at /tm parse (walk step 2); publish.go:325-331 stamps Ts with a second, later time.Now() at publish; run.go:360 anchors northbound's clock with a third read at walk end (and run.go:428 builds the published 24h schedule from that possibly-poisoned serverNow); run.go:598-601 rewalk republish pairs refreshed.Ts=now.Unix() with the CACHED message's pre-step ClockOffset. cmd/hub/state.go:394 (`r.utclk.Anchor(msg.Ts + msg.ClockOffset)`) is the hub's ONLY Anchor site and utilitytime.go:285-292 Anchor accepts unconditionally — so one incoherent observation re-poisons TASK-037's monotonic protection exactly as claimed; state.go:430's staleness check reduces to now−Ts (offsets cancel) and cannot detect the poison. Downstream sites verified: engine.go:983-984 CurrentTarget has no debounce; optimizer.go:488 TOU shifts identically; expiry debounce at state.go:736-738/63. Bench evidence verified: mayhem_world.go:1497-1537 steps the hub's OWN clock via SSH (+3600 tick 15, −3600 tick 55); qa-mayhem-20260716-084620.md shows the FAIL (breach t=82-86s, first 1230W over a 0W cap, control still ACTIVE, plan-follow battery=1630W discharge — not an unseat); 4 sibling runs that night PASSed, confirming the claimed intermittency consistent with a straddle-probability mechanism (FAST = engine 3s/discovery 5s per hub-replay-tune.sh). The proposed atomic-composition fix (one captured monotonic instant at /tm parse driving Ts, anchor, and the rewalk republish recomputed from d.clk.ServerNow()) is correct and also covers the poisoned schedule.Build/Pricing path.

**Verifier corrections:** Two refinements, neither invalidating the root cause: (1) The claim "hub control-expiry is debounce-protected (rides out the ~5s excursion)" is true only at FAST cadence. At product STOCK cadence, state.go:63 expiryConfirmWindowS=9.0 with confirmTicksFor(15s engine interval)=ceil(9/15)=1 tick, while the poison window is up to one 20s discovery interval — so a forward-poisoned anchor CAN expire-and-drop a still-valid control (any control with <1h residual validity) for ~one discovery interval on a real site. The product-default exposure is worse than the finding states, and the fix's tests should cover it. (2) The observed 27-31s step-to-breach latency is not fully explained by the ≤5s poisoned-anchor window plus an instantaneous CurrentTarget slot flip. The more persistent path: engine.go:631 replan() / engine.go:712 (now = state.Timestamp + ClockOffset; WindowStart = now.Unix()) — the planner wakes on every SetPrices/SetDERConstraints (fed by every ~5s bench walk's Pricing/Schedule publishes), so a replan landing inside the poisoned window rebuilds the ENTIRE 24h plan with WindowStart displaced ±3600s, and that misbuilt plan persists past the anchor's self-heal until the next replan; combined with battery ramp latency this matches the late, sustained breach better. Same root cause, same fix — but regression tests should also assert plan WindowStart stability (a replan fired during the poisoned window), not only CurrentTarget's interval index across two control arrivals.

### CS-2 [high/bug/confidence=high]
**Northbound scheduler expiry is instantaneous and its clock-step guard is backward-only: one forward-poisoned serverNow unseats an active event to the DEFAULT**

**Evidence:** scheduler.go:318-324: `if resolved.Source == "default" && s.lastGood != nil && s.lastGood.Source == "event" && !controlExpired(s.lastGood, serverNow) && stillServed(hp, s.lastGood.MRID)` — the `!controlExpired` term disarms the hold exactly when a forward step fires; scheduler.go:398-400 `return utilitytime.Expired(ac.ValidUntil, serverNow)` (no debounce anywhere in Evaluate). Contrast cmd/hub/state.go:63 `expiryConfirmWindowS = 9.0` + utilitytime.DebouncedExpiry (expiry.go:23-50).

**Root cause:** scheduler.failClosed's clock-regression guards (scheduler.go:318-324 default-fallback half, :363-381 nil half) hold last-known-good only while the event is unexpired: `!controlExpired(s.lastGood, serverNow) && stillServed(...)`. controlExpired (scheduler.go:398-400) is an instantaneous `serverNow >= ValidUntil` with no debounce. A single Evaluate whose serverNow stepped FORWARD past the event's end (CS-1's poisoned anchor, or a genuine server-clock excursion) reads the still-served event as expired, so resolve() falls back to DefaultDERControl and failClosed ADOPTS it and overwrites lastGood (scheduler.go:325-327 `stored := *resolved; s.lastGood = &stored`) — the 0W cap is replaced by the permissive default on the retained topic and the hub un-curtails. It self-heals on the next walk whose offset re-measures (~5s FAST, up to 60s+ STOCK), matching the reported 'brief ~10s unseat'. The hub side has DebouncedExpiry (AD-004, expiryConfirmWindowS=9s) for exactly this fault class; the northbound scheduler never got the equivalent, and the guard comments (:364-373) show only the backward direction ('the server's clock stepped back past its start') was ever considered — local-clock-step-back PASSes, forward FAILs intermittently.

**Proposed fix:** Symmetric, debounced hold: in failClosed, when the freshly-resolved source is 'default' (or nil) while lastGood is a still-served event that flipped to expired in a single cycle (or when the walk's clk.SetOffset/LocalStep classified a Step), hold the event for one confirm cycle — give the scheduler a DebouncedExpiry keyed on consecutive walks, mirroring the hub's expiryConfirmWindowS rationale. A genuinely-ended event still releases on the next confirming walk. Tests: scheduler table test — Evaluate(programs, serverNow+3600) once → expect Held event, not default; twice consecutively → default; extend utilitytime_equiv/failclosed tests with a forward-step row.

**Blast radius:** Real commissioning scenario: the first NTP sync after install steps the SOM clock; if it lands mid-walk, an active utility curtailment is replaced by the default for up to one discovery interval (60s STOCK) while PV exports — wrong control behavior possible on a real site — plus a spurious event-transition Response POSTed to the server (lastGood identity churn feeds responses.Tracker).

### ED-2 [medium/bug/confidence=high]
**doGet's unconditional same-path retry doubles the walk-loop blackout under a per-resource stall (30s per failed walk)**

**Evidence:** fetcher.go:163-175 (quoted retry block); internal/tlsclient/config.go:19 `DefaultReadTimeout = 15 * time.Second`; run.go:219-265 single-goroutine Loop (rewalk pokes coalesce into the same goroutine, so a wedged RunOnce delays everything, including TASK-042 rewalks).

**Root cause:** internal/tlsclient/fetcher.go:159-175: on any Get error doGet does `f.client.Close(); f.client.Dial(); raw, err = f.client.Get(path)` — the retry-once exists for stale keep-alive connections, but it also fires on a READ TIMEOUT, where an immediate same-path retry is near-certain to hit the same stall. Under the 20s/GET delay each walk burns 2×15s = 30s in the single-flight walk goroutine (run.go Loop is the only RunOnce caller), so northbound is blind ~35s per cycle instead of ~20s — precisely what kept the loop occupied through the inter-run recovery hole in ED-1, and what stretches control-adoption latency during any real head-end brownout.

**Proposed fix:** Distinguish error classes in doGet: retry once only when the failure smells like a dead keep-alive (write error / immediate EOF / connection reset), not when the first attempt was on a fresh dial or the error is a read timeout (SO_RCVTIMEO). Alternatively cap total per-logical-request time. Test: fake server stalling > ReadTimeout; assert one attempt and ~15s elapsed; assert a genuine half-closed keep-alive still gets its retry.

**Blast radius:** Northbound control-refresh latency during partial outages; at STOCK (60s interval) a slow resource still costs 30s of loop occupancy per walk.

### CS-3 [medium/process/confidence=medium]
**QA report mislabels the clock-step breach as an 'unseat'; its own evidence shows a plan-follow discharge over a still-active cap (e0864c9 headroom trusting commanded EV draw is a co-suspect)**

**Evidence:** csip-tls-test logs/qa/qa-mayhem-20260716-084620.md:143-148 (quoted); scratchpad QA_CAMPAIGN_FINDINGS.md FINDING #6; lexa-hub commit e0864c9 'cap plan-followed discharge under an active export limit'; engine.go:983-984 slot selection; optimizer.go:436 applyPlanRule with planDischargeCapW.

**Root cause:** The session report (QA_SESSION_REPORT finding D / campaign FINDING #6) says 'brief 10s/1230W unseat + an unnecessary CannotComply … residual gap in TASK-037 anchoring during re-anchor' without hub journals. Its own artifact contradicts 'unseat': cannot_comply=true requires an ACTIVE control (breach episodes only exist with one), and the final plan line shows '[plan/export-cap] plan discharge 5000W would export past the active limit→capped to 1630W (export headroom) | … battery=1630W ev=12.0A | [csip/export-limit] holding generation ≤ 0W' — the export cap was adopted and enforced end-to-end; the 1230–3600W export at t=82–86 came from plan-followed BATTERY discharge (solar pinned at 0W). Root-cause candidates, in order: (a) CS-1's backward-poisoned anchor flipping CurrentTarget to an hour-earlier discharge slot for ~one walk interval (duration fits); (b) the e0864c9 discharge-headroom cap counting the EV's COMMANDED 12A (~2.8kW) as guaranteed local consumption — if actual EV draw dips, discharging 1630W exports ~1380W ≈ the observed 1230W. Distinguishing them needs the hub journal (which decision fired at t=82), which was not captured. Also note the mis-attribution in the report's fix-hint ('expiryConfirmTicks / freshness anchoring' — the hub-side debounce, which is actually fine).

**Proposed fix:** On the next repro capture the hub journal + lexa/hub/plan history across the step (decision tags distinguish slot-flip vs EV-dip immediately). Product hardening regardless: compute plan-follow discharge headroom from MEASURED EV draw (state.EVSEs power) rather than the commanded setpoint, or clamp to metered-export feedback within one tick. Correct the session report's finding-D wording (no unseat occurred in that run).

**Blast radius:** Mis-triage of finding D; and the headroom-vs-measured-EV-draw assumption stands alone as a small export-cap leak on any EV pause under plan-follow.

### CS-4 [low/bug/confidence=high]
**onCSIPControl's stale-at-adoption age check is raw wall-clock arithmetic; a forward local step causes a spurious stale-suspect WARN + rewalk request**

**Evidence:** state.go:427-437 (quoted); rewalkRateLimit=10s (state.go:248); nbRewalkRateLimit=10s (run.go:556).

**Root cause:** cmd/hub/state.go:430 computes `age := utilitytime.ServerNowAt(time.Now(), msg.ClockOffset) - (msg.Ts + msg.ClockOffset)`, which reduces to now.Unix() − msg.Ts — pure wall difference. A +3600s local step occurring between a message's stamping and its adoption (e.g. a retained redelivery right after an NTP step) reads age > retained_adoption_max_age_s (300, configs/hub.json:99) and fires the stale-suspect WARN + rewalk even though the control is seconds old. Enforcement is unaffected (enforce-but-verify; both sides rate-limit rewalks at 10s), but it adds alarm noise in exactly the NTP-step window where operators are already confused by journald timestamp jumps.

**Proposed fix:** Rides for free on CS-1's fix: with a single server_ts field on the message, compute age against the anchored clock (utclk.ServerNow() − server_ts), which is step-immune; or gate the stale-suspect path on r.utclk.LocalStep() not currently reporting a step. Test: adopt a fresh retained message with an injected +3600 wall step between stamp and adoption; assert no rewalk fires.

**Blast radius:** One spurious WARN + one rewalk round-trip per local step; no control impact.

### OK-1 [info/ok-verified/confidence=high]
**Fail-closed walk discipline, walker atomicity, fetcher timeout hygiene, hub-side TASK-037 anchoring between arrivals, and the backward-step guard verified correct**

**Evidence:** (1) run.go:309-327: a walk error publishes NOTHING and holds last-published; no code path publishes 'none'/'default' on failure. (2) walker.go:203-341: every required sub-resource fetch failure aborts the whole walk, so a partial tree can never resolve the default and unseat an event. (3) fetcher.go:163-175 + client.go:142-161: read timeout is SO_RCVTIMEO on the wolfSSL fd; every error path Closes the session before redial, so a delayed response can never desynchronize keep-alive request/response pairing. (4) cmd/hub/state.go:736-756 + internal/utilitytime/utilitytime.go:253-292: expiry is evaluated on the monotonic-anchored Clock and debounced (confirmTicksFor floors at 2 ticks), and freshness windows are time.Now()+Sub monotonic — a local step BETWEEN control arrivals cannot expire or stale anything (the clock-step FAIL run's clean samples t=15–82 confirm this live). (5) scheduler.go:363-381 backward-step guard works (local-clock-step-back PASSes consistently). The only gaps found are the observation-composition window (CS-1) and the forward-step asymmetry (CS-2).

**Root cause:** n/a — verification result.

**Proposed fix:** n/a

**Blast radius:** n/a
