## Probe: finding-D-churn-dither-malform

**Probe summary:** Probe: root-cause three finding-D failures (control-churn silent breach, export-dither-at-breach CannotComply, malform-huge-activepower unseat) from the 2026-07-16 QA session. I read internal/orchestrator/optimizer.go (applyExportLimitRule, checkExportLimitConvergence, expGuard/expOverTicks), orchestrator/constraint/export.go (the shadow port), cmd/hub/state.go (onCSIPControl adoption + expiry debounce), internal/northbound/scheduler/scheduler.go (Evaluate/failClosed/plausibleControl), internal/northbound/run/run.go (per-walk publish), the bench's scenario/oracle code (csip-tls-test cmd/dashboard/mayhem*.go, sim/gridsim/malform.go, admin.go), and the raw soak logs + bench-health logs in the prior session's scratchpad. Verdicts: (1) control-churn — the QA report's hypothesis is WRONG at the counter level (expOverTicks deliberately survives mRID/value churn since c47b516; verified) but RIGHT one layer down: the ceiling controller (expGuard, incl. solarCeilingW and filteredExportW) is fully reset on every cap VALUE change, re-running "first-tick one-step correction" logic against a lagged meter with the up-slew limiter bypassed (prevCeiling NaN), so every 0↔500 W supersession pays a fresh multi-second over-cap transient; the counter never trips because samples in the ±100 W band and the alternating looser phase decrement it, and any walk that lands in the delete→replace gap adopts the bench default/none instantly (no release debounce) and zeroes the counter. (2) export-dither — the leaky expOverTicks counter IS hold-biased (verified, 3/4 five-minute soaks clean); the FAIL's spurious CannotComply almost certainly comes from the OTHER, undebounced breach emitter at optimizer.go:1448 (single-tick zero-lever trip, easily armed under a 0 W cap where the ceiling naturally sits near the 100 W trip region). (3) malform-huge — the plausibility gate + last-known-good hold exist, are correct, and are tested (32767e9 W > maxPlausibleLimitW=1e9 → rejected, held, metric + Table-27 reject posted); the single cycle-4 FAIL is not explained by the adoption code, bench-health shows sims healthy during the run, and the harness has a verified arming race (armAfterCapAdopted matches type+limit only, never mRID, while consecutive malform scenarios all post identical 0 W caps) plus an oracle that never checks which control the hub actually held — classify as test-infra/oracle gap requiring an instrumented repro, not a confirmed hub bug.

### D1-churn-controller-reset [high/bug/confidence=high] — **verifier: PARTLY**
**control-churn: expGuard full reset on every cap VALUE change re-runs onset logic against a lagged meter — multi-second over-cap transient per supersession, silent (no CannotComply)**

**Evidence:** optimizer.go:954-957: `// New limit value → start the guard fresh. if limits.exportLimitW != o.expGuard.activeLimitW { o.expGuard = exportGuard{... filteredExportW: math.NaN(), solarCeilingW: math.NaN()} }` — the reset discards the converged solar ceiling and the low-pass export filter, which are PLANT state, not per-cap state. optimizer.go:1333-1334: on NaN prevCeiling the controller takes a "full one-step correction" `desiredCeilingW = totalSolarW + (conservativeW - effectiveExportW)` that trusts the current meter sample, and optimizer.go:1353 `if !math.IsNaN(prevCeilingW)` skips the ~166 W/s up-slew limiter entirely on that first tick — so a 0→500 W supersession can jump the ceiling in one tick against a 1-2-tick-lagged meter and overshoot (run qa-run-12-aa.log: 9 violation samples t=44-72s, first over the looser 500 W judge line by only 50 W — controller settling above the cap after mid-window flips, 16 s cumulative; even PASS runs show 4-7 s out-of-limit per run). Why silent: checkExportLimitConvergence (optimizer.go:1511) only counts samples over cap+complianceBreachW (100 W, optimizer.go:2449) against the CURRENT cap — 550 W during a 500 W phase is inside the band, and during the alternating looser/default phases the leaky counter DECREMENTS (optimizer.go:1515-1516), so accumulation never reaches scaleTicks(exportBreachTicks)=3. Verified the mRID itself resets nothing (reset keys on value only) — the QA report's "new mRID = new guard session" hypothesis is refuted at the counter and correct only for the controller.

**Root cause:** Controller session state (solar ceiling, export filter, safeCount) is keyed to the cap VALUE instead of to the physical export axis; a supersession with a different value is treated as a brand-new episode, so onset heuristics (one-step correction, slew bypass, filter reseed) re-run against measurements still reflecting the previous phase.

**Proposed fix:** Persist plant-continuous state across cap value changes: keep expGuard.filteredExportW and solarCeilingW (and battStallTicks) on a value change, recompute only conservativeW/targets; reserve the full reset for the NaN→value (new episode) edge. The existing maxDropW/maxRiseW slew then handles both tighten and relax correctly. Apply the identical change to the shadow port (constraint/export_session.go resetControllerForNewLimit; export.go:122-126 keeps the two cadences mirrored — parity must be preserved or the shadow-diff gate fires). Tests: optimizer unit test flipping exportLimitW 0↔500 every 4 ticks with a 1-tick-lagged netW model, asserting (a) ceiling continuity (no one-tick jump > maxRiseW) and (b) no sample over looser-cap+band after initial convergence; port-parity test in constraint/.

**Blast radius:** Any real utility that supersedes/rewrites export caps during a volatile event (the exact CSIP delete-and-replace pattern) gets a multi-second export breach after every rewrite, with no CannotComply admission — INV-EXPORT violation on a real site, silent to the grid operator.

**Verifier reasoning:** EVERY code/log citation in the finding is accurate (verified by direct read): (1) optimizer.go:955-957 does a FULL expGuard reset keyed on `limits.exportLimitW != o.expGuard.activeLimitW` (value, not mRID), discarding filteredExportW, solarCeilingW, batteryAbsorbW, evSetpointA/evCmdW, safeCount, battStallTicks; (2) optimizer.go:1333-1336 takes the full one-step correction `desiredCeilingW = totalSolarW + (conservativeW - effectiveExportW)` on NaN prevCeiling and optimizer.go:1353 (`if !math.IsNaN(prevCeilingW)`) skips the slew limiter on that tick — the comment at 1349-1350 says this bypass is deliberate; (3) checkExportLimitConvergence (optimizer.go:1494-1531) only increments when `exportW > exportLimitW+complianceBreachW` (100 W, :2449) against the CURRENT cap, decrements leakily (:1515-1516), threshold scaleTicks(3) (:1468,1510); (4) expOverTicks deliberately survives value changes (field comment :170-180) — the finding's refutation of the QA report's "new mRID = new guard session" counter hypothesis is correct; (5) the shadow port mirrors the same value-keyed reset (constraint/export.go:124-126 → export_session.go:67-69); (6) qa-run-12-aa.log lines 90-99 confirm FAIL: 9 INV-EXPORT samples t=44-72s, first +50 W over 500 W, 16 s out-of-limit, peak 3900 W, cannot_comply=False; PASS runs (qa-run-02/07/17, mayhem-regression) show 4-7 s out-of-limit each, confirming a per-run silent transient. So the finding is REAL as a phenomenon and the small (+50 W-class) settling samples are consistent with its mechanism.

HOWEVER the root-cause attribution is quantitatively wrong for the FAIL-driving excursions. The scenario pins the battery at SOC 100% (mayhem_world.go:1088 `SoC_pct: 100`), killing the absorb lever (optimizer.go:1089 skips at socFull), and uses pvHighW=4800 (mayhem.go:2675) / loadLow=250 (mayhem_world.go:930). Peak "3900 W over 500" = export ≈ 4400 W ≈ FULL UNCURTAILED PV export (4800-250); run-07's 8900 over = export ≈ 9400 ≈ full PV PLUS ~full 5 kW battery discharge. From a converged operating point under either churn phase (gen ≈ 250-650 W, export ≈ 0-400 W), the one-step correction's error is bounded by the meter-staleness delta (a few hundred W) — it computes ceiling = gen + (conservative − export) and structurally cannot command a ~4.5 kW ceiling; and SolarCommands are re-issued every tick a cap is active (optimizer.go:1419-1441, sticky). Reaching full-nameplate output therefore requires ticks where the hub held NO export cap at all: optimizer.go:949-951 clears the guard on NaN and the restore rule un-curtails, the plan/TOU discharge is then legitimately uncapped (which is why commit e0864c9, 2026-07-15 20:46, 'cap plan-followed discharge under an ACTIVE export limit', did not stop run-07's 8900 W at 05:38 next morning), and — the stronger silence mechanism the finding missed — optimizer.go:1496 zeroes expOverTicks on any NaN-cap tick, wiping accumulation across every gap. The scenario is delete-and-replace every 12 s (mayhem_world.go:1098-1106: deleteControls then postCap), and its own Fix text names exactly this mode: "without dropping to no-control between replacements". The dominant defect is therefore in the adoption/scheduler turnover (a transient no-control publish between delete and replace), with the controller-reset transient as a real but secondary (+50 W-class, few-second) contributor. This gap attribution is inferred from magnitudes + code (no hub journal was captured for the churn runs), whereas the reset-transient mechanics are verified in code.

On the proposed fix: persisting filteredExportW/solarCeilingW across value changes is reasonable and the tighten edge stays fast (I initially suspected it would slow cap defence, but the feed-forward bound at optimizer.go:1399-1402 drops by the cap delta in one tick and deliberately bypasses the down-slew, so a tighten still curtails in ~1 tick); the parity requirement with constraint/export_session.go is correctly stated. But the fix is incomplete: (a) it leaves batteryAbsorbW/evCmdW/evSetpointA resetting, re-exposing the commanded-vs-measured conservation-identity hazard the code itself documents at optimizer.go:1028-1049 (identity falls back to measured values that are only consistent in pre-event steady state — mid-episode OCPP lags ~10 s, the documented "multi-kW import" failure); those command echoes are plant-continuous too; (b) it would NOT flip run-12-class FAILs, because it touches neither the no-control window during supersession turnover nor the expOverTicks wipe at :1496.

**Verifier corrections:** Recharacterize: two co-existing defects, not one. (1) SECONDARY (the finding's mechanism, verified in code): the value-keyed full expGuard reset (optimizer.go:955-957) re-runs onset heuristics (one-step correction :1334, slew bypass :1353, filter reseed :991-992, ratchet loss :1115) against a 1-2-tick-lagged meter on every supersession — explains the small (+50 W-class) settling violations and can prolong an excursion via the nameplate clamp (:1420-1423) when gen is high and the meter stale. Fix as proposed, but persist ALL plant-continuous state including batteryAbsorbW/evCmdW/evSetpointA (not just filteredExportW/solarCeilingW/battStallTicks), or the identity fallback at :1042-1049 regresses to the documented multi-kW-import hazard; mirror in constraint/export_session.go. (2) PRIMARY (inferred from log magnitudes + code, needs a hub-journal/mqtt capture to confirm): during delete-and-replace turnover the hub transiently holds NO export cap — full-restore-magnitude peaks (3900 W over = uncurtailed pvHighW 4800 − loadLow 250; 8900 W over = that plus ~full battery discharge, uncapped because e0864c9 only binds under an ACTIVE limit) and expOverTicks zeroed at optimizer.go:1496 on the NaN tick (the real reason CannotComply never fires — stronger than the band/leaky-decrement argument). Fix direction: debounce/hold the compliance session and last-good cap across a brief no-control window during rapid supersession (northbound scheduler / hub adoption path), and make expOverTicks survive a short NaN gap rather than clearing instantly — while still releasing on a genuine sustained removal. Repro/verify: capture lexa/csip/control + lexa/desired/solar/+ during the churn window and look for a no-cap or restore publish between replacements.

### D3-dither-zerolever-undebounced [high/bug/confidence=medium] — **verifier: CONFIRMED**
**export-dither-at-breach: the spurious CannotComply comes from the UNdebounced zero-lever breach path (optimizer.go:1448), not from expOverTicks — single-tick trip with no hysteresis**

**Evidence:** optimizer.go:1448-1456: `if actualExportW > limits.exportLimitW+complianceBreachW && desiredCeilingW <= complianceBreachW { o.recordBreach(...) }` — fires on ONE tick, no counter, no re-arm hysteresis. Under a 0 W cap the converged ceiling ≈ home load (~250 W), and a lagged ~150 W meter excursion drives the integrator down 0.5×error/tick (optimizer.go:1330-1336) to ≤100 W in 2-3 ticks while the meter still reads over — both trip conditions coincide. Run evidence (qa-run-18-ab.log, cycle 4): FAIL with cannot_comply=True, total excursion only 5 s / 150 W peak at t=293-297 of a 303 s dither soak, INV-HUNT clean. Arithmetic excludes the debounced counter as the emitter: 5 s at the FAST 3 s tick is ≤2 over-band engine ticks, below threshold scaleTicks(exportBreachTicks)=3 (optimizer.go:1468, 285-295; bench FAST engine_interval_s=3 per csip-tls-test scripts/hub-replay-tune.sh:8), and with 0 prior over-band samples in 300 s there was no residual accumulation. The counter itself is verified hold-biased: leaky ±1, capped at threshold, decrement-not-zero on an in-band sample (optimizer.go:1511-1517) — 3 of 4 five-minute dither soaks passed with peak 0 W (qa-run-03/08/13-ab.log). Confidence medium only because the emitting call site isn't provable from the captured logs (no hub journal); the timing/threshold arithmetic makes :1448 the only consistent emitter. Failure shape on a real site: a 5 s meter/PV noise excursion under a long-held 0 W cap posts a CannotComply for a condition that self-corrects within one control interval.

**Root cause:** Two breach emitters share the export axis: the convergence backstop is properly debounced/leaky, but the 'last lever exhausted' immediate path was left single-sample — and a 0 W cap parks the system permanently adjacent to its trip region (ceiling ≈ load; band = 100 W).

**Proposed fix:** Debounce the zero-lever path with the same leaky pattern: only recordBreach at :1448 after the condition persists scaleTicks(exportBreachTicks) ticks (or feed it into expOverTicks with a 2x-weight increment so a genuine no-lever episode still escalates fast), and add re-arm hysteresis (trip at cap+complianceBreachW, re-arm below cap+complianceBreachW/2). Mirror in constraint/export.go's zeroLeverBreach (export.go:128-136). Tests: 1- and 2-tick 150 W excursions under a 0 W cap with ceiling forced ≤100 W must NOT breach; a sustained (≥threshold) one must.

**Blast radius:** Spurious CannotComply POSTs to the grid operator under any tight cap with realistic meter noise (each noise blip is a new episode past the GEN.044 dedupe); also intermittently breaks the bench's dither biconditional oracle.

**Verifier reasoning:** Verified in code and logs. (1) The undebounced zero-lever emitter exists as cited: internal/orchestrator/optimizer.go:1448-1456 `if actualExportW > limits.exportLimitW+complianceBreachW && desiredCeilingW <= complianceBreachW { o.recordBreach(...) }` — single-sample, no counter, no re-arm hysteresis. (2) No downstream damping: cmd/hub/breach.go:30-33 explicitly does no debounce because "both sources already damp onset via the optimizer's expOverTicks counters" — false for this path; OnPlan (breach.go:240-248) + emit (breach.go:292-311) open an episode and emit an Active ComplianceAlert on the FIRST breaching non-safety plan, and each clear/re-trip mints a NEW episodeID (emit's `ev.mrid != b.activeMRID` after a clear), so northbound's per-episode dedupe does not suppress repeat noise trips. Reconciler evidence excluded as emitter (DefaultConvergeTimeout=60s, internal/reconcile/reconcile.go:76, vs a 5 s excursion). (3) Arithmetic exclusion of expOverTicks confirmed: threshold scaleTicks(exportBreachTicks=3)=3 at FAST 3 s (optimizer.go:250,285-295; csip-tls-test scripts/hub-replay-tune.sh:8); qa-run-18-ab.log:112,118 shows the sole excursion was 5 s (t=293-297, 150 W peak) = ≤2 engine ticks after 293 s clean (counter at 0), so the properly leaky counter (optimizer.go:1510-1517) cannot have fired; gen/import emitters not armed; qa-run-03/08/13-ab.log all PASS this scenario. (4) Scenario premise confirmed: mayhem_world.go:930 loadLow=250 W, exportDitherLoadDeltaW=150 (mayhem_world.go:1638), cap 0 ⇒ conservativeW=0 (optimizer.go:967), converged ceiling ≈ load. The trip is actually FASTER than the finding's 2-3-tick integrator estimate: the feed-forward ceiling (optimizer.go:1391-1402, homeSinkW+predictedBatteryAbsorbW+evCmdW+conservativeW, deliberately bypassing the down-slew) drops the ceiling to ≈ load−excursion = 100 W ≤ complianceBreachW on the FIRST over-band tick while actualExportW=150>100 — both conditions coincide immediately. Root cause (two emitters share the axis; only the convergence one is debounced; a 0 W cap parks ceiling≈load adjacent to the 100 W trip band) is correct; proposed fix (debounce :1448 with scaleTicks(exportBreachTicks) + hysteresis, mirror in constraint/export.go) is sound — checkExportLimitConvergence stays as the independent ~9 s backstop and the plan.Breach==nil guard at optimizer.go:1518 prevents duplication.

**Verifier corrections:** Two refinements, neither changing the verdict: (a) Mechanism — the dominant single-tick trip path is the feed-forward ceiling bound at optimizer.go:1391-1402 (bypasses the down-slew; ceiling → homeSinkW≈load−excursion≈100 W in ONE tick), not only the 0.5-gain integrator at :1330-1336 (which needs ~2 ticks at 75 W/step from 250 W); any fix must debounce the breach CHECK at :1448, not just slow the ceiling controller. (b) Line cite — constraint/export.go's mirrored single-sample condition is at export.go:436-450 (inside applyExportControl's return), not :128-136 (that is the zeroLeverBreach-vs-convBreach merge site in Evaluate). Also note the original finding's "confidence medium (no hub journal)" caveat can be upgraded: reconciler (60 s ConvergeTimeout) and gen/import emitters are positively excluded, leaving :1448 as the only possible emitter, and the feed-forward arithmetic reproduces the observed ≤2-tick trip exactly.

### D5-malform-harness-race [high/test-blindspot/confidence=medium] — **verifier: PARTLY**
**malform-huge FAIL (run 19, cycle 4) is unexplained by hub code; the harness has a verified arming race (mRID-blind adoption check across scenarios that all post identical 0 W caps) and the oracle cannot distinguish 'cap unseated' from 'cap held but lever dead'**

**Evidence:** Harness race (verified in code): mayhem.go:743 arms the malform when `h.ctrlActive && h.ctrlTyp == typ && h.ctrlLimW == limW` — type+limit only, though postCap RETURNS the mRID (mayhem.go:2804-2808) and hubState parses csip_control.mrid (mayhem.go:2555). All five malformScenario instances post identical exportCap 0 W (mayhem.go:1535) and ran consecutively in run 19 (order: malformed-csip → missing-href → empty-program → huge), so a stale hub /status still showing the PREVIOUS scenario's 0 W cap (northbound hasn't re-walked since resetForScenario's deleteControls, mayhem.go:2727-2730) satisfies the arm check immediately — the malform can be served before the scenario's own cap is ever cleanly walked, after which every walk serves only the corrupted control and the scheduler has nothing valid to adopt; hold-vs-release then depends on the previous cap's ValidUntil, i.e. inter-scenario timing drift, matching the cycle-granularity intermittency. Oracle blindspot (verified): diagnoseMalform:1590-1597 explicitly refuses the CannotComply excuse for exportCap ("the hub can always curtail PV") and judges only INV-EXPORT — it never asserts which mRID/limit the hub held at breach time and never gates on the SOLAR sim's health (forceBlindOnConstraintProbeGap:924-933 uses only the constraint's judging meter probe), so an arming-race run and an inverter-actuation blackout produce the same 'malformed resource unseated the safe control' verdict. Counter-evidence against the session report's own late-soak-degradation theory for THIS run: qa-bench-health2.log shows sims=[so=200 ...] at 11:05:50 and 11:10:51, bracketing run 19's malform-huge (~11:05-11:07), and errs=0/75. The run-19 signature (adopted=True reacted=False cannot_comply=True, 'Last hub plan: [plan/follow]', out-of-limit 69 s of ~76 — never enforced at any point) is not explained by any code path I could verify; hub/northbound journals were not captured, so the exact chain is unproven. Inferred, not verified: which of the race vs a real hold-failure occurred in run 19.

**Root cause:** The adoption gate that sequences 'cap adopted, THEN malform' is identity-blind, and the FAIL diagnosis asserts nothing about the hub's held control — so the scenario can neither prove the malform arrived after clean adoption nor prove the hub dropped the cap.

**Proposed fix:** (1) armAfterCapAdopted must match cons.MRID (already returned by postCap and available as hubState.ctrlMRID). (2) diagnoseMalform's FAIL branch should sample hubState at breach time and branch on whether csip_control still shows the scenario's mRID+0 W (held-but-not-actuating → point at southbound/reconciler, not the walker). (3) Capture lexa-northbound journal lines ('holding last-known-good', ImplausibleRejects counter) into the finding. Then re-run malform-huge ~10x; only a FAIL with the cap verifiably held-then-dropped implicates the hub.

**Blast radius:** A SAFETY-class conformance scenario whose FAIL verdict is unreliable in both directions at soak timescales — it escalated a possibly-false finding into the session's punch list, and symmetrically could mask a real unseat behind the excused settling ramp.

**Verifier reasoning:** CONFIRMED (verified in code, all files read): (1) Arming race is real and mRID-blind — csip-tls-test/cmd/dashboard/mayhem.go:743 arms on `h.ctrlActive && h.ctrlTyp == typ && h.ctrlLimW == limW` only, while postCap returns the mRID (mayhem.go:2804-2808) and hubState parses csip_control.mrid (mayhem.go:2555, sampled at 793-794). All five malformScenario variants post identical exportCap 0 W (mayhem.go:1535) via the shared builder (1516-1553); run 19 log confirms consecutive order malformed-csip→missing-href→empty-program→huge (qa-run-19-ac.log:54,66,78,90). The runner calls resetForScenario (deleteControls, mayhem.go:2728-2730) immediately before setup with no settle (mayhem.go:496→511), so a 2 s arm tick can see the previous scenario's stale 0 W cap before the next walk (~5-20 s cadence). (2) Oracle blindspot is real — diagnoseMalform's FAIL branch (mayhem.go:1623-1631) judges only INV-EXPORT, refuses the CannotComply excuse for exportCap (1590-1597), never inspects the per-sample AdoptedMRID/AdoptedLimW (recorded at 793-794 and used by OTHER diagnosers, e.g. mayhem_pagination.go:140 — so the data exists), and forceBlindOnConstraintProbeGap (924-933) guards only the PASS branch (called at 1605, and forceBlindOnProbeGap:909 returns unless verdict==PASS). (3) Hub-side fail-closed behavior is correct as documented: 32767e9 W exceeds maxPlausibleLimitW=1e9 (lexa-hub/internal/northbound/scheduler/scheduler.go:187,449-460) → failClosed holds last-known-good and fires RejectHook (scheduler.go:333-351); the malform preserves the control's own mRID, only replacing OpModExpLimW (csip-tls-test/sim/gridsim/malform.go:130-135). (4) Health-log counter-evidence verified: qa-bench-health2.log line 21 shows sims all 200 at 11:05:50.

CORRECTIONS — the root-cause narrative for run 19 is incomplete/partly wrong on three points: (a) The finding's race timeline (stale-status early-fire → hold-vs-release keyed to the PREVIOUS cap's ValidUntil) does not reproduce run 19's observed signature. The previous cap is the SAME 0 W export limit, so any window where the scheduler holds it (failClosed scheduler.go:343-347) the hub enforces 0 W and the oracle sees no breach — yet run 19 shows raw breach ~69 s of 76 starting ~t=7 with reacted=False and 'Last hub plan: [plan/follow]' (qa-run-19-ac.log:90-99), i.e. NO 0 W cap in force essentially ever; that requires the previous cap already expired at window start (needs ≥~148 s inter-scenario elapsed vs a nominal ~85-100 s — possible only under severe late-soak stretch). (b) The finding missed the bigger arming defect: armAfterCapAdopted's 60 s maxWait deadline fires fn() UNCONDITIONALLY (mayhem.go:736-740), so the malform is served even when the scenario's cap was NEVER adopted — a better fit for run 19 (hub never adopts the new 0 W cap for 60+ s [itself the real unexplained anomaly — possibly a genuine hub adoption-latency defect, possibly bench degradation; hub journals absent], breach begins at PV ramp t≈7 long before the malform arms at t=60, then the deadline-armed malform makes every subsequent walk unadoptable and the verdict blames the malform for a pre-existing breach). (c) cannot_comply=True is presented as part of an 'unexplained signature' but is fully explained and carries zero signal: the hub's WP-7 implausible-reject posts a Table 27 status-253 Response for the scenario's own mRID (scheduler.go:340-342), and gridsim classifies 253 as a CannotComply alert (sim/gridsim/server.go:1089-1099, recorded 1043-1054) — all three PASSING malform-huge runs (qa-run-04/09/14-ac.log:92) also show cannot_comply=True. (d) Additional blindspot the finding missed: scanSamples' adopted counter checks typ only, not limW (mayhem.go:984), so the ever-present 5 kW program-0 DEFAULT export cap satisfies adopted=True — the reported 'adopted=True' cannot distinguish the scenario's 0 W cap from the bench default. Re-run evidence: run 20 was aborted after 2 scenarios (qa-run-20-ac.log) — malform-huge never re-ran; gridsim.log in the scratchpad is a stale 15-line July-15 startup log, no runtime evidence; no hub/northbound journals captured, so the exact run-19 chain remains unproven (agreeing with the finding's own admission). The session report's classification of malform-huge under 'Finding D boundary-dither/hunt class — hub guards chatter at decision boundaries' (QA_SESSION_REPORT_2026-07-16.md:47,227) is unsupported: nothing in the run-19 evidence shows hunting; the harness cannot certify either a hub defect or its absence here.

**Verifier corrections:** The finding's severity/kind (high, test-blindspot) stand, but the root cause must be broadened: the 'cap adopted, THEN malform' sequencing is broken by TWO paths, not one — (1) the mRID-blind early-fire race (mayhem.go:743, as claimed), and (2) the 60 s maxWait deadline fallback (mayhem.go:736-740) that arms the malform unconditionally even when the cap was never adopted; path (2), not (1), best fits run 19's never-enforced-from-t≈7 signature, because under path (1) the held previous cap enforces the identical 0 W limit and would mask the breach, not cause it. The proposed fix is right-direction but incomplete: (a) match cons.MRID in the arm check (data already available); (b) ALSO change the deadline fallback to mark the scenario INCONCLUSIVE ('cap never adopted within 60 s — adoption failure, not a malform-containment result') instead of firing the malform; (c) diagnoseMalform's FAIL branch should branch on the per-sample AdoptedMRID/AdoptedLimW already recorded (mayhem.go:793-794) — no new probe needed — distinguishing cap-never-adopted / default-held / scenario-cap-held-but-not-actuated; (d) fix or annotate scanSamples' limW-blind adopted metric (mayhem.go:984) and stop treating cannot_comply=True as breach evidence in malform scenarios (it is the expected WP-7 253 reject receipt, present on every PASS); (e) capture lexa-northbound journals (implausible-limit reject lines, lexa_nb_implausible_rejects_total, adoption timestamps) — required to determine whether run 19's 60+ s failure to adopt a freshly posted control is a real hub defect or bench degradation; that adoption gap, not 'unseating', is the open hub-side question.

### D2-churn-release-undebounced [medium/design-flaw/confidence=high]
**control-churn: an arriving 'none'/default control unseats the cap instantly and zeroes the breach counter — no release-side counterpart to the 9 s expiry debounce**

**Evidence:** cmd/hub/state.go:381-384: onCSIPControl unconditionally replaces the held control (`prev := r.lastCSIP; r.lastCSIP = &msg`) — no debounce for a release/looser message, while EXPIRY is debounced 9 s (state.go:63 expiryConfirmWindowS, utilitytime.DebouncedExpiry at state.go:737-756). optimizer.go:1495-1497: `if math.IsNaN(exportLimitW) { o.expOverTicks = 0 }` — one NaN tick wipes the whole compliance accumulation. Northbound side: run/run.go:399+415-416 publishes ToActiveControl(active) on EVERY walk, and scheduler.go:363-379 releases (explicit clear) or adopts the bench default the moment a walk sees the deleted event gone (stillServed=false is correct for genuine withdrawal, scheduler.go:374), so a FAST 5 s-cadence walk landing in gridsim's delete→re-post gap (mayhem_world.go:1097-1104: deleteControls then postCap, two sequential HTTP calls) publishes default/none, the hub adopts it that tick, the export rule releases/relaxes, and the counter restarts from zero when the replacement cap arrives.

**Root cause:** Asymmetric debouncing: expiry-by-clock is confirmed over 9 s, but release-by-message (Source flip to none/default, or a looser value) is adopted in one tick; the breach counter's only reset condition (limit reads NaN) is likewise un-debounced.

**Proposed fix:** (a) Debounce the counter reset: require confirmTicksFor-style N consecutive NaN ticks before zeroing expOverTicks (mirror the meter-blind hold at optimizer.go:1502-1504). (b) Hub-side release confirm: when an arriving control LOOSENS/clears the export axis while the previous control is unexpired, hold the tighter value for one confirm tick (bounded, e.g. 3-5 s) before adopting the release — sized so curtailment-release scenarios (which pin prompt release) still pass. Tests: expOverTicks survives a 1-tick NaN gap mid-escalation (currently fails); release still completes within the curtailment-release scenario's expected latency.

**Blast radius:** Delete-and-replace churn (or any transient no-control walk) both unseats a safety cap for a walk cycle and destroys the CannotComply escalation evidence — amplifies D1 into the observed fully-silent breach.

### D4-malform-gate-verified [info/ok-verified/confidence=high]
**malform-huge-activepower: the northbound plausibility gate + last-known-good hold are implemented, tested, and correct — 32767e9 W is rejected, never adopted, never stored**

**Evidence:** scheduler.go:187 `const maxPlausibleLimitW = 1e9` with the exact overflow-bait rationale (:181-186: "value×10^multiplier can reach ~3.3e13 (32767×10^9)"); :520-527 plausibleField rejects NaN/Inf/|w|>1e9 on every OpMod limit; failClosed (:330-351) never adopts nor stores a malformed control and re-serves lastGood marked Held+ImplausibleReject while unexpired; RejectHook (:340-342) surfaces a Table-27 status-253 receipt-reject (which is why PASS runs show cannot_comply=True with peak 0 W); run/run.go:401-412 logs the hold and increments metrics.ImplausibleRejects. gridsim serves exactly Multiplier:9,Value:32767 on the SAME control as the safe cap (sim/gridsim/malform.go:130-135) so the hold path is what's exercised. Pinned by scheduler failclosed_test.go (hold/expiry/explicit-clear tables) and fuzz_test.go:205-220 (no |limit|>maxPlausibleLimitW ever passes plausibleControl). GAP-09's NaN gate is orthogonal and correctly bypassed (the value is finite); the magnitude gate is what catches it, per internal/northbound/CLAUDE.md rule 6. Residual by-design gap (low): a finite absurd limit ≤1e9 (e.g. 5e8 W) IS adopted — harmless for caps (a loose cap ≈ no cap; the solar ceiling is clamped to nameplate at optimizer.go:1419-1422) but a site-nameplate-scaled bound would be tighter.

### D6-counter-churn-proofing-verified [info/ok-verified/confidence=high]
**expOverTicks churn-proofing (2026-07-03 fix) verified present and correctly reasoned — the QA report's 'each replacement resets the guard session' hypothesis is refuted at the counter layer**

**Evidence:** optimizer.go:170-180 (field doc): expOverTicks is "Deliberately NOT a field of expGuard — that struct is the ceiling controller's state and resets on every cap VALUE change, but a rewritten cap value is a new controller session with the SAME compliance obligation... reset only when the export limit clears entirely"; enforced at optimizer.go:1494-1517 (reset only on NaN, leaky ±1 otherwise). Introduced by commit c47b516 (2026-07-03, 'QA v3-v6 compliance hardening'), predating this session. The shadow port preserves the split exactly (constraint/export.go:116-126: "overTicks is deliberately NOT touched here"). The counter's residual weaknesses under churn are the band/decrement/NaN semantics reported in D1/D2, not a per-mRID or per-value reset — adopting a new mRID with the same value resets nothing (optimizer.go:955 compares values only).

---

## Probe: finding-A-ev-architecture

**Probe summary:** Probe on finding A (plan-follow suppresses reactive EV charging). I read the full EV command path in lexa-hub: internal/orchestrator/optimizer.go (rule cascade, applyPlanRule, applyEVChargingRule, applyExportLimitRule), planner.go (DP EV action space, PlanInterval/PlanTarget), engine.go (tick/run/plannerLoop/replan/Wake/buildPlannerParams), cmd/hub/main.go + state.go (lexa/evse/+/state ingestion), configs/hub.json, plus the bench-side scenarios (csip-tls-test cmd/dashboard/mayhem_ocpp_openadr.go) and the prior session's live capture (hub-evrule-capture.log, 65 ticks of "ev=0.0A"). Verdict: the session report's finding A is accurate and verified in code, but it UNDERSTATES the defect — beyond the 900 s replan staleness, (1) a fresh replan can still legitimately defer charging for hours (intentional smart charging when EV target/departure are configured), and (2) far worse, on any battery site whose planner does NOT model an EV (documented config `ev_capacity_kwh: 0` "disables EV planning"), every plan interval carries EVMaxCurrentA=0 and applyPlanRule pushes that 0 A to every active session on every tick, forever — replanning never fixes it; the EV permanently never charges, silently. I also found the plan's early EV command disables the export-limit rule's EV-absorption lever (hasEVSECommand skip). There is no session-connect replan trigger anywhere (onEVSEState only stores state; Wake() forces a tick, not a replan, and a forced tick still follows the stale plan). Of the four product options I recommend (b) in a specific bounded form — the plan owns the EV axis ONLY when it actually modelled an EV asset (the existing PlanTarget.EVSetpointW NaN sentinel is precisely "plan is silent on EV"); otherwise EVSEs fall through to applyEVChargingRule, which already enforces import-cap suspend + cooldown + solar-budget throttle, with CSIP-AUS load caps clamping after economics — plus option (a) session-connect replan as a cheap follow-up for modelled-EV staleness. Options (c) and (d) rejected: (c) regresses shipped V2G (D8/WP-14 EVSetpointW carriage) and TOU EV cost optimization; (d) leaves a real product bug and makes QA certify around it. Details, per-option cost/risk analysis, and file:line evidence are in the findings.

### A-1 [high/design-flaw/confidence=high] — **verifier: CONFIRMED**
**VERIFIED finding A: plan-follow suppresses the reactive EV rule and pushes plan ev=0.0A to newly-connected sessions; no session-connect replan trigger exists (recommended fix: option (b), bounded)**

**Evidence:** Verified in code end-to-end (lexa-hub). (1) Suppression gate: internal/orchestrator/optimizer.go:434-436 `planFollowed := false; if state.CSIPControl == nil || state.CSIPControl.Base.OpModFixedW == nil { batteries, surplusW, planFollowed = applyPlanRule(...) }` and optimizer.go:479 `if !planFollowed {` wrapping Rule 4 (:481), Rule 5 (:518), and Rule 6 `applyEVChargingRule(...)` (:526). planFollowed is true whenever the plan has ANY non-NaN battery setpoint (applyPlanRule returns false only for nil target, NaN setW, or totalCap==0 — optimizer.go:770-804); the live capture shows `battery=0W` still counts as followed. (2) EV command: optimizer.go:840-846 `for _, ev := range evses { if ev.Connected && ev.SessionActive { cmd := EVSECommand{... MaxCurrentA: target.EVMaxCurrentA}` — the plan's per-slot value is pushed to every active session unconditionally. (3) Replan cadence: engine.go:607-611 `interval := time.Duration(e.plannerCfg.ReplanIntervalS) * time.Second; if interval <= 0 { interval = 15 * time.Minute }`; configs/hub.json:45 `"replan_interval_s": 900`. plannerWake fires only from setPlanIn (DER constraints/prices/EVGoal/solar forecast/load profile/tariff — engine.go:319-425) and the ticker; the EVSE state subscription (cmd/hub/main.go:931-936) calls only `reader.onEVSEState` + `dersite.OnEVSEState` — no Wake, no replan poke. (4) Wake() semantics: engine.go:486-491 plus run() :553-557 — urgentWake forces a control TICK; tick() re-injects the SAME stale plan (engine.go:982-984 `dp := e.state.dailyPlan.Load(); state.DailyPlanTarget = dp.CurrentTarget(serverTime)`), so even a hypothetical Wake-on-session-connect would not start charging. (5) Planner session-awareness: buildPlannerParams (engine.go:832-840) reads an active session ONLY to seed InitialEVSocKwh/EVMaxChargeKw; the EV asset itself is modelled purely from config (`evCapKwh := cfg.EVCapacityKwh`, engine.go:818). (6) Live corroboration: scratchpad hub-evrule-capture.log contains 65 ticks of `[plan/follow] following 24h plan: battery=0W ev=0.0A → set 1 batteries, 1 EVSEs`, matching the AddDecision format at optimizer.go:868-870. No config switch disables plan-follow in optimizer mode (cmd/hub/mode.go's gateway flip is a different author entirely). Root cause: Rule 2.5 was designed as an exclusive economics author keyed only on the plan's battery term, the planner has no session-arrival concept, and a session connect is not a planner input. Blast radius: every real battery site — a newly plugged EV waits up to 15 min for the plan to even see its SOC and typically until the plan's cheap-tariff window (e.g. 2am) to start charging; also fails all 1.6J mayhem EV scenarios (80-95 s windows vs 900 s replan).

**Root cause:** applyPlanRule takes exclusive EV write authority whenever the plan has a battery term, while the planner's EV schedule is config-static with no session-arrival concept and no event-driven replan; the only replan triggers are the 900 s ticker and planner-INPUT changes.

**Proposed fix:** OPTION ANALYSIS (do-not-implement, as tasked). (a) Session-connect -> immediate replan: ~30 LOC (SessionActive rising edge in cmd/hub/state.go -> new Engine.RequestReplan() doing a non-blocking plannerWake send, same pattern as engine.go:337-341; DP runs off the tick path; buffered(1) channel coalesces flapping). Safe for single-writer invariant (plannerLoop stays dailyPlan's sole writer). BUT insufficient alone: a fresh replan with ev_capacity_kwh=0 still yields 0 A forever (finding A-2), and with the EV modelled it may STILL legitimately say 0 A now (cheaper at 2am) — fixes staleness, not the behavior. (b) RECOMMENDED, bounded form: plan owns the EV axis ONLY when it modelled an EV asset — gate applyPlanRule's EV block (optimizer.go:840-866) on `!math.IsNaN(target.EVSetpointW)` (planner.go:719-726 documents NaN == no EV asset modelled; the sentinel already rides PlanTarget, planner.go:203-207), and run applyEVChargingRule for still-uncommanded EVSEs even when planFollowed (battery rules 4-5 stay suppressed). Safety in both cap directions: extra EV draw REDUCES export (safe under export caps); under import caps applyEVChargingRule already suspends at/above importLimitW (optimizer.go:2090-2101), holds during import-guard cooldown (:2069-2080), and throttles to solar budget (:2114-2126); the CSIP-AUS load cap (Rule 3.7) clamps final EV draw after economics (optimizer.go:545-549). TOU optimality: modelled EVs keep smart charging (plan wins); unmodelled EVs revert to the pre-planner reactive behavior. ev_storage/V2G: untouched — V2G requires a modelled EV, so EVSetpointW is non-NaN and the plan keeps authority; the D8/WP-14 carriage is unchanged. Invariants: change is cascade-local (single control goroutine), no engineState writers, no actuator-registration changes, ~40-60 LOC + tests. It also fixes A-2 outright and restores the export rule's EV lever (A-3). (c) Plan advisory / reactive owns EV: regresses shipped TOU EV optimization and the entire ev_storage design (which exists BECAUSE the plan owns EV) — rejected. (d) Leave as-is + re-scope QA: leaves the A-2 permanent-suspension bug and the 15-min blind window on real sites; QA would certify around a product defect — rejected. RECOMMENDATION: (b) now; (a) as a small follow-up so modelled-EV plans absorb the session's live SOC within one DP run instead of 900 s; optionally a DP tie-break preferring the EARLIEST equal-cost charge slot so flat off-peak pricing does not gratuitously defer to 2am (the 23:50 capture shows exactly this indifference-deferral).

**Blast radius:** All battery-equipped sites (plan-follow effectively always on in optimizer mode). EV charge start delayed >=15 min minimum, hours typical; QA 1.6J scenarios structurally unfalsifiable.

**Verifier reasoning:** Every load-bearing claim verified by direct code read in /home/dmitri/projects/lexa-hub. (1) Gate: internal/orchestrator/optimizer.go:434-437 sets planFollowed from applyPlanRule whenever CSIP OpModFixedW is absent, and :479 "if !planFollowed {" wraps Rules 4 (:481), 5 (:518), and 6 applyEVChargingRule (:526); applyPlanRule returns false ONLY on nil target (:770), NaN BattSetpointW (:774-776), or totalCap==0 (:802) — setW=0 ("battery=0W") still claims authority. (2) EV push: optimizer.go:840-846 pushes target.EVMaxCurrentA to every Connected+SessionActive EVSE; with no EV modelled the planner's action space is evCurrents := []float64{0} (planner.go:303), so the pushed value is 0 A (suspend). (3) No session-connect trigger: exhaustive grep — Wake()/signalReplan fire only from mode.go:215, main.go:923 (CSIP Connect=false), and the Set* planner-input mutators (engine.go:321-431); the EVSE handler (cmd/hub/main.go:931-936 → state.go:523-527) is a pure map store. Replan cadence engine.go:607-611 + configs/hub.json:45 replan_interval_s=900. (4) Wake insufficiency: engine.go:553-557/982-984 — a forced tick re-injects the same stale dailyPlan via CurrentTarget. (5) Planner session-blindness: engine.go:818-840 (evCapKwh := cfg.EVCapacityKwh; session only seeds InitialEVSocKwh/EVMaxChargeKw); plan-follow engages whenever a battery is modelled (planner.go:281 hasBatt := p.BattCapacityKwh > 0 → non-NaN BattSetpointW); no disable flag exists. (6) Live corroboration: scratchpad hub-evrule-capture.log has exactly 65 "[plan/follow] following 24h plan: battery=0W ev=0.0A → set 1 batteries, 1 EVSEs" ticks (2026-07-15 23:50), matching the AddDecision format at optimizer.go:868-870; mayhem-ocpp16-fixed.log FAIL "charger stayed pinned near ~0.0A after the control was cleared" is consistent. (7) Fix (b) premises verified: EVSetpointW NaN sentinel == no EV modelled (planner.go:719-726, carried at :203-207); applyEVChargingRule's import suspend/cooldown/solar-throttle at optimizer.go:2090-2101/:2069-2080/:2114-2126; and the A-3 rationale is real — applyExportLimitRule skips plan-commanded EVSEs (optimizer.go:1016-1022 !hasEVSECommand), so plan-follow removes the export rule's EV absorption lever. No refuting evidence found; severity=high, kind=design-flaw is appropriate.

**Verifier corrections:** Root cause and recommended fix stand as stated. One implementation caveat to add to fix (b): applyPlanRule returns surplusW=0 (optimizer.go:873 "Zero surplusW so self-consumption and TOU rules don't fire after us"), so running applyEVChargingRule for still-uncommanded EVSEs under planFollowed will hit the no-grid-constraint solar-budget branch (optimizer.go:2114-2126) with surplusW=0 whenever solarW>0 and floor the EV at minChargeA (6 A, math.Max at :2122) instead of full rate — the change must decide which surplus figure the reactive EV path sees under plan-follow (e.g. preserve the pre-plan surplus for the EV branch, or accept the 6 A floor deliberately). Also note the shipped configs/hub.json models the EV (ev_capacity_kwh: 60.0, line 37), so on default config fix (b) changes nothing until a site omits/zeroes that key — the unmodelled-EV permanent-suspend (finding A-2) is the config-dependent half; the 900 s session-blind window (fix (a)) applies to modelled EVs too.

### A-2 [high/bug/confidence=high] — **verifier: CONFIRMED**
**Worse than reported: with ev_capacity_kwh unset/0 on a battery site, the plan commands 0 A to every active EV session FOREVER — replanning never fixes it**

**Evidence:** Verified in code (not observed live — bench config has ev_capacity_kwh: 60). internal/orchestrator/planner.go:282 `hasEV := p.EVCapacityKwh > 0`; planner.go:303-304 `evCurrents := []float64{0}` expanded only `if hasEV && p.EVMaxChargeKw > 0`; planner.go:525-526 forces the zero action `if (evGone || !hasEV) && ci != zeroEVIdx`; backtracking emits planner.go:717 `evMaxA := math.Max(0, evA)` = 0 into every PlanInterval.EVMaxCurrentA (:731). applyPlanRule then pushes it to hardware every tick: optimizer.go:841-845 `if ev.Connected && ev.SessionActive { cmd := EVSECommand{... MaxCurrentA: target.EVMaxCurrentA}` — a standing 0 A suspend re-issued to every session while planFollowed suppresses applyEVChargingRule (optimizer.go:479, 526). Because the 0 A stems from the asset being unmodelled — not staleness — every future replan reproduces it. The config doc directly contradicts the actual effect: planner.go:213 `// EV asset. EVCapacityKwh == 0 disables EV planning.` — it does not disable EV planning; it converts the planner into a permanent EV-suspend author. Preconditions: connected battery (non-NaN BattSetpointW, totalCap>0 — optimizer.go:773-804) + configured EVSE with an active session + no OpModFixedW. This is 'inferred from code' in the sense that no live capture of this exact config exists, but every code step is quoted and unconditional.

**Root cause:** The plan encodes 'no EV asset modelled' as EVMaxCurrentA=0, indistinguishable from a deliberate suspend; applyPlanRule never consults the correct sentinel (EVSetpointW=NaN, planner.go:719-726) that PlanTarget already carries.

**Proposed fix:** Same code change as A-1's recommended option (b): gate applyPlanRule's EV block on `!math.IsNaN(target.EVSetpointW)`; fall through to applyEVChargingRule. Fix the planner.go:213 doc comment. Regression test: battery-planned site, hasEV=false, active session => EV receives a reactive command, never a standing 0 A.

**Blast radius:** Any commissioned site with battery + EVSE where the installer left planner.ev_capacity_kwh unset (a documented, legal config): EV charging silently and permanently disabled with a healthy-looking plan log ('following 24h plan: ... ev=0.0A') — no alarm, no breach, no CannotComply.

**Verifier reasoning:** Every cited code step verified by direct read. (1) planner.go:282 `hasEV := p.EVCapacityKwh > 0`; :303-304 evCurrents=[0] unless hasEV && EVMaxChargeKw>0; :400-403 zeroEVIdx=0. (2) planner.go:526 `if (evGone || !hasEV) && ci != zeroEVIdx { continue }` pins the DP to 0 A. (3) planner.go:688/:717/:731 emit EVMaxCurrentA=0 into every PlanInterval; :723-726 EVSetpointW=NaN when !hasEV. (4) Preconditions match code: battW non-NaN iff hasBatt (planner.go:683-684; engine.go:773-806 seeds BattCapacityKwh from any connected battery's live CapacityWh, so a battery site always plans); applyPlanRule bails only on NaN setW (optimizer.go:774-776) or totalCap==0 (:802-803); OpModFixedW gate at :435. (5) optimizer.go:840-846 commands MaxCurrentA=0 to every Connected+SessionActive EVSE; the setpoint-mode branch (:858) requires non-NaN >0, so NaN keeps ceiling-mode 0 A; :873 returns planFollowed=true, suppressing applyEVChargingRule (:479/:526). No later rule lifts it: export-rule EV absorption skips already-commanded EVSEs (optimizer.go:1016-1021) and applyEVChargingRule skips them too (:2064). (6) 0 A is actuated as an explicit standing suspend: cmd/hub/desired.go:525-527 ("MaxCurrentA == 0 is an explicit suspend ... reconciler maps that to a 0 A SetChargingProfile"), retained + reasserted on reconnect. (7) Permanence verified: plannerLoop plans unconditionally at startup + every interval (engine.go:614-625); evCapKwh := cfg.EVCapacityKwh each replan (engine.go:818), EVGoal fallback gated on evStorage=false default (:819-823) — config-driven, so every replan reproduces it; not a staleness issue. (8) Doc contradiction verified: planner.go:213 says "EVCapacityKwh == 0 disables EV planning" while the actual effect on a battery site is a permanent plan-authored EV suspend (engine.go:817's "silently un-modelled" comment is likewise wrong for this case). Bench config ships ev_capacity_kwh: 60 (configs/hub.json:37), consistent with "verified in code, not observed live". The QA report §7.1 (Finding A) only described the modelled-EV/stale-plan variant, so "worse than reported" is fair. Severity=high is defensible (wrong standing control on a real battery+EVSE site with a plausible commissioning config, but no safety guard defeated — the EV just never charges).

**Verifier corrections:** Finding, root cause, and fix direction are correct; two fix-completeness caveats. (a) The "fall through to applyEVChargingRule" half must relax the `!planFollowed` gate at optimizer.go:479/:526 (per-EVSE hasEVSECommand ownership at :2064 already prevents double-commanding), and note applyPlanRule returns surplusW=0 (optimizer.go:873) — a naive fall-through hands rule 6 a zeroed surplus, under-serving solar-aware EV charging; pass the pre-zero surplus or recompute. (b) The NaN-EVSetpointW sentinel covers only EVCapacityKwh==0. The adjacent misconfig ev_capacity_kwh>0 with EVMaxChargeKw effectively 0 (planner.go:303-304; the live derivation at engine.go:833-838 requires an active session reporting non-NaN EV SOC, which SoC-less EVSEs never do) produces the identical permanent 0 A suspend but with EVSetpointW=0 (non-NaN, planner.go:723-726), which the proposed gate does not catch — the regression test matrix should include that case or the fix should gate on "plan had a usable EV action space" rather than the NaN sentinel alone.

### A-3 [medium/design-flaw/confidence=high]
**Plan-follow's early EV command also disables the export-limit rule's EV-absorption lever (Rule 3 skips already-commanded EVSEs)**

**Evidence:** Verified in code. Rule 2.5 appends EVSECommands before Rule 3 runs (cascade order: optimizer.go:436 then :441). applyExportLimitRule selects its EV lever only among un-commanded EVSEs: optimizer.go:1016-1022 `if evses[i].Connected && evses[i].SessionActive && !hasEVSECommand(plan.EVSECommands, evses[i].StationID, evses[i].ConnectorID) { ev = &evses[i]; break }` then `if ev == nil { o.expGuard.evSetpointA = math.NaN(); o.expGuard.evCmdW = math.NaN() }`. So while plan-follow holds ev=0.0A, the export-limit rule cannot absorb surplus into the EV — one of its three documented levers ('absorbs surplus into battery-charge/EV and curtails solar', optimizer.go:421-423 and QA report 2.1). The 2026-07-15 capture shows compensation via solar curtailment ('[csip/export-limit] holding generation <= 770W...'), so this is a lost lever, not an observed breach; residual risk is battery-full + export cap where EV absorption would be the only lever besides the e0864c9 discharge cap.

**Root cause:** Command-ownership coordination (hasEVSECommand) treats the plan's 0 A suspend as an authoritative claim on the EV axis; later compliance rules may narrow but never widen an owned axis (the cascade's documented convention, optimizer.go:534-537).

**Proposed fix:** Fold into A-1's option (b): when the plan did not model an EV, the axis stays unclaimed and Rule 3's existing selection (optimizer.go:1016) re-engages with zero extra code. When the plan DID model the EV, keep today's ownership (widening a V2G/TOU EV decision from the export rule needs a deliberate design pass, not a side effect). Pin with a test.

**Blast radius:** Compliance headroom loss under export caps on plan-followed sites, not an active breach today; the A-1 fix restores the lever for free when the plan is EV-silent.

### A-4 [medium/test-blindspot/confidence=high]
**QA oracle misattributes the failure class: ocpp16 scenarios FAIL against INV-OCPP16 while the 1.6 bridge is untested (EV never charged for plan reasons); no charging-precondition gate**

**Evidence:** Verified in bench code (csip-tls-test). ocpp16SmartChargeScenario (cmd/dashboard/mayhem_ocpp_openadr.go:142-177, HoldS 80) and clearProfileReleaseScenario (:179-214, HoldS 95) start a session (`start_session`, :158/:195) then post an import cap and judge 'charger current drops... then climbs back' (:148, :185) under Category 'OCPP 1.6J compatibility (INV-OCPP16)' (:146, :183). Neither setup nor evaluate asserts the precondition 'the EV was actually drawing current before the cap'; with the hub in plan-follow commanding ev=0.0A (A-1, verified), the charger never draws, nothing is curtailed or released, and each scenario's Fix text points at the wrong subsystem (bridge16.go / reconcile_shell.go, :150/:187). Knock-on blind pass recorded by the session itself: QA_SESSION_REPORT_2026-07-16.md:172 — batch-3 OCPP scenarios passed while 'EV draw coherence not exercised'. Scenario windows (80-95 s) are far shorter than the 900 s replan cadence, so the oracle cannot distinguish 'bridge broken' from 'plan says 0 A'.

**Root cause:** Scenarios assume the reactive EV rule governs a fresh session; they neither force the hub out of plan-follow nor verify the EV-charging precondition before judging the compatibility invariant.

**Proposed fix:** Regardless of which product option ships: add a precondition assertion (ground-truth charger current above a floor before the cap posts; otherwise INCONCLUSIVE with cause 'EV never charged — hub plan-follow?', never FAIL vs INV-OCPP16). This is diagnosis hygiene, not a substitute for the product fix — option (d) alone (re-scope QA, keep product as-is) is rejected because it certifies around the A-1/A-2 defects.

**Blast radius:** 1.6J compatibility currently uncertifiable either way: FAILs misattributed, some passes blind. A QA oracle that can both wrongly condemn and wrongly certify the OCPP16 path.

### A-5 [info/ok-verified/confidence=high]
**ok-verified: session report 7.1's factual claims about finding A are accurate against code and captures (with two understatements reported separately)**

**Evidence:** Each 7.1 claim checked against code I read: (1) 'plan-follow suppresses the reactive EV rule (optimizer.go rules 4-6 gated on !planFollowed)' — optimizer.go:479-527, exact. (2) 'the 24h plan commands ev=0.0A' with a live capture — hub-evrule-capture.log has 65 `[plan/follow] following 24h plan: battery=0W ev=0.0A` lines whose format matches optimizer.go:868-870 (`"following 24h plan: battery=%.0fW ev=%.1fA"`). (3) 'replan interval 900s' — configs/hub.json:45 + engine.go:607-611. (4) 'a newly-started session isn't in the stale plan' — buildPlannerParams samples session SOC only at replan time (engine.go:832-840); no event-driven replan on session connect (cmd/hub/main.go:931-936). (5) 'proto-agnostic (would affect 2.0.1 too)' — suppression and the 0 A command live in the optimizer cascade upstream of any OCPP version split (optimizer.go:840-866 emits generic EVSECommand). (6) 'fix 2.1/e0864c9 necessary but not sufficient' — that fix (planExportDischargeCapW, optimizer.go:433, 714-757, 782-787) touches only the battery-discharge axis, not EV suppression. The report understates only the permanent-0A unmodelled-EV case (A-2) and the lost export-absorption lever (A-3).

**Root cause:** n/a — verification finding.

**Proposed fix:** n/a

**Blast radius:** n/a
