## Probe: finding-E-modsim-leak

**Probe summary:** Probe E (modsim /state HTTP 500 after fault-injection cycles) is root-caused, and the session report's "cumulative resource leak" hypothesis is disproven. I read the full sim stack (csip-tls-test/sim/modsim/main.go, sim/simapi/server.go+logs.go, sim/southbound/{sim,solar,solar_adv,faults,battery}.go), the vendored lexa-proto sunspec decode (scale.go, layout.go, der1547.go), the hub-side write paths (lexa-hub vendor/lexa-proto/derbase/derbase.go, internal/southbound/inverter, cmd/modbus/reconcile_adv.go), the mayhem scenario definitions (qa/scenarios/nan-sentinel.json, mayhem_transport.go, clearAllFaults), and the session's raw batch logs. The only 500 path for GET /state is simapi writeJSON's json.Marshal error (server.go:267-271), which fires when the snapshot contains NaN; lexa-proto View.Float returns NaN for the SunSpec 0x8000 sentinel (layout.go:259-271) and advSnapshot copies Parse704 floats verbatim into the JSON. The corruption vector: the nan-sentinel scenario makes every Modbus read return 0x8000 (faults.go:153-159); the hub's model-704 writers are whole-block read-modify-writes (derbase write704, derbase.go:355-367, used for ALL ceiling/PF/var/setpoint writes on a 7xx device); a write during the 35 s fault window writes the all-sentinel block back, the sim persists it verbatim (faults.intercept pass-through, faults.go:314-316), and /state 500s permanently until restart. Bench evidence matches exactly: all three crashes cluster on soak batch ad (the only batch with solar nan-sentinel) — crash #1 was already dead at the first sample of the following ae batch — and the battery sim, which ran its own nan-sentinel scenario every aa batch but serves no 7xx models (so hub writes to it are single-register), never crashed. One link (a 704 write firing inside each window) is inferred from campaign config (advanced_der:on, reconciler.adv:active) rather than journal-verified; the proposed one-line bench diagnostic (the 500 body reads "json: unsupported value: NaN"; /registers stays 200 showing 32768s across the 704 block) confirms it without redeploy. The same chain exposes a product-severity bug: write704 writes back an unvalidated read, so a real half-initialized/torn device read coinciding with any 704 control write programs garbage into a real inverter. Fixes proposed at three layers (sanitize /state, validate-before-write-back in derbase with MTR-4 paired-PR discipline, and a nan_sentinel-RMW regression test plus a 10k /inject+/fault soak test). No actual resource leak exists — verified and reported as such.

### E2-write704-blind-rmw-product-bug [critical/bug/confidence=medium] — **verifier: CONFIRMED**

> **RESOLVED 2026-07-16 (H7):** fixed in lexa-proto `85af8d5` — `proto.pin` bumped identically in both repos (verified) and the vendored trees regenerated (the H7 paired-PR, MTR-4 discipline). `write704` and its 703 twin `SetEnterService` now refuse a sentinel-corrupt read via `sunspec.View.ReadLooksCorrupt()` (`vendor/lexa-proto/derbase/derbase.go`) instead of writing an all-0x8000 block back to the device. The `[critical/bug]` analysis below describes the **pre-fix** behavior and is retained only as the historical record — it is no longer a live-open vulnerability.

**Product bug exposed by the same chain: derbase write704 blindly writes back an unvalidated read — a sentinel-saturated or torn read coinciding with any 704 write programs garbage (including -32768 setpoints and enabled sync groups) into a REAL inverter's control registers**

**Evidence:** lexa-hub/vendor/lexa-proto/derbase/derbase.go:355-367: `func (b *Base) write704(tag string, fn func(v sunspec.View)) error { ... regs, err := b.Reader.ReadModel(sunspec.ModelDERCtlAC) ... fn(sunspec.L704.View(regs)); return b.Reader.WriteModel(sunspec.ModelDERCtlAC, 0, regs[:sunspec.L704.Len()]) }` — there is NO validation of the read block before it is written back: no check that SF registers are sane, no check for 0x8000 saturation, no plausibility bound. Every 704 control (SetFixedPF, SetConstantVar, SetActivePowerWatts, SetWMaxLimPctW — derbase.go:369-433) and every ceiling applied to a Has704 device via ApplyControl (derbase.go:284-289) rides this path. FaultNanSentinel explicitly models 'a half-initialised or failed register bank' (sim/southbound/sim.go:89-93) — i.e., a real device rebooting mid-poll returns exactly this. On real hardware the write-back would set e.g. WSet=0x8000 (-32768 W) with WSetEna=0x8000 (nonzero, likely decoded as enabled) and enable sync groups the hub never commanded. The bench PROVED the write-back happens (three modsim corruptions in one night, finding E1); what is unverified (hence confidence medium, severity per 'wrong control behavior possible on a real site') is how a specific real inverter treats writes of sentinel values to writable control registers — some will reject out-of-range writes, some will not. register_tearing gives a second, subtler instance: a torn mid-block register written back one power-of-ten off. Note the comment at derbase.go:356 says the whole-block write exists to 'keep PF sync groups (PF+Ext) atomic per the spec' — the fix must preserve that atomicity, not abandon RMW.

**Root cause:** write704 trusts its own read unconditionally. The mayhem suite's own INV-TRANSPORT oracle enforces 'never act on a sentinel reading' for the MEASUREMENT path (cmd/dashboard/mayhem.go:1634-1700), but the WRITE path's embedded read was never put under the same rule — a QA blind spot: diagnoseTransport watches HubSolarW plausibility, never what the hub wrote back to the device during the fault.

**Proposed fix:** In lexa-proto derbase.write704 (and the analogous curve/703 RMW paths): validate the read block before mutation — reject (return error, do not write) if any referenced SF register decodes to the notImplemented sentinel or if more than N registers of the block read 0x8000; optionally scope the write-back to the target sync group's register span instead of the full model (keeps PF+Ext atomicity with a much smaller poison surface). This is a lexa-proto change → paired-PR/pin-bump discipline per MTR-4 (both proto.pin files + both vendor trees in one session). Add a bench oracle: during transport-fault scenarios, sample the sim's /registers for 0x8000 in writable 704 registers after the window — turns this from invisible to a FAIL.

**Blast radius:** Real sites with 1547-2018 (7xx) inverters: any transient bad read coinciding with a control write can program persistent garbage setpoints/enables into the device. On the bench it is the direct cause of finding E.

**Verifier reasoning:** VERIFIED IN CODE (all files read directly): (1) The unvalidated RMW is real: lexa-hub/vendor/lexa-proto/derbase/derbase.go:357-367 — `regs, err := b.Reader.ReadModel(sunspec.ModelDERCtlAC); ... fn(sunspec.L704.View(regs)); return b.Reader.WriteModel(sunspec.ModelDERCtlAC, 0, regs[:sunspec.L704.Len()])` — no sentinel/SF/plausibility check anywhere; ReadModel/WriteModel (lexa-proto/sunspec/reader.go:51-102) validate nothing about content. All cited call sites confirmed: SetFixedPF/SetConstantVar/SetActivePowerWatts/SetWMaxLimPctW (derbase.go:369-435) and the Has704 ceiling path in ApplyControl (derbase.go:284-289). The 703 SetEnterService (derbase.go:323-330) is the same pattern. The hub exercises this live: cmd/modbus/reconcile_adv.go:24-29 uses derbase.SetFixedPF/SetConstantVar, and the campaign bench ran reconciler.adv=active + advanced_der=on (QA report §11). (2) Sim fault model verified: FaultNanSentinel rewrites READS to all-0x8000 (sim/southbound/faults.go:141-157); writes land verbatim in the register bank (sim.go HandleHoldingRegisters write path), so a write704 during the fault window permanently poisons the bank. (3) The modsim-crash causation chain is code-complete: /state decodes M704 from the live bank via Parse704 (solar_adv.go:566-580); sentinel→View.Float→NaN; json.Marshal fails on NaN → writeJSON returns 500 (sim/simapi/server.go:267-271) — exactly finding E's fingerprint (process active, /state 500 persistent, restart recovers). Timeline corroborates: the nan-sentinel scenario arms the fault ON the solar sim (scenariospec_migration_test.go:462), modbus-register-tearing also targets solar (mayhem_transport.go:149); soak batch ad contained nan-sentinel and crashes 2 and 3 occurred 'after ad' / mid-ad (qa-bench-health2.log: 'so=500' alert at 09:35 = end of batch ad per QA_CAMPAIGN_FINDINGS.md run #15); crash 1 was detected at the ae review after an unmonitored ac+ad window (the sims-not-health-checked gap is admitted in QA_CAMPAIGN_FINDINGS.md finding #3). The QA report's claim that crashes happened 'during transport scenarios that don't use the solar sim' is factually wrong — both transport scenarios arm faults on the solar sim — which undermines its 'resource leak' attribution. (4) QA oracle blind spot verified: diagnoseTransport (cmd/dashboard/mayhem.go:1640-1700) checks only HubReachable and HubSolarW plausibility; no oracle samples writable control registers after the window; the transport scenarios hold an active zero-export cap during the fault (modbusSurvivalFinding comment, mayhem_transport.go:157-163), making a hub write during the poisoned-read window likely by design. INFERRED (not directly observed): no /registers dump or 500 response body was captured in any artifact, so 'the bench PROVED the write-back' is an overstatement — it is the only mechanism found that matches the crash fingerprint and timeline, but it is a strongly corroborated hypothesis, not observed proof. Real-inverter impact is device-dependent (a block write spanning read-only SF registers may be rejected wholesale by some firmware), which the finding itself acknowledged; severity=critical under 'wrong control behavior possible' is defensible.

**Verifier corrections:** Two refinements, neither overturning the finding: (1) Mechanism detail — under an all-sentinel read the poison is subtler and arguably worse than claimed: View.SetFloat is a SILENT NO-OP when the SF register reads sentinel (layout.go:326-333, `v.SF(f.SF)` ok=false → return), so the commanded setpoint is never encoded; but SetBool/SetEnum/SetU32 have no SF dependency and write unconditionally (layout.go:295-316). The written block is therefore: target sync group Ena=1 (exactly 1, not 0x8000), mode enum + RvrtTms written, the setpoint itself LEFT at 0x8000 from the poisoned read, and every other writable register 0x8000 — an explicit enable paired with a −32768 sentinel setpoint. Other groups' Ena registers are written as 0x8000 (=32768, nonzero); whether real firmware decodes that as enabled is device-dependent (this repo's own Parse704 Bool would read it as false). SetFloat's silent no-op on unknown SF is itself a second defect worth fixing (enable-without-setpoint even absent faults). (2) Evidence framing — 'the bench PROVED the write-back happens' should read 'strongly corroborated': the full causal chain (write704 RMW → verbatim sim bank write → Parse704 NaN → json.Marshal failure → persistent /state 500) is code-verified end-to-end and uniquely fits all three crash fingerprints and timelines, and it CORRECTS the QA session report's own finding-E attribution ('cumulative resource leak' — likely wrong), but no post-crash register dump or 500 body exists in the artifacts. Fix proposal is sound with one completeness note: sentinel/SF validation of the pre-read does NOT cover the register_tearing variant (a torn block can be sentinel-free and plausible); scoping the write-back to the target sync-group's span plus the reconciler's existing verify-by-readback is the complementary mitigation. The proposed bench oracle (sample the sim's /registers — endpoint exists, simapi/server.go:92 — for 0x8000 in writable 704 registers after transport-fault windows) is apt and would have turned all three modsim crashes into attributed FAILs.

### E1-modsim-state-500-root-cause [high/infra/confidence=high] — **verifier: CONFIRMED**
**modsim /state 500 is NOT a resource leak: it is permanent register-map corruption — the hub's whole-block model-704 read-modify-write fires during a nan_sentinel (or register_tearing) fault window and persists 0x8000 into the sim's 704 block, making Snapshot() contain NaN and json.Marshal fail forever**

**Evidence:** Chain, every link read in code: (1) The ONLY way GET /state returns HTTP 500 is writeJSON's marshal-error path — csip-tls-test/sim/simapi/server.go:267-271: `b, err := json.Marshal(v); if err != nil { http.Error(w, err.Error(), http.StatusInternalServerError) }`. A handler panic would reset the connection, not 500, and handleState has no other error path (server.go:116-122). json.Marshal fails only on NaN/±Inf float64 ("json: unsupported value: NaN"). (2) NaN source: vendor/lexa-proto/sunspec/layout.go:259-271 — `View.Float` returns `math.NaN()` when the field value is the 0x8000 not-implemented sentinel OR its scale-factor register is sentinel (`if !ok || !v.Present(name) || v.notImpl(o, f) { return math.NaN() }` and `s, ok := v.SF(f.SF); if !ok { return math.NaN() }`). advSnapshot copies Parse704 floats verbatim into the /state JSON: sim/southbound/solar_adv.go:577-580 `c704 := sunspec.Parse704(...); out.FixedPF = advPFState{Ena: c704.PFWInjEna, PF: c704.PFWInjPF}` (also FixedVar.Pct, Ceiling704.Pct). (3) Corruption vector: the nan-sentinel scenario (csip-tls-test/qa/scenarios/nan-sentinel.json) arms `nan_sentinel` on solar for hold_s=35; sim/southbound/faults.go:153-159 then rewrites EVERY Modbus read to 0x8000 (`out[i] = 0x8000`). The hub's 704 writes are whole-block RMW: lexa-hub/vendor/lexa-proto/derbase/derbase.go:355-367 `write704 read-modify-writes the whole 704 block`: `regs, err := b.Reader.ReadModel(sunspec.ModelDERCtlAC); fn(sunspec.L704.View(regs)); return b.Reader.WriteModel(sunspec.ModelDERCtlAC, 0, regs[:sunspec.L704.Len()])`. Because the bench modsim runs -advanced (serves 704), `Has704` is true and EVERY inverter ceiling command goes through this RMW, not the legacy single-register M123 path — derbase.go:284-289 `if lim := firstNonNil(ctrl.OpModExpLimW, ctrl.OpModMaxLimW, ctrl.OpModGenLimW); lim != nil { if b.Has704 { b.SetWMaxLimPctW(...) } }`, and SetFixedPF/SetConstantVar/SetActivePowerWatts are all write704 wrappers (derbase.go:369-416). (4) The sim persists the poisoned write verbatim: RegisterMap.HandleHoldingRegisters write path (sim/southbound/sim.go:295-319) → OnWriteAttempt → faultController.intercept returns `true // no write-time fault armed — apply verbatim` (faults.go:314-316) when only nan_sentinel (a READ fault) is armed, so all-0x8000 lands permanently in the 704 registers, including PF_SF/WMaxLimPct_SF/VarSet_SF and PFWInj_PF. From then on Parse704 → NaN → /state 500 on every request until process restart (nothing ever rewrites those registers with clean values; a later healthy write704 re-reads the corrupt block and writes it back). Bench corroboration from the session artifacts: campaign config was `advanced_der:on, reconciler.adv:active` (scratchpad QA_CAMPAIGN_FINDINGS.md:6); the solar `nan-sentinel` scenario is in soak batch **ad** (scratchpad/soak-batch-ad) and all three crashes cluster on ad: crash #1 surfaced at the START of batch ae immediately after run 05-ad (qa-run-06-ae.log:26-30 "solar probe absent for 100% of the window" — dead before the batch began), crash #2 "after ad" (QA_CAMPAIGN_FINDINGS.md:66), crash #3 "during cycle3 batch ad" (QA_CAMPAIGN_FINDINGS.md:77-78). Differential control: batsim ran `battery-nan-sentinel` every aa batch (qa-run-02/07/12-aa.log:234-235 PASS) and NEVER 500'd — the battery sim serves no 7xx models (sim/southbound/battery.go:5-13, models 1/120/121/103/123/802), so Has704 is false and hub battery writes use the legacy single-register path (derbase.go:766-797 setLegacyWMaxLimPct writes RmpTms, WMaxLimPct, Ena as three 1-register writes — reads the block only to fetch the SF, never writes it back). Only the one 7xx device on the bench crashed. The one INFERRED (not directly verified — needs hub journals) link is that a 704-path write fired inside each 35 s fault window; with reconciler.adv:active + a standing retained adv/solar desired doc (the report itself documents retained adv-doc cross-scenario pollution) this is expected, and it exactly explains why the crash is intermittent (roughly 3 crashes over ~5 ad runs) rather than deterministic.

**Root cause:** Not a cumulative leak. A read-path fault injector (nan_sentinel / register_tearing) corrupts what the hub reads; the hub's model-704 writers are whole-block read-modify-writes; the corrupted block is written back and persisted by the sim's register map; the sim's /state snapshot decodes the persisted 0x8000 sentinels to NaN via lexa-proto sunspec.View.Float; json.Marshal rejects NaN; simapi.writeJSON turns that into HTTP 500 on every subsequent request. State is poisoned permanently (restart re-populates registers, hence 'restart recovers'). The apparent 'acceleration' tracks batch-ad run cadence, not a growing leak.

**Proposed fix:** Three layers (first two are test-infra, in csip-tls-test): (a) Make /state un-killable: in sim/simapi/server.go writeJSON, on marshal error re-marshal through a NaN/Inf-sanitizing pass (replace non-finite floats with null) and log the offending payload once — the QA ground-truth endpoint must degrade, never 500; same guard in broadcastLoop (server.go:250-252 currently silently `continue`s, muting the WS feed). (b) Sanitize at the source: sim/southbound/solar_adv.go advSnapshot should map NaN from Parse701/Parse704 to 0 or a null-able pointer field — sentinel-corrupted registers are legitimate sim states QA wants to SEE, not crash on. Optionally add fidelity: mark SF registers write-protected in the sim's RegisterMap (a real device's SFs are read-only), which also surfaces the hub's bad write-back as an observable divergence instead of silent corruption. (c) Regression test: a unit test in sim/southbound that arms nan_sentinel, performs a hub-style RMW through HandleHoldingRegisters (read the 704 span — receives all-0x8000 — then write it back), clears the fault, and asserts `json.Marshal(ss.Snapshot())` returns nil error; plus a soak test hammering /inject + /fault (all kinds, arm/clear) 10k times asserting marshal always succeeds and runtime.NumGoroutine() stays bounded. Immediate bench diagnostic that confirms this analysis without a redeploy: when /state next 500s, the response BODY will read 'json: unsupported value: NaN', and GET /registers will still return 200 showing 32768 across the 704 block while /state fails.

**Blast radius:** Test bench only for this finding (spurious inverter/meter BLINDs, 2 sim-induced FAILs, one invalidated 20-scenario batch, operator now doing preventive restarts) — but see E2 for the product-side half of the same defect.

**Verifier reasoning:** Every link of the claimed chain verified by direct code read. (1) 500 path: csip-tls-test/sim/simapi/server.go:267-275 writeJSON is the only error path of handleState (server.go:116-122) — `b, err := json.Marshal(v); if err != nil { http.Error(w, err.Error(), http.StatusInternalServerError) }`; broadcastLoop (server.go:250-252) silently `continue`s on the same error, muting the WS feed as claimed. (2) NaN source: lexa-proto/sunspec/layout.go:259-271 View.Float returns math.NaN() when the value or its SF register is the 0x8000/sentinel (`if !ok || !v.Present(name) || v.notImpl(o, f) { return math.NaN() }`; SF at layout.go:244-250 returns ok=false when `v.reg(o) == sentI16`). Parse704 populates value-typed float64 fields via v.Float (lexa-proto/sunspec/der1547.go:205-214, fields at 182-198), and advSnapshot copies them into value float64 JSON fields advPFState/advVarState/advCeilState (csip-tls-test/sim/southbound/solar_adv.go:543-556, 577-580) — json.Marshal fails on NaN. (3) Fault: qa/scenarios/nan-sentinel.json arms nan_sentinel on solar for 35s; sim/southbound/faults.go:153-158 rewrites EVERY read to `out[i] = 0x8000`, applied via the OnRead hook at sim/southbound/sim.go:350-352. (4) Hub RMW: lexa-hub/vendor/lexa-proto/derbase/derbase.go:355-367 write704 = ReadModel → fn(View) → WriteModel of the whole block; Has704 = r.HasModel(ModelDERCtlAC) (derbase.go:70); ceilings route to SetWMaxLimPctW when Has704 (derbase.go:285-289); SetFixedPF/SetConstantVar/SetActivePowerWatts are write704 wrappers (derbase.go:371-416). L704 is ~65-70 registers (derlayout.go:116-140), under the FC16 123-register cap, so the write-back lands in one transaction. (5) Persistence: with only a read fault armed, faultController.intercept returns true (faults.go:314-316 `return true // no write-time fault armed — apply verbatim`) and HandleHoldingRegisters stores req.Args verbatim (sim.go:305-315). populate704 runs only at init (solar_adv.go:142, 237-240) — nothing heals the block, matching "restart recovers". advSnapshot reads registers directly via readSlice/r.Get (solar_adv.go:168-174), bypassing OnRead — so a 500 requires actual persisted corruption, not merely an armed fault, exactly as the theory requires. (6) Differential controls verified: battery sim serves models 1/120/121/103/123/802 only (sim/southbound/battery.go:5-13) — no 7xx, Has704 false, battery-nan-sentinel (batch aa) never crashed; modbus-register-tearing sits in batch ac (soak-batch-ac line 15) which ran clean 4 cycles — the tear adds a finite delta to the block's MID register (sim.go:364-378), far from L704's SF cluster, producing finite values. (7) Logs: solar nan-sentinel is item 5 of soak-batch-ad; qa-run-05-ad.log:270 shows nan-sentinel PASS, then qa-run-06-ae.log shows "solar probe absent for 100% of the window" from batch start (scenarios 12-14 BLIND); crashes #2/#3 follow runs 10-ad/15-ad (QA_CAMPAIGN_FINDINGS.md FINDING #3 update and Run #15); mayhem's solar ground-truth probe is GET /state (mayhem_transport.go:333, mayhem_adv.go:132-137, which also confirms bench modsim ran -advanced serving 704). The one inferred link (a write704 fired inside each 35s window) stays inferred without hub journals, but is corroborated by campaign config `reconciler.adv:active` (QA_CAMPAIGN_FINDINGS.md line 6) plus the report's own retained-adv-doc pollution finding (a standing adv desired doc ⇒ divergence-driven corrective writes during the NaN readback window).

**Verifier corrections:** Three refinements, none overturning the finding. (a) It is stronger than "intermittent": all 3 recorded solar-nan-sentinel batch runs (05-ad, 10-ad, 15-ad) were followed by or contained a crash — 3/3, effectively deterministic per ad batch; the finding's "roughly 3 crashes over ~5 ad runs / intermittent" framing undersells the correlation (cycle-4's ad ran under the preventive-restart policy, so no counterexample exists). (b) The "(or register_tearing)" co-vector should be dropped: modbus-register-tearing lived in batch ac, which ran clean in all 4 cycles, and code-wise tearBlock perturbs the middle register of the block with a finite delta (+2000..+3500) that lands nowhere near L704's scale-factor cluster and yields finite Float values — no NaN/Inf, no marshal failure. nan_sentinel is the sole demonstrated vector. (c) Extra detail strengthening the mechanism: during the fault window View.SetFloat silently no-ops because the SF register reads sentinel (layout.go:321-333 `s, ok := v.SF(f.SF); if !ok { return }`), so the hub writes back an essentially all-0x8000 block with only the Ena/enum registers set — the corruption is even more total than "RMW with fn applied" suggests, and the hub's commanded value never lands at all. The proposed 3-layer fix is sound; within (b) prefer the null-able pointer over mapping NaN→0 (0 is a legitimate PF/pct value and would forge ground truth for QA oracles), and the write-protected-SF fidelity option is worth doing since a real device's read-only SFs would have surfaced the hub's corrupt write-back as a divergence.

### E3-report-misdiagnosis [medium/process/confidence=high]
**QA session report's finding-E hypothesis ('cumulative resource leak, accelerating, independent of scenario') is wrong on all three counts, and the adopted mitigation (preventive restarts) masks the defect instead of isolating it**

**Evidence:** docs/QA_SESSION_REPORT_2026-07-16.md §7.5 claims 'independent of the active scenario ... → a cumulative resource leak', and QA_CAMPAIGN_FINDINGS.md:78 says 'during TRANSPORT scenarios that don't use the solar sim → the modsim crashes CUMULATIVELY/independently, a worsening leak over the soak'. The session's own logs refute this: crash #1 was already present at the FIRST sample of batch ae ('solar probe absent for 100% of the window', qa-run-06-ae.log:28,30) — i.e. it happened during/at the end of the PRECEDING batch 05-ad, which contains the solar nan-sentinel scenario (soak-batch-ad); crashes #2 and #3 are logged as 'after ad' and 'during cycle3 batch ad' (QA_CAMPAIGN_FINDINGS.md:66,77). All three crashes correlate with the one batch that arms nan_sentinel on solar; none of the code has an unbounded structure (see E4). 'Accelerating ~hourly' tracks the operator's shift to faster curated batches (more ad passes per hour), not growth. The 'PASS' verdicts on nan-sentinel itself (qa-run-05/10/15-ad.log:270,284) are correct for the hub but hid that the scenario was lethally side-effecting the sim — the scenario can pass while destroying the test fixture for every subsequent scenario.

**Root cause:** Correlation was done against the scenario running WHEN the 500 was noticed, not against the scenario that ran BEFORE the first bad sample; 'process up + endpoint 500 + restart fixes it' pattern-matched to 'leak' without reading the 500 response body (which literally says 'json: unsupported value: NaN').

**Proposed fix:** Bench-runbook additions: (1) when a sim endpoint 500s, capture the response BODY, not just the status code; (2) the mayhem runner should hard-fail (or auto-restart + flag) a batch the moment a sim /state goes non-200, recording the immediately-preceding scenario id; (3) treat 'sim health check per review' (already adopted) as a stopgap, not a fix.

**Blast radius:** Process/triage quality: an engineer following the report would soak-profile modsim memory/goroutines and find nothing.

### E5-simapi-degraded-error-surfaces [low/design-flaw/confidence=high]
**Minor simapi robustness gaps around the same failure: WS broadcast goes silently mute on marshal error, and a failed ListenAndServe leaves a permanently dead API that still looks 'started'**

**Evidence:** sim/simapi/server.go:250-252: broadcastLoop does `b, err := json.Marshal(s.stateFn()); if err != nil { continue }` — once state contains NaN the dashboard's live WS feed silently freezes with no log line, compounding the /state 500 confusion. server.go:96-101: `go func() { if err := http.ListenAndServe(addr, cors(mux)); err != nil { log.Printf(...) } }()` — a bind failure is logged once and the Server object is returned as if healthy; nothing retries or crashes the sim (crash-only would be more consistent with the bench's AD-011 philosophy).

**Root cause:** Error paths written for the happy bench case; both become observability black holes exactly when the sim is unhealthy.

**Proposed fix:** Log (rate-limited) on broadcast marshal failure; make ListenAndServe failure fatal to the sim process so systemd restarts it visibly.

**Blast radius:** Bench observability only.

### E4-simapi-no-resource-leak [info/ok-verified/confidence=high]
**Verified: no cumulative resource leak exists in modsim/simapi — WS client lifecycle, log ring, inject/fault handlers, timers, and the tcp_drop listener bounce are all bounded**

**Evidence:** Hunted every category the leak hypothesis implies, all clean: (a) WebSocket: sim/simapi/server.go:202-242 handleWS removes the client from the broadcast map, closes its channel, and waits for the writer goroutine on disconnect (`delete(s.clients, ch); close(ch); <-writerDone; conn.Close()`); broadcastLoop uses non-blocking sends (server.go:256-259) so a slow client cannot block or accumulate. (b) Log ring: sim/simapi/logs.go:21,61-63 caps at maxLogLines=400 with slice trim; SSE subscribers unsubscribe via defer (logs.go:108). (c) /inject and /fault parse into function-local maps/structs with a 64 KiB LimitReader (server.go:133,178); the sim-side Inject writes fixed registers (sim/southbound/solar.go:313-375) and faultController.apply flips fixed booleans (faults.go:368-486) — no per-call allocation is retained. (d) The ack_before_effect timer is Stop()ed and replaced on each write and on clear (faults.go:351-357,382-386) — at most one outstanding. (e) tcp_drop bounces the Modbus listener synchronously under srvMu (sim/southbound/sim.go:548-566); the animation goroutine is one ticker created once (solar.go:519-521). (f) The register map is a fixed-address map — Set only ever writes addresses already in the populated layout, so it cannot grow per injection. Memory/goroutine/fd growth is therefore not the mechanism; the 500 is state corruption (E1).

**Proposed fix:** Keep the proposed 10k-cycle /inject+/fault soak unit test (E1 fix c) as a permanent guard so this verified property stays true.

**Blast radius:** None — negative result recorded so the orchestrator knows the leak space was searched, not skipped.

---

## Probe: config-drift-process

**Probe summary:** Audited bench-config drift and process state after the 2026-07-15/16 QA session. Read: docs/QA_SESSION_REPORT_2026-07-16.md (§3, §11, §12), lexa-hub scripts/deploy-hub-pi.sh (all 733 lines), configs/{hub,modbus,northbound,ocpp}.json, DEVKIT.md deploy sections, cmd/api/config.go (plan_stall), internal/orchestrator/optimizer.go (tunedTickInterval/scaleTicks), cmd/northbound/config.go + internal/northbound/responses/tracker.go (CannotComply vocab), csip-tls-test scripts/{bench-up.sh,hub-replay-tune.sh,mayhem-campaign.sh,mayhem.py,check-proto-pin.sh}, cmd/dashboard/mayhem{,_world}.go, sim/gridsim (Table-27 acceptance), and git state of all three repos. Overall judgment: the report's §11 bench-state table is accurate and its metrics_addr claim verified (deploy-hub-pi.sh has ZERO metrics_addr handling — grep confirms), but the drift problem is structurally worse than reported: there is NO working scripted deploy to the live dev-kit hub (deploy-hub-pi.sh hard-aborts on Yocto at mosquitto_passwd under set -e; DEVKIT.md documents raw scp that clobbers every hand-set key, and CLAUDE.md's deploy instruction contradicts DEVKIT.md). A redeploy by either path wipes metrics_addr, the mqttproxy broker port, FAST timing, advanced_der, reconciler.adv, and — worst — regresses legacy_cannotcomply_code to true, whose "until gridsim flips" footnote condition is already satisfied in committed gridsim code, making the shipped example config a conformance regression on the product-ish Pi deploy path. Process-wise, proto-pin lockstep is intact (both repos pin 60bdb1b; the session commits touch neither proto.pin nor vendor/), but ALL campaign work is local-only: 33 lexa-hub commits, 32 csip-tls-test commits, and 2 lexa-proto commits — including the pinned SHA 60bdb1b itself — exist on no remote, so PR-gated CI has never run on any of it and the pinned proto SHA is unreconstructible if this disk is lost. QA timing is FAST-consistent where it matters (plan_stall 75s and watchdogs safe at both cadences, no oracle reads the heartbeat), but mayhem.py lacks the engine-interval precondition mayhem-campaign.sh has, and the entire soak ran at the 3s cadence the hub's breach counters are calibrated at — the product's 15s cadence (scaleTicks floor-2 path) is essentially untested by this campaign.

### DRIFT-1 [high/infra/confidence=high] — **verifier: CONFIRMED**
**No scripted deploy path exists for the live dev-kit hub; both documented paths destroy or abort — all bench config is hand-managed by necessity**

**Evidence:** deploy-hub-pi.sh:133 `set -euo pipefail` + :242 `mosquitto_passwd -b "$PASSWD_FILE" "lexa-$svc" "$pass"` runs unconditionally (comment :225 'This always runs, independent of --bench-insecure'), but DEVKIT.md:48 states 'no mosquitto_passwd on Yocto' — so the script hard-aborts on 69.0.0.2 before ever reaching the config install at :354. CLAUDE.md 'Current bench deployment' says 'Deploy with scripts/deploy-hub-pi.sh 69.0.0.2 root per DEVKIT.md', but DEVKIT.md's actual procedure (§'Deploy to the dev kit') is `scp configs/*.json root@69.0.0.2:/etc/lexa/` with the parenthetical '(edit these on the device if they already exist — scp overwrites)'. Verified in code/docs.

**Root cause:** deploy-hub-pi.sh was written for the Debian Pi (apt, mosquitto_passwd, lexa user); the hub migrated to the Yocto dev kit 2026-07-07 but no devkit-compatible deploy script was created — CLAUDE.md's deploy line is stale/contradictory.

**Proposed fix:** Add a devkit-aware path: guard the mosquitto_passwd block on `command -v mosquitto_passwd` (DEVKIT.md already documents the broker is anonymous there), or add scripts/deploy-devkit.sh that reuses the binary/config/patch stages. Fix the CLAUDE.md deploy sentence to match reality.

**Blast radius:** Every deploy to the live hub is a hand-crafted scp/edit session; config drift (this whole probe) is structural, not incidental. The QA session's 'surgical' binary swap (report §3) was the only option, which is exactly how the metrics_addr gap arose.

**Verifier reasoning:** All cited evidence verified by direct read. (1) scripts/deploy-hub-pi.sh:133 has `set -euo pipefail`; the operative one for the abort is line 190, inside the `ssh sudo bash -s` remote heredoc. Lines 233-246 run `mosquitto_passwd -b` (242) / `-b -c` (244, the fresh-devkit branch) unconditionally, with the "This always runs, independent of --bench-insecure" comment at 225-228; two more unconditional mosquitto_passwd calls at 267-271 and 291-295. (2) DEVKIT.md:45-49 confirms "no mosquitto_passwd on Yocto" (mosquitto cross-built WITH_TLS=no, allow_anonymous true, no passwd/ACL); under set -e the exit-127 aborts the remote script before the config install at deploy-hub-pi.sh:354 (`install -m 644 $D/configs/... /etc/lexa/`) — possibly even earlier at line 205 (apt-get, absent on Yocto) or 210 (useradd). The abort is inferred shell semantics (SSH to 69.0.0.2 forbidden for this audit), but independently corroborated: csip-tls-test/docs/BENCH.md §Deploy (~line 93-95) states verbatim that deploy-hub-pi.sh "is Debian/sudo/lexa-user only and does NOT run against Yocto" and that the dev-kit path is "manual root@ scp path per lexa-hub/DEVKIT.md". (3) CLAUDE.md's "Deploy with scripts/deploy-hub-pi.sh 69.0.0.2 root per DEVKIT.md" is contradictory as claimed — grep for deploy-hub-pi in DEVKIT.md returns nothing; DEVKIT.md:249-271 is raw scp with ":258 (edit these on the device if they already exist — scp overwrites)", plus the User=lexa sed gotcha (:280-282) and 2026-07-15 hand-patch gotchas (:423-432). (4) "Hand-managed by necessity" is corroborated by the QA session report itself (line 136: metrics_addr hand-set on-device after the "surgical deploy" missed it, degrading QA oracles; line 138: binaries swapped by hand stop→swap→start with .bak backups). Root cause as claimed (script written for Debian Pi; hub migrated to Yocto dev kit 2026-07-07; no devkit script created) is consistent with BENCH.md's 2026-07-07 migration note and DEVKIT.md's history.

**Verifier corrections:** Finding and root cause stand; the FIX's first alternative is insufficient and the finding under-counts the stale docs. (a) Guarding only the mosquitto_passwd block on `command -v` does NOT make the script devkit-safe: the default path still writes /etc/mosquitto/conf.d/lexa.conf with `allow_anonymous false` + `password_file /etc/mosquitto/lexa-passwd` (deploy-hub-pi.sh:324-337) — a passwd file that would then never exist — and restarts mosquitto (:341), breaking the devkit's anonymous no-passwd broker (or being silently ignored if the cross-built broker's unit doesn't read conf.d; DEVKIT.md:173 shows its config is /etc/mosquitto/mosquitto.conf). It also still blindly overwrites the six configs (:354), destroying the devkit's hand-set mqtt_broker tcp://localhost:1882 mqttproxy repoint and metrics_addr rewrites (DEVKIT.md:61-63), and installs User=lexa units Yocto can't run un-sed'd (DEVKIT.md:273-283). Only the second proposed alternative — a real scripts/deploy-devkit.sh (or a --yocto mode that skips broker/user provisioning and preserves/reapplies the devkit config patches) — is a viable fix, and it must also cover the api.json/ocpp.json bench:true patching DEVKIT.md's 2026-07-15 gotchas require. (b) Additional stale artifacts in the same class the finding missed: lexa-hub/.claude/skills/hub-deploy/SKILL.md:8-10 still claims the hub is hub-pi 69.0.0.1 and "the ConnectCore dev kit (69.0.0.2) is offline", and :54 claims the deploy script "does NOT overwrite" configs — contradicted by deploy-hub-pi.sh:349-354 ("always overwritten"); CLAUDE.md's "in-repo default stays conservative (battery: off)" is contradicted by configs/modbus.json:9-13 ("battery":"active","solar":"active"). Note csip-tls-test/docs/BENCH.md already documents the true state correctly, so the doc fix is aligning CLAUDE.md and the hub-deploy skill with BENCH.md, not inventing new truth. Severity=high is defensible under the "QA oracle" rubric: this exact gap already degraded mayhem oracles (metrics scrape failure → adv-shadow-no-writes DEGRADED, per QA report line 136).

### DRIFT-3 [high/bug/confidence=high] — **verifier: CONFIRMED**
**configs/northbound.json still ships legacy_cannotcomply_code:true although the gridsim Table-27 flip (the footnote's precondition) is already committed — a redeploy regresses the hub to legacy 0xF0 CannotComply codes**

**Evidence:** configs/northbound.json:17 `"legacy_cannotcomply_code": true`. CLAUDE.md flag table: default false with footnote '*bench config ships true until gridsim flips — MTR-4 paired change'. The gridsim side HAS flipped, in committed code: csip-tls-test sim/gridsim/server.go:1041 ('Table 27 CannotComply-family codes the hub now sends by default') and sim/gridsim/cannotcomply_test.go:36-40 pin acceptance of codes 8/10/252/253/254 as VocabTable27. The bench device runs false (report §11, corroborated by cannotcomply-table27 executing against Table-27 accept). Code default is false: cmd/northbound/config.go:106 'false (the shipped [default])' / responses/tracker.go:160 'false — the default'. So the committed EXAMPLE config is the only artifact still carrying the legacy value, and it is exactly what deploy-hub-pi.sh:354 installs.

**Root cause:** The MTR-4 'paired change' was completed as a hand-edit on the device plus a gridsim commit, but the lexa-hub half (flipping the committed example config) was never landed — the pairing discipline was applied to the wire, not the repo.

**Proposed fix:** One-line commit: configs/northbound.json legacy_cannotcomply_code → false (or delete the key — omitempty, code default is already false). Highest-value single fix from this probe.

**Blast radius:** Any Pi deploy via deploy-hub-pi.sh (the product-shaped path) posts nonconformant legacy 0xF0 CannotComply codes instead of IEEE 2030.5 Table 27; a bench redeploy silently regresses cannotcomply-table27 and the WP-7 conformance posture.

**Verifier reasoning:** Every element of the finding checks out against code I read directly. (1) The committed example config carries the legacy value: /home/dmitri/projects/lexa-hub/configs/northbound.json:17 `"legacy_cannotcomply_code": true` — working tree clean (`git status --short configs/` empty), so this is the committed state, introduced by commit ea8b228 (WP-7) whose own doc comment explains the pairing intent: cmd/northbound/config.go:106-113 "false (the shipped default) makes responses.Tracker emit standard IEEE 2030.5 Table 27 codes ... true restores the pre-WP-7 LEXA 0xF0 extension byte-for-byte, for benches whose gridsim expectation has not been updated in the same session (configs/northbound.json ships true for exactly that reason — MTR-4 paired-change discipline)". (2) The key is live, not inert: cmd/northbound/main.go:228 `respTracker.SetLegacyCannotComplyCode(cfg.LegacyCannotComplyCode)`; internal/northbound/responses/tracker.go:158-163 confirms false is the code default. (3) The gridsim precondition IS satisfied in committed code: csip-tls-test commit 89c4f01 "feat(gridsim,tlsserver): ... Table27 acceptance ..."; sim/gridsim/server.go:1041 ("Table 27 CannotComply-family codes the hub now sends by default") and classifyResponseStatus returns VocabTable27 for 8/10/252/253/254, pinned by sim/gridsim/cannotcomply_test.go:33-40; `git status --short sim/gridsim/` is clean. (4) The deploy path installs exactly this file, always overwriting: scripts/deploy-hub-pi.sh:354 `install -m 644 $D/configs/hub.json $D/configs/northbound.json ... /etc/lexa/` under the comment "The six services' configs are always overwritten from the repo's example". (5) The bench device currently runs false per the session report §11 (line 293: "legacy_cannotcomply_code | northbound.json | false | product default (Table 27)") — inferred from the report, not ssh-verified (read-only mandate), but corroborated by the cannotcomply-table27 scenario's §12 config-dependency row (line 312: needs `legacy_cannotcomply_code:false`) and the scenario having executed against Table-27 acceptance. (6) The regression is real and would be QA-visible, not silent: csip-tls-test/cmd/dashboard/mayhem_reporting.go:707-718 fails the scenario with "hub posted the legacy 0xF0 CannotComply extension (%d of %d alerts), not IEEE 2030.5 Table 27" if any alert records vocab=legacy — so a plain redeploy flips cannotcomply-table27 from its pinned DEGRADED-by-design to FAIL, and the hub's northbound wire behavior regresses to the retired nonstandard 0xF0 codes (interop bug #6). Additional aggravating fact the original finding missed: the same file feeds the PRODUCT install path — Makefile:128-133 `install-configs` copies configs/*.json (no-overwrite), so a fresh product install also lands legacy=true, contradicting CLAUDE.md's "product default is byte-identical / Table 27 by default" posture. Note configs/factory/northbound.json omits the key entirely (grep empty) and is therefore already correct — but it is not what deploy-hub-pi.sh:354 or install-configs installs.

**Verifier corrections:** Root cause and fix are essentially right; two completions. (a) The one-line flip (configs/northbound.json `legacy_cannotcomply_code` → false, or delete the key — the field is `omitempty` with zero-value false, and configs/factory/northbound.json already demonstrates key-omission is the clean form) should be accompanied in the SAME commit by updating the now-stale CLAUDE.md flag-table footnote ("*bench config ships true until gridsim flips — MTR-4 paired change") and the stale pairing rationale in cmd/northbound/config.go:110-113, otherwise the docs re-assert the condition that just got fixed. (b) Severity nuance: gridsim's classifyResponseStatus accepts BOTH vocabularies (legacy 0xF0-0xFF AND Table 27), so a redeploy does not blind alert recording and the mayhem oracle would loudly FAIL cannotcomply-table27 rather than certify a broken hub — the defect is a conformance regression on the wire (retired nonstandard codes) plus a deploy/QA whiplash, which supports high (conformance defect), not critical. The finding's scope was also slightly understated: the exposure includes fresh product installs via `make install-configs` (Makefile:128-133), not only bench redeploys via deploy-hub-pi.sh:354.

### DRIFT-2 [medium/process/confidence=high]
**A plain redeploy wipes six bench-critical config values, silently breaking the demo, the QA metric oracles, and the mqttproxy fault seam**

**Evidence:** grep of deploy-hub-pi.sh for 'metrics_addr|engine_interval|plan_stall|discovery' returns ZERO hits — the script installs repo configs at :354 (`install -m 644 $D/configs/hub.json ...northbound...modbus...ocpp...telemetry...api.json /etc/lexa/`) and re-patches ONLY mqtt_user/mqtt_pass_file (:417-430), api listen_addr/token/bench (:500-531), and ocpp SP2-or-bench fields (:548-603). Shipped values a redeploy restores: configs/hub.json:7 `"metrics_addr": ""` (⇒127.0.0.1, dashboard scrape-dark), :8 `"engine_interval_s": 15`; configs/northbound.json:13 `"discovery_interval_s": 20`; configs/modbus.json:8 `"poll_interval_s": 10`, :12 `"adv": "off"`; configs/hub.json:12 `"advanced_der": "off"`, :10 `"enforce_aus_limits": false`; all configs `"mqtt_broker": "tcp://localhost:1883"` vs the dev kit's live `tcp://localhost:1882` mqttproxy interposition (DEVKIT.md:62-63: 'all /etc/lexa/*.json point mqtt_broker at tcp://localhost:1882 ... metrics_addr rewritten to 69.0.0.2'). The report's §3 claim ('deploy-hub-pi.sh should set this per CLAUDE.md's bench pattern — the surgical deploy missed it') is verified but UNDERSTATED: the script has no metrics_addr support at all, so a full scripted deploy would also wipe it.

**Root cause:** The bench profile (metrics 0.0.0.0, proxy broker port, FAST timing, demo flags) lives only as hand-edits on the device; the deploy script's patch stage covers security keys only.

**Proposed fix:** See DRIFT-7 ranked plan: committed bench-profile overlay applied by the deploy script + a drift-check script.

**Blast radius:** Post-redeploy: dashboard metric scrapes fail (every metric-corroborated mayhem oracle degrades — exactly the failure mode the session hit), mqtt-chaos fault injection silently bypassed, Bench Replay pacing broken (stock 15s engine can't keep up with 8s replay ticks), demo Volt-VAr/adv authoring dead.

### DRIFT-4 [medium/process/confidence=high]
**All campaign work is local-only: 33 lexa-hub + 32 csip-tls-test commits unpushed, the pinned lexa-proto SHA 60bdb1b exists on no remote, and the QA report is untracked — CI has never run on any of it**

**Evidence:** lexa-hub: `git branch -r` shows only origin/HEAD and origin/main — branch standards-buildout (33 commits ahead of local main, verified `git log main..standards-buildout | wc -l` = 33) was never pushed; `git status` shows only untracked docs/QA_SESSION_REPORT_2026-07-16.md. csip-tls-test: origin has only main + docs/engineering-handbook; feat/dashboard-v2 is 32 commits ahead of main, unpushed. lexa-proto: HAS a remote now (github.com/dsizzle83/lexa-proto — note CLAUDE.md/AD-003(c) 'no hosted remote yet' is stale) but local main is 2 commits ahead of origin/main, and those 2 (b6d5bb0, 60bdb1b) include the SHA both consumers pin in proto.pin. CI is PR-gated (.github/workflows/ci.yml 'on every PR'), so vet/-race/cgo-build and the proto-pin job (ci.yml:372-390) have never executed on any session commit. Lockstep itself is INTACT: both repos' proto.pin = 60bdb1b087e7... (verified byte-identical) and the two session commits touch only cmd/modbus/reconcile_adv{,_test}.go and internal/orchestrator/optimizer{,_rules_test}.go (git show --stat verified) — no proto.pin/vendor changes, so the gate would pass.

**Root cause:** Feature-branch workflow with no push discipline during a long overnight session; lexa-proto's remote was created after AD-003(c) was written but the push habit never followed.

**Proposed fix:** Before any further work: push standards-buildout, feat/dashboard-v2, and lexa-proto main to origin; `git add docs/QA_SESSION_REPORT_2026-07-16.md` and commit; open the two PRs so CI (including proto-pin) actually runs. Note lexa-hub's proto-pin job needs the CSIP_TLS_TEST_RO_TOKEN secret (check-proto-pin.sh header says 'not yet created' — unverifiable locally; expect a checkout-step failure, not a pin mismatch).

**Blast radius:** Single-disk point of failure for ~65 commits of product+bench work including two live-deployed safety fixes; the deployed binaries on 69.0.0.2 are built from commits no remote can reproduce; the vendored proto tree preserves content but not the pinned commit identity.

### DRIFT-5 [medium/test-blindspot/confidence=high]
**mayhem.py (the runner the playbook and the overnight soak used) has no FAST-timing precondition; only mayhem-campaign.sh verifies engine_interval_s**

**Evidence:** mayhem-campaign.sh:111-164 reads /etc/lexa/hub.json engine_interval_s over SSH and aborts on mismatch ('error: hub.json engine_interval_s=$GOT after requesting $MODE (expected $WANT) — aborting campaign'). scripts/mayhem.py has no equivalent (grep for engine_interval/fast returns only a help-text mention at :268). Scenario calibration assumes FAST: mayhem_world.go:1620-1627 'a ~4 s half-cycle — comfortably under exportBreachTicks(3) * tunedTickInterval(3s) ≈ 9 s FAST'. Report §10's operational playbook instructs running mayhem.py directly. Mitigating: the hub itself rescales its counters (optimizer.go:279-296 scaleTicks preserves wall-clock holds, floor 2), and the dither math stays safe at STOCK (45s ≫ 4s), so a stock-timed run skews reaction-time expectations inside fixed HoldS windows (spurious FAIL/INCONCLUSIVE) rather than false-PASSing.

**Root cause:** The precondition check was built into the release-gate wrapper but not the day-to-day runner; FAST timing is assumed ambient bench state.

**Proposed fix:** Port mayhem-campaign.sh's read_engine_interval check into mayhem.py (or the dashboard's run-start handler): refuse to start unless engine_interval_s matches the requested profile, printing which profile is live.

**Blast radius:** A silent timing regression (e.g. any redeploy per DRIFT-2) makes an entire mayhem.py campaign's verdicts untrustworthy in the noisy direction — wasted soak hours and false hub-bug reports, not false certification.

### DRIFT-6 [medium/test-blindspot/confidence=high]
**Bench state masks product defaults: the entire QA campaign and demo run only under hand-set flags (advanced_der:on, reconciler.adv:active, enforce_aus_limits:true, metrics 0.0.0.0) and at the FAST cadence the guards were tuned at — product-default, STOCK-cadence behavior is largely unexercised**

**Evidence:** Shipped defaults are all fail-closed: hub.json:10 enforce_aus_limits:false, :12 advanced_der:"off", modbus.json:12 adv:"off", metrics loopback. Report §11 confirms the bench carries the opposite of each. optimizer.go:246-250: 'tunedTickInterval is the engine cadence the *BreachTicks constants were calibrated at (the FAST replay/QA tick)' = 3s; product default engine_interval_s=15 exercises the scaleTicks floor-2 rescale path (optimizer.go:285-296) that no soak scenario ran. The boundary-dither findings B/D (report §7/§8) were all observed at FAST only. Additionally enforce_aus_limits:true was left ON (report §11: 'revert to false for the pre-campaign default'), drifting the bench from its own baseline.

**Root cause:** Campaign flags were flipped by hand per scenario and left standing; no STOCK-cadence pass was in the soak plan (mayhem-campaign.sh --stock exists for release gates but wasn't run).

**Proposed fix:** Revert enforce_aus_limits to false on the bench now (per the report's own note); make aus/adv scenario setup/teardown own their flag flips; schedule one STOCK-cadence mayhem-campaign.sh pass as part of the B/D hardening verification.

**Blast radius:** A demo rehearsed on this bench (Volt-VAr, AUS caps, metric panels) goes dark on any product-default deploy — by design, but nobody's tracking which demo features depend on which hand-set flag. Guard chatter at the 15s cadence (different leaky-counter granularity) is uncharacterized even as findings B/D get fixed against 3s behavior.

### DRIFT-7 [medium/process/confidence=high]
**Durable config-management fix (ranked): commit the Table-27 flip, add a committed bench profile to the deploy path, add a drift check wired into bench-up.sh and mayhem preconditions**

**Evidence:** Synthesis of DRIFT-1/2/3/5. The deploy script already has the exact mechanism needed — the post-install python patch stage (deploy-hub-pi.sh:417-430 mqtt creds, :500-531 api, :563-599 ocpp) — it just doesn't cover the bench keys; CLAUDE.md 05 §6 discipline ('the in-repo default stays conservative and the flip is a deliberate, binary-only deploy + hand-set Pi config') was written for ONE key (reconciler.battery) and has silently scaled to ~8 hand-set keys across 6 files plus timing, which is past the point where hand-edits are auditable.

**Root cause:** Bench-vs-product divergence grew key-by-key with no owning artifact.

**Proposed fix:** Ranked: (1) Commit configs/northbound.json legacy_cannotcomply_code:false NOW (DRIFT-3; precondition already satisfied in committed gridsim). (2) Add a committed bench overlay — e.g. configs/bench/overlay.json listing {hub: {metrics_addr, advanced_der:"on"}, modbus: {metrics_addr, reconciler.adv:"active", mqtt_broker proxy port on the devkit}, northbound/ocpp/telemetry: {metrics_addr}} — applied by a new `--bench-profile` patch stage in deploy-hub-pi.sh (and a devkit-safe variant per DRIFT-1). Keep FAST timing OUT of the overlay (it stays hub-replay-tune.sh's job — it's a mode, not a profile) and keep enforce_aus_limits/registration_pin/port_16/pairing_mode scenario-scoped, never standing. (3) Add scripts/check-bench-drift.sh (csip-tls-test): ssh-dump /etc/lexa/*.json, normalize (strip deploy-patched secrets/creds), diff against repo config + overlay, print unexpected keys; call it from bench-up.sh's verify step and as mayhem.py's run precondition alongside the DRIFT-5 timing check. (4) Update CLAUDE.md's deploy sentence and the 05 §6 discipline text to name the overlay as the single source of bench truth.

**Blast radius:** Every future deploy/QA session repeats this session's §3 rediscovery loop.

CLAUDE.md: 'hub-pi dhpi4 at 69.0.0.1 is STANDBY (lexa services stopped+disabled) — do not deploy there without deliberately deciding to move the hub.' bench-up.sh:36 correctly defaults HUB=69.0.0.2/root and passes it through (:45, :141), so the scripted path is safe; only direct invocation without args hits the stale default.

**Evidence:** (a) Both repos' proto.pin = 60bdb1b087e7bc694e4cabf93919aa5b7a6f04b4 (byte-identical, read both); git show --stat of 29e9552 (cmd/modbus/reconcile_adv.go + test) and e0864c9 (internal/orchestrator/optimizer.go + test) confirms neither touches proto.pin or vendor/lexa-proto — no paired-PR obligation triggered; check-proto-pin.sh (a) pin-vs-pin would pass. **Proposed fix:** Optional: fix the config.go:74 doc-comment typo ('5 × 15 s FAST' → '5 × 3 s FAST'); update CLAUDE.md's stale 'lexa-proto has no hosted remote yet' (AD-003(c)) — github.com/dsizzle83/lexa-proto exists.
