## Probe: dashboard-app-state

**Probe summary:** Audited the csip-tls-test dashboard QA application (cmd/dashboard, branch feat/dashboard-v2, clean tree, 32 commits ahead of main) against the five probe items, reading mayhem_adv.go (all 1320 lines), mayhem.go (run lifecycle, baseline, sampling, verdict machinery), mqtt_scenarios.go metric diagnosers, mayhem_world.go SSH helpers, scripts/mayhem.py, the React UI health surface, docs/DASHBOARD_V2_PLAN.md, and the lexa-hub bus/reconciler types the adv oracles depend on. The session report's §10 recommendation is confirmed and feasible: MRID is present end-to-end (bus.ReconcileReport.MRID is populated by both adv-shell publish paths, and every injected desired doc carries a unique per-run mrid) but the oracle's advReportMsg deliberately does not decode it, so the retained per-device report topic can silently certify a broken hub from a stale prior-run report — the most serious finding here. Metrics-scrape failure is handled without ever conflating into FAIL (verified across four diagnosers) but the folding is inconsistent (DEGRADED vs PASS-with-note vs note-only) and carries no machine-readable INFRA marker, which is exactly why the loopback metrics_addr misconfiguration read as product degradation. The 409 "run in progress" stranding is precisely explained: mayhem.py handles only SIGINT, `timeout`-kill sends SIGTERM, so the abort is never posted; the server run itself is fire-and-forget by design and finishes eventually — except that the SSH helpers use exec.Command with no execution deadline, so a hung remote command can wedge Running=true unrecoverably (abort can't reach it). Per-sim health exists only as a browser-side dot row (HealthDots.tsx); neither the runner nor the engine has a programmatic health gate, so the modsim-500 class surfaces only post-hoc as BLIND/spurious verdicts. DASHBOARD_V2_PLAN phases 2-3 are fully committed, phase 4 is half-committed (gridsim dynamic tariff yes; Replay V2 no — replayRate and the hardcoded 2026-06-01 epoch survive in replay.go); nothing is uncommitted, and the memory index's "phases 2-4 pending/uncommitted" line is stale.

### DASH-1 [high/test-blindspot/confidence=high] — **verifier: PARTLY**
**Adv oracles read the retained per-device reconcile report without mrid (or ts) matching — a stale report from a prior scenario/run can falsely PASS a regressed hub**

**Evidence:** cmd/dashboard/mayhem_adv.go:424-432 — advReportMsg decodes only {Kind, DeviceClass, DeviceID, Axis, AdoptState, CurveHash, Ts}; no MRID field, and Ts is decoded but never compared to scenario start. mayhem_adv.go:786-789 is the ONLY pollution defense: `if report.Axis != wantAxis { f.Verdict = "INCONCLUSIVE" ... "the report is retained per DEVICE, not per axis" }` — it cannot distinguish this run's fixed_pf report from last run's fixed_pf report. mayhem_adv.go:466-483 advReportWithRetry returns the FIRST present read (`if ok && present { return msg, true, nil }`), so a lingering retained report is accepted instantly even if the real report lands seconds later. MRID is available end-to-end, verified in lexa-hub: internal/bus/messages.go:182 `MRID string \`json:"mrid,omitempty\"`` on ReconcileReport; cmd/modbus/reconcile_adv.go:1776 `MRID: rep.MRID` (observe path) and :1798 `MRID: s.docMRID` (publishReportLocked), fed from the desired doc at :1109 `s.docMRID, s.docSeq, s.docIssuedAt = doc.MRID, ...`. The injected docs already carry unique mrids: mayhem_adv.go:744 `mrid := fmt.Sprintf("mayhem-curve-lies-%d", time.Now().UnixNano())` and :877 (pf). Concrete false-PASS: run pf-var-measured-convergence once against a correct hub → retained report {axis:fixed_pf, adopt_state:diverged}; re-run against a hub whose adv shell silently drops the doc (e.g. lexa-modbus adv reconciler off/crashed after the SSH precondition probe, or the doc superseded by WP-9) → teardown reads the STALE diverged report → PASS at mayhem_adv.go:954-960 certifying a hub that never even processed the command.

**Root cause:** advReportMsg was scoped to the fields the axis-check needed; the report's mrid (present on the wire since WP-10) was never threaded into the oracle, and the retry loop treats 'present' as 'fresh'.

**Proposed fix:** 1) Add `MRID string `json:"mrid"`` to advReportMsg (mayhem_adv.go:424). 2) Hoist the injected mrid out of setup into the scenario closure and pass it through to the diagnosers. 3) In advReportWithRetry, treat present-but-mrid-mismatch the same as not-present (keep polling — the fresh report may still land), and on exhaustion return the mismatched report so the diagnoser can emit INCONCLUSIVE 'retained report is for a different command (mrid X, wanted Y) — WP-9 authorship or a previous scenario's retained report'. 4) Keep the axis check as a secondary guard. This makes the §10 'run individually + clear topics' convention unnecessary for correctness (though still good hygiene).

**Blast radius:** All three adv-isolation scenarios (adv-shadow-no-writes indirectly, curve-adopt-readback-divergence, pf-var-measured-convergence). These gate INV-ADV-READBACK — the 'trust measurement, not the handshake' safety discipline for advanced-DER provisioning. The QA report §10 already flags this operationally ('clear adv topics between runs'), which is a manual convention, not a guard.

**Verifier reasoning:** Core defect VERIFIED IN CODE. (1) csip-tls-test/cmd/dashboard/mayhem_adv.go:424-432 — advReportMsg is exactly {Kind, DeviceClass, DeviceID, Axis, AdoptState, CurveHash, Ts}; no MRID, and report.Ts is never referenced in either diagnoser (read lines 771-985 in full). (2) mayhem_adv.go:470-471 — advReportWithRetry: `if ok && present { return msg, true, nil }` — first retained read accepted as fresh. (3) mayhem_adv.go:786-790 / 929-932 — the axis check is the sole pollution guard; it cannot distinguish runs. (4) MRID is on the wire end-to-end: lexa-hub/internal/bus/messages.go:182 (`MRID string json:"mrid,omitempty"` on ReconcileReport), cmd/modbus/reconcile_adv.go:1776 (`MRID: rep.MRID`), :1798 (`MRID: s.docMRID`), :1109 (docMRID set from doc.MRID); injected docs carry unique mrids (mayhem_adv.go:744, 877). (5) No retained-topic hygiene between scenarios: mayhem.go:2727-2744 resetForScenario clears sim faults/controls only. (6) The session's own report already concedes the gap (docs/QA_SESSION_REPORT_2026-07-16.md:275 recommends exactly this mrid-matching hardening) — the finding is real but restates a documented known gap with sharper mechanics. REFUTED DETAIL: the concrete false-PASS repro ("run once against a correct hub, re-run against a broken one → PASS") is wrong as stated. Teardown publishes a release doc AFTER reading the report (mayhem_adv.go:757-758, 898-899); a correct hub's shell processes it and executeReleaseLocked → transitionLocked(rn, "", now) (cmd/modbus/reconcile_adv.go:1497-1503) republishes the retained report with adopt_state:"" and mrid:"" (desiredAdvReleasePayload, mayhem_adv.go:412-418, has no mrid field). So a cleanly-completed prior run leaves a RELEASE report retained, and the broken-hub re-run produces a false FAIL in the pf diagnoser (mayhem_adv.go:945 `case "adopted", "":` lumps "" with adopted — misleading diagnosis, but a failing verdict) or INCONCLUSIVE in the curve diagnoser (default arm) — not PASS.

**Verifier corrections:** The blindspot and fix are real; the repro needs a precondition the original finding omitted: the prior run's diverged report survives only if the teardown release never took effect — (a) dashboard process killed mid-hold (teardown at mayhem.go:546-547 runs only if the process lives; setup-failure and abort paths do run it), (b) the teardown mqttInject error is silently discarded (`_ = d.mqttInject(...)` at mayhem_adv.go:758/899 — an SSH blip loses the release with no trace), or (c) lexa-modbus/adv shell dies after publishing diverged but before processing the release. Case (c) coincides exactly with the "regressed hub" the oracle exists to catch, so a false PASS is genuinely reachable and severity=high stands — it is just narrower than claimed; the COMMON stale-report outcome is a false FAIL (pf, with a misleading "reported adopted/converged" headline) or INCONCLUSIVE (curve), i.e. wrong-diagnosis noise rather than false certification. The proposed 4-part fix is correct and has a bonus: because release reports carry mrid:"", mrid-matching also eliminates the false-FAIL path (the "" release remnant becomes a mismatch → INCONCLUSIVE instead of falling into the pf diagnoser's `"adopted", ""` FAIL arm). One addition: the fix should keep treating adopt_state:"" as distinct from "adopted" in diagnosePFVarMeasuredConvergence regardless, since a same-run WP-9-authored release could in principle produce it too.

### DASH-2 [medium/design-flaw/confidence=high]
**Metrics-scrape failure never becomes FAIL (verified) but is folded inconsistently across oracles and carries no machine-readable INFRA marker**

**Evidence:** Four distinct treatments, all read in code: (a) diagnoseAdvShadowNoWrites, mayhem_adv.go:674-681 — `if !metricsAvail { f.Verdict = "DEGRADED"; f.Headline = "zero writes landed (ground truth), but lexa-modbus's :9103 metrics were unavailable — cannot corroborate..." }` — infra failure DEGRADES the verdict. (b) diagnosePFVarMeasuredConvergence, mayhem_adv.go:939-941 — unavailable metric becomes a prose note (`"lexa_mb_adv_divergences_total unavailable (metrics scrape failed)"`), verdict unchanged; but a metric that IS available and contradicts the report downgrades PASS→DEGRADED (:961-965) — reasonable asymmetry. (c) diagnoseDuplicateClientID, mqtt_scenarios.go:430-433 — `case !counterOK: detectionLine = "detection INCONCLUSIVE: lexa_mqtt_reconnects_total not available..."` and the verdict switch's `case counterOK && !detectionRose:` DEGRADED branch is skipped when !counterOK, so scrape failure lands in the default PASS branch — scrape-dead is judged MORE leniently than scrape-alive-but-flat. (d) diagnoseMqttStorm, mqtt_scenarios.go:497-501 — note only, and the silent-wedge FAIL escalation is explicitly `counterOK && ...` gated. Verdict vocabulary (mayhem.go:159 `PASS|DEGRADED|FAIL|BLIND|INCONCLUSIVE`) has no infra/DEGRADED-cause distinction, and mayFinding carries no structured field for it (only Metrics.HubBlind for sim-probe blindness). This is why the §3 loopback-metrics_addr misconfiguration presented as scenario degradation (adv-shadow-no-writes DEGRADED→PASS after the config fix) — the summary counts cannot distinguish 'hub imperfect' from 'bench couldn't see'.

**Root cause:** Each oracle invented its own scrape-failure policy; there is no shared convention or structured marker for 'secondary evidence unavailable'.

**Proposed fix:** Add a structured field to mayFinding, e.g. `EvidenceGaps []string` or `Infra bool`, set whenever a secondary probe (metrics scrape, SSH read) was unavailable; adopt one convention: ground-truth invariant held + corroboration unavailable ⇒ PASS (or DEGRADED) WITH the gap recorded, and surface a per-run 'evidence gaps' rollup in the final report so a bench-wide scrape failure (the metrics_addr class) is one loud line instead of N quiet DEGRADEDs. Also consider a run-start preflight scrape of the five :910x endpoints in baseline() that logs a single warning.

**Blast radius:** Every metric-corroborated oracle (adv-shadow, pf, aus-*, duplicate-client-id, mqtt-storm, shadow-divergence notes). Operators triaging a campaign summary see DEGRADED counts and cannot programmatically attribute them to bench misconfiguration; conversely duplicate-client-id's PASS-when-scrape-dead slightly overstates coverage.

### DASH-3 [medium/process/confidence=high]
**409 'run already in progress' after a client timeout-kill: mayhem.py aborts only on SIGINT; `timeout` sends SIGTERM, so the abort is never posted**

**Evidence:** scripts/mayhem.py:171-185 — the follow loop's only cleanup path is `except KeyboardInterrupt: ... api(base, "/api/qa/abort", method="POST")`; grep shows no `import signal`/`signal.signal` anywhere in the 294-line file, so SIGTERM (what coreutils `timeout` sends by default) kills the process with no abort posted. Server side, mayhem.go:374-379 — `if d.status.Running { http.Error(w, "a mayhem run is already in progress", http.StatusConflict) }` — and the run is deliberately detached (mayhem.go:391 `go d.runGuarded(...)`; DASHBOARD_V2_PLAN.md Part 1 explicitly preserves 'server-side long-running drivers that survive tab close'). So the report §10's 'strands the engine' is slightly overstated: the run is not wedged, it keeps executing (for a >2h full suite) and finish()/restoreBench() eventually clear it — but every start in the interim 409s, and there is no lease/heartbeat/takeover mechanism. handleAbort (mayhem.go:459-471) works and is honored within one sample interval (holdAndSample's select on ctx.Done, mayhem.go:631-635) or between scenarios (mayhem.go:485-490), with WS-3 forcing aborted-mid-scenario findings INCONCLUSIVE (mayhem.go:556-571 — verified correct).

**Root cause:** Client-side signal-handling gap plus an intentionally fire-and-forget server run with no takeover path.

**Proposed fix:** Smallest robust fix, two halves: (1) mayhem.py: `signal.signal(signal.SIGTERM, lambda *a: (_ for _ in ()).throw(KeyboardInterrupt))` (or an atexit/finally that posts abort when a run this invocation started is still running) — 3 lines, converts timeout-kill into the existing Ctrl-C path. (2) Optionally server-side: accept `{"takeover": true}` on POST /api/qa/start that calls the existing cancel, waits (bounded, e.g. 2× sample interval + teardown allowance) for Running=false, then proceeds — reusing handleAbort's machinery. A dead-client lease/auto-abort is NOT recommended: detached multi-hour soaks with no poller are a supported, deliberate usage (the ~11h soak relied on it).

**Blast radius:** Operational only: lost bench time and operator confusion during campaigns (cost the QA session 'one early mis-read' per its own report). No verdict corruption — WS-3 abort handling is sound.

### DASH-4 [medium/bug/confidence=high]
**SSH helpers have no execution deadline — a hung remote command in setup/teardown blocks the run goroutine where ctx is never checked, wedging Running=true beyond abort's reach**

**Evidence:** mayhem_world.go:122-126 and :141-145 — both hubSSH and hubSSHOutput use `exec.Command("ssh", "-o", "BatchMode=yes", "-o", "ConnectTimeout=4", target, command)` with `cmd.CombinedOutput()`/`cmd.Output()`: ConnectTimeout bounds only the TCP/auth handshake, not remote command execution. Some remote commands self-bound (advReconcileReportCommand wraps `timeout 4 mosquitto_sub`, mayhem_adv.go:437-441) but others do not (config greps at mayhem_adv.go:147/189/214, journal reads in intent_scenarios.go:222-240, netem commands in mayhem_world.go). The run loop consults ctx only in holdAndSample (mayhem.go:631-635) and between scenarios (mayhem.go:485-490); sc.setup/sc.teardown calls (mayhem.go:511, :547) are synchronous with no context, so a hub Pi that accepts the SSH connection but wedges mid-command (D-state, disk full, journald hang) blocks the run goroutine indefinitely: Running stays true, POST /api/qa/abort cancels a context nobody is watching, and only a dashboard-process restart clears the 409. Contrast: all driver HTTP calls are bounded (`client: &http.Client{Timeout: 3 * time.Second, ...}`, mayhem.go:238). This is the one genuine 'stranded engine' mechanism behind the report's 409 complaint (distinct from DASH-3's benign still-running case).

**Root cause:** exec.Command instead of exec.CommandContext; no per-call wall-clock bound on remote execution.

**Proposed fix:** Give hubSSH/hubSSHOutput/nodeSSHOutput a bounded context: `ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(context.Background(), 30*time.Second); exec.CommandContext(ctx, "ssh", ...)` (CommandContext kills the ssh process on expiry). ~6 lines across mayhem_world.go and mayhem_ocpp_openadr.go:887; callers already handle errors as INCONCLUSIVE/soft-proceed, so no oracle changes needed.

**Blast radius:** Any scenario using SSH probes/readbacks (adv preconditions, retained-topic reads, journal oracles, netem, pin/pairing config probes) can permanently strand the QA engine on a sick bench host — the exact situation a hostile-QA campaign creates.

### DASH-5 [medium/infra/confidence=high]
**Per-sim health exists only as a browser-side dot row; no programmatic endpoint or engine pre-flight — the modsim-500 class surfaces only post-hoc as BLIND/spurious verdicts**

**Evidence:** The UI has real per-sim health: cmd/dashboard/ui/src/components/HealthDots.tsx:13-20 probes hub /healthz, gridsim /admin/status, and all four sims' /state every 5 s, green on 2xx (ui/src/lib/api.ts:103-115 probeHealth returns `res.ok`) — a modsim returning HTTP 500 on /state shows a red dot. But it is computed in the browser; there is no server-side aggregate route (main.go:100-161 lists every route: proxies, /api/logs/all, /api/replay/*, /api/qa/* — no health endpoint), so scripts/mayhem.py and any automation must hand-roll per-sim curls (exactly what the QA report §10 prescribes: `curl ... http://69.0.0.10:6020/state`). The mayhem engine itself checks sims only once per RUN in baseline() (mayhem.go:2650-2680, fails the whole run if solar/meter /control error) and then relies on per-sample OK flags (getJSON returns error on >=300, mayhem.go:2361-2379; sample() sets SolarOK etc. only on success, mayhem.go:763) feeding the WS-3 BLIND machinery (mayhem_probeavail_test.go pins mostly-dead-judging-sensor ⇒ BLIND, never PASS — verified sound). So a sim that dies mid-campaign (finding E: /state=500 while systemd shows active) produces BLINDs and sim-induced FAILs attributed to scenarios, with nothing a runner can consult between batches.

**Root cause:** Health probing was built as a UI shell concern (HealthDots comment: 'kept here, not lib/'); no API-first equivalent, and resetForScenario does no health gate.

**Proposed fix:** Add GET /api/qa/benchhealth to the dashboard: server-side probe of the same six targets HealthDots uses (reuse d.backends + d.client with its 3 s timeout), returning {target: {ok, http_status, latency_ms}}. Consume it in three places: (1) scripts/mayhem.py prints it before start and between --only batches, refusing to start (or warning loudly) on a red sim; (2) resetForScenario records a pre-fault health snapshot and stamps findings whose judging sim was already unhealthy at scenario START with an evidence-gap marker (ties into DASH-2's structured field) so sim-death FAILs are attributable; (3) HealthDots switches to polling the new endpoint, deleting the browser-side fan-out.

**Blast radius:** Campaign signal quality: the ~11h soak's late-cycle noise (report §6) and the finding-E spurious FAILs are exactly this gap; an operatorless soak cannot self-detect a degraded bench.

### DASH-6 [info/process/confidence=high]
**DASHBOARD_V2_PLAN phases 2-3 fully committed; phase 4 half-done (gridsim tariff yes, Replay V2 no); nothing uncommitted; memory index line is stale**

**Evidence:** git status on feat/dashboard-v2 is clean; branch is 32 commits ahead of main (unmerged). DASHBOARD_V2_PLAN.md phase status verified against the tree: Phase 2 (UI platform + Live Ops core) — committed: ui/ Vite+React+TS with views Ops/Bench/Logs/Proof/Studio, dist/ committed (git ls-files cmd/dashboard/ui/dist shows assets), Live Ops commit 49e1283. Phase 3 (Savings Studio) — committed: c4d7b75 'Savings Studio — the money view', internal/tariff + internal/whatif + internal/scenariodata + data/{tariffs,scenarios} all present, whatif API da0905b. Phase 4 (Protocol truth + Replay V2) — PARTIAL: gridsim dynamic tariff committed (e517a21, sim/gridsim/pricing_dynamic.go serves POST/GET/DELETE /admin/tariff, wired at admin.go:23), but the Replay V2 half is NOT built: replay.go:44 still defines `func replayRate(hour float64)` (the plan's 'delete the three duplicated price definitions' exit criterion), replay.go:244-246 still hardcodes `simEpoch := time.Date(2026, 6, 1, ..., time.Local)` (no configurable epoch/TZ), and no scenario-ref consumption exists in replay.go. The cross-repo 'hub prices from walked CSIP tariff' gate appears resolved in the hub's favor per the demo-buildout memory (hub defers to retained lexa/csip/pricing via D9 precedence) but was not re-verified in lexa-hub code this audit. Separately, the demo-buildout campaign's phases (the memory-index reading of 'phases 2-4'): Phase 1 committed 914c666, Phase 2 injection console committed a4ff1bf (ui/src/views/ops/ScenarioConsole.tsx), Phase 3 VAr+OpenADR committed 85e1fb5, Phase 4 QA fixes committed fbcaca0 + 3e907f2 — so MEMORY.md's index line 'Phases 2/3/4 pending; changes uncommitted' is stale (the memory file body itself is current and says P2/P3 committed).

**Root cause:** Plan/memory docs lag the branch; the QA campaign consumed the sessions that would have finished Replay V2.

**Proposed fix:** Update the MEMORY.md index line; treat Replay V2 (scenario refs, epoch/TZ, tariff-engine costing, replayRate deletion) as the open remainder of Phase 4 before any demo that loads a dynamic tariff while using Bench Replay.

**Blast radius:** Planning only. Risk worth naming: replay's hardcoded tariff (replayRate) now DISAGREES with gridsim's dynamic /admin/tariff when one is loaded — the exact three-definitions drift the plan's Phase 4 was written to kill.

### DASH-7 [info/ok-verified/confidence=high]
**Verified correct: mrid feasibility end-to-end, session commits, abort-mid-scenario integrity, probe-availability BLIND machinery, aus-load-cap oracle fix**

**Evidence:** (1) MRID end-to-end: bus.ReconcileReport.MRID (lexa-hub internal/bus/messages.go:182) populated on both adv-shell publish paths (cmd/modbus/reconcile_adv.go:1776, :1798 from s.docMRID set at :1109); injected docs stamp unique mrids (mayhem_adv.go:390 `"mrid":%q` in desiredAdvVoltVarPayload, :744/:877 nano-timestamped) — the report §10 recommendation is implementable with no hub-side change. (2) All four claimed session commits exist on the stated branches: lexa-hub 29e9552/e0864c9 (git log head of standards-buildout), csip-tls-test fbcaca0/3e907f2 (head of feat/dashboard-v2); trees clean. (3) The fbcaca0 oracle fix is sound as committed: diagnoseAusCap (mayhem_adv.go:1125-1218) threads cannotComplyLegit, PASSes load-cap CannotComply-for-unmeetable (:1200-1207), keeps gen-cap DEGRADED (:1208-1211), and keeps silent-breach FAIL for both (:1212-1215) — matching the scenario's own Expected text (:1236). (4) WS-3 abort integrity verified: an abort mid-scenario forces the partial-window verdict to INCONCLUSIVE with an 'aborted mid-scenario' marker (mayhem.go:556-571), and runGuarded's recover keeps a diagnoser panic from killing the server while restoreBench still fires (mayhem.go:396-417). (5) The vacuous-PASS gap is closed and pinned: dead judging sensor ⇒ BLIND never PASS (mayhem_probeavail_test.go TestDiagnoseConstraint_DeadSolarProbeForcesBlind et al.), which is the machinery that correctly caught the modsim-500 class as BLIND rather than PASS during the soak.

**Root cause:** n/a — verification record

**Proposed fix:** n/a

**Blast radius:** n/a

---

## Completeness critic

**Summary:** Completeness audit of the 14-probe fan-out against the 2026-07-15/16 QA session. I read the full session report, the 101-scenario inventory (all-scenario-ids.txt) and soak batch files, the raw health-logger and vtnsim artifacts, the mayhem suite's scenario/oracle sources (mayhem_ocpp_openadr.go, mayhem.go, invariants.go, gridsim), and the hub-side code for every subsystem I checked for coverage (cmd/hub/openadr_adopt.go, internal/northbound/flowres, cmd/hub/adv.go). The prior probes are deep on what they covered but the fan-out has systematic blind spots in all four requested dimensions. (a) The two hub commits were verified under mutually exclusive bench configs (§12 forces advanced_der:off for the PF fix; the export-cap fix ran under advanced_der:on) and no scenario combines a W-domain export cap with an adv reactive axis; separately, 29e9552's two-sided band mechanically increases corrective 704 RMW writes, amplifying exposure to the write704 blind-RMW corruption another probe rated critical — no probe assessed that coupling. (b) Whole services have zero verdict coverage: lexa-telemetry/MUP posting is asserted by no scenario or invariant despite gridsim serving /mup, and telemetry is not even in the soak health monitor (5 service slots); the lexa-openadr VEN, the lexa/openadr/prices topic, and both OpenADR staleness gates are bench-unexercised by documented design; flowres has no gridsim endpoint at all; no scenario exercises watchdog-triggered restart, the plan-heartbeat stalled state, api auth rejection, or cert-expiry monitoring. (c) The report's "all 7 lexa services active" bench-state claim was cross-checked by nobody and is contradicted in scope by the artifacts (5-slot health log, vtnsim bind failure, port-mismatched openadr.json). (d) Plan-forward: the QA report is untracked, all raw evidence for a critical safety finding lives under /tmp (wiped on reboot on this machine), no open finding (B/C/D/E) exists in any in-repo backlog, the bench was left with enforce_aus_limits:true against the report's own instruction, and the load-bearing pre-session proto commit 60bdb1b (chunked >125-register reads that the PF fix's model-701 measurements ride on) was audited by no probe. Overall: the 14 probes verified the session's specific claims well; what is missing is coverage of everything the campaign structurally could not see.

### CC-1 [high/test-blindspot]
**lexa-telemetry (MUP posting) has zero verdict coverage in the entire 101-scenario suite and is absent from the soak health monitor — a hub with dead utility telemetry certifies clean**

**Evidence:** Searched all 101 scenario IDs (scratchpad all-scenario-ids.txt): none reference telemetry/MUP. `grep -rn -i "mup|mirror" cmd/dashboard/mayhem*.go cmd/dashboard/invariants.go` in csip-tls-test returns only comments using the word 'mirrors' — no oracle or invariant asserts a MirrorMeterReading ever reached the utility server. Yet gridsim fully serves the flow (sim/gridsim/server.go:388-390 `case path == "/mup": s.handleMUPCreate(...)`), so an oracle is feasible today. The soak health logger tracked only 5 services: qa-bench-health.log line 2 `hub-svcs=[active active active active active ] gridsim=200 dash=200` — telemetry (and openadr) have no slot. The campaign's new telemetry flags (configs/telemetry.json post_var/post_wh, CLAUDE.md flag table) therefore shipped with no bench verification of any kind. Verified in code/artifacts.

**Proposed fix:** Add a telemetry-roundtrip scenario: sample gridsim's MUP store count before/after a hold window and FAIL if no new readings land (plus assert VAr/Wh types when post_var/post_wh are on); add telemetry (and openadr) slots to the health logger.

### CC-2 [medium/test-blindspot]
**Commits e0864c9 and 29e9552 were never validated in a shared configuration — their verification configs are mutually exclusive per the report's own §12 matrix, and no scenario combines an export cap with an adv reactive axis**

**Evidence:** QA report §12: pf-var-measured-convergence requires `advanced_der:off` and 'run individually'; §11 shows the soak/openadr scenarios ran under `advanced_der:"on"`. Report §2.2 itself concedes the PF axis is INCONCLUSIVE under advanced_der:on (WP-9's energize doc supersedes the injected fixed_pf doc). Scenario inventory (101 ids) contains no scenario asserting both an active export/OpenADR cap and a fixed-PF/var axis simultaneously. The coupling is real in the product: cmd/hub/adv.go:342-353 authors a fixed_pf desired doc whenever a CSIP control carries FixedPFInject/Absorb, so on a real site both fixes run concurrently — the W-domain plan-discharge cap (optimizer.go) and the VAr-domain PF convergence (reconcile_adv.go) — a combination that has never once been judgeable on the bench. The sim additionally does not model P/Q (kVA) coupling that would tie the domains physically (sim/southbound/solar_adv.go models 704 PF/var with measured 701 effect but no W derating). Searched-and-absent verified; the interaction defect itself is inferred, not demonstrated.

**Proposed fix:** Make the adv oracle mrid-bound (already recommended by the dashboard probe) so adv scenarios can run under advanced_der:on, then add one scenario that holds an export cap while a fixed_pf axis is in force.

### CC-3 [medium/test-blindspot]
**29e9552's two-sided band mechanically increases corrective 704 RMW write frequency, widening exposure to the write704 blind-RMW corruption the finding-E probe rated CRITICAL — no probe assessed this cross-commit coupling**

**Evidence:** Synthesis of two confirmed probe results: probe commit-29e9552 confirmed 'band-edge dither yields an immediate corrective 704 RMW write per divergence onset' (the two-sided band adds a second undamped boundary), and probe finding-E-modsim-leak confirmed (critical) that derbase write704 'blindly writes back an unvalidated read — a sentinel-saturated or torn read coinciding with any 704 write programs garbage into a REAL inverter'. The new two-sided check converts previously-converged states (measured |PF| closer to unity than commanded, e.g. commanded 0.95 / measured 0.98) into diverged verdicts that fire corrective writes on every backoff interval — strictly more 704 RMW cycles than pre-commit, hence strictly more coincidence windows with torn/sentinel reads. The bench was left with reconciler.adv:"active" (report §11), so this write-rate increase is live. Inferred from two independently code-verified findings; the amplification itself was measured by no probe and exercised by no scenario (nan-sentinel scenarios never ran concurrently with a diverged fixed_pf axis).

**Proposed fix:** Land the finding-E validate-before-write-back fix in derbase BEFORE (or with) any release containing 29e9552; add hysteresis to the two-sided band (already proposed by probe 2) to bound the write rate.

### CC-4 [medium/test-blindspot]
**lexa-openadr VEN, lexa/openadr/prices, and both OpenADR staleness gates have zero bench coverage — the scenarios bypass the service by documented design and always inject fresh, never-expiring documents**

**Evidence:** cmd/dashboard/mayhem_ocpp_openadr.go:65-88 (csip-tls-test) states the bypass explicitly: scenarios 'inject a bus.OpenADRLimits-shaped document directly onto the retained lexa/openadr/limits topic … does NOT exercise the VEN's HTTP polling, OAuth2 token flow, or CP-profile translation'. Grep confirms no scenario touches lexa/openadr/prices at all (only openADRTopicLimits, mayhem_ocpp_openadr.go:698); pricing-attack is CSIP tariff, not OpenADR (mayhem.go:2902-2907). Both injected limit payloads use fresh ts and `"valid_until":0` (mayhem_ocpp_openadr.go:718, 758), so the hub's staleness/expiry code paths — cmd/hub/openadr_adopt.go:186-192 (price stale-at-adoption skip) and :269 ('OpenADR capacity limit past valid_until — dropped') — have unit-test-only coverage. Session artifacts show the VTN half was broken during the session: vtn.log line 2 `listen tcp :26030: bind: address already in use`, and scratchpad openadr.json points vtn_url at http://69.0.0.20:6030 while vtnsim's base_url is :26030. Verified in code and artifacts.

**Proposed fix:** Script the follow-up the mayhem file itself calls for: wire vtn_url to vtnsim in a bench harness, add a stale-prices and a past-valid_until limits scenario, and reconcile the openadr.json port with vtnsim's actual listen address.

### CC-5 [medium/test-blindspot]
**Flow Reservation (§10.9, internal/northbound/flowres) has zero scenario coverage and gridsim serves no FlowReservation endpoint — the path is untestable on the bench as built**

**Evidence:** `grep -rn -i "flowres|FlowReservation" cmd/dashboard/ sim/server sim/gridsim` in csip-tls-test returns nothing; `grep -rn -i flow sim/gridsim/*.go` hits only comments about the MUP flow. The product path is real and wired unconditionally: internal/northbound/flowres/manager.go (POSTs FlowReservationRequests to the utility), constructed at cmd/northbound/main.go:229 with an MQTT subscription at main.go:319, fed by bus.FlowReservationRequestMsg on lexa/csip/flowreservation/request (internal/bus/messages.go:371-375), and included in cert-rotation (cmd/northbound/rotate.go:235 rotates the 'flow-reservation' fetcher). None of the 101 scenarios reference it, and ev-setpoint-clamp (the V2G-adjacent scenario) injects desired docs downstream of the hub, never driving an FR request. Verified absence.

**Proposed fix:** Add a gridsim FlowReservationRequest store + an FR-roundtrip scenario (hub emits request → northbound POSTs → assert arrival), or explicitly de-scope §10.9 in VERIFICATION_SWEEP with a rationale.

### CC-6 [medium/test-blindspot]
**No scenario exercises watchdog-triggered restart, the plan-heartbeat 'stalled' state, lexa-api auth rejection, or cert-EXPIRY monitoring — the liveness/authn layer of the product is judged by nothing**

**Evidence:** Searched-and-absent, each verified: (1) watchdog — `grep -rn -i "watchdog|SIGSTOP|sd_notify" cmd/dashboard/mayhem*.go` yields only a hypothesis comment (mayhem_world.go:1219); every restart scenario in the inventory (hub-restart-mid-cap, northbound-restart-mid-breach, battery/solar-reboot, consumer-restart-after-quiescence) is a COMMANDED restart — nothing wedges a service and asserts systemd's WatchdogSec recovery, the behavior CLAUDE.md's Type=notify table says to 'verify via the northbound-hang/wan-outage Mayhem scenarios' (those verify the hold, not the restart). (2) plan heartbeat — `grep -rn "plan_heartbeat|stalled" cmd/dashboard/mayhem*.go` matches nothing relevant; no oracle ever reads /status.plan_heartbeat, so lexa-api's stall detector (cmd/api/heartbeat.go per CLAUDE.md) has never fired on the bench. (3) api auth — mayhem.go:235-237 uses bearer auth positively on every sample ('Bearer auth unchanged'); no negative-auth or no-token-refusal scenario exists (api_token_file startup refusal, TASK-014). (4) cert expiry — cert-rotation-failclosed covers rotation only; no scenario manipulates NotAfter or asserts lexa/northbound/certstatus / lexa_cert_expiry_* gauges (TASK-072).

**Proposed fix:** Add: a SIGSTOP-the-hub scenario asserting watchdog restart within WatchdogSec + retained-state re-seed; a hub-pause scenario asserting plan_heartbeat flips to 'stalled'; an unauthenticated /status probe asserting 401; a near-expiry cert fixture asserting the warn gauge.

### CC-7 [medium/process]
**Report §11 claim 'all 7 lexa services active' was cross-checked by no probe and is contradicted in scope by the session's own artifacts**

**Evidence:** QA report line 282: 'Verified: all 7 lexa services active'. The only continuous evidence stream, qa-bench-health.log, tracks FIVE services (`hub-svcs=[active active active active active ]` — hub/northbound/modbus/ocpp/api per report §6's own wording), never telemetry or openadr. lexa-openadr's bench deploy is still listed as bench-deferred in lexa-hub CLAUDE.md ('lexa-openadr deploy wiring' under Bench-deferred), the report's §11 config table has rows for hub/modbus/northbound/ocpp json but none for openadr.json, and the scratchpad's openadr.json + vtn.log show a half-configured VTN wiring (port mismatch 6030 vs 26030, vtnsim bind failure). None of the 14 probes examined whether telemetry/openadr were even running during the campaign. The claim may be true (end-of-session one-shot check) but nothing in the record supports it, and the sims — which DID die 3× (finding E) — were also outside the health cadence despite §10's own 'check the sims at every review' rule.

**Proposed fix:** Next bench visit: `systemctl status lexa-\*` capture into the repo; widen the health logger to all 7 services + all 4 sims; state monitor scope explicitly in future reports.

### CC-8 [medium/process]
**All raw evidence for the campaign (including the critical safety finding B) lives under /tmp, the QA report is untracked, and no open finding exists in any in-repo backlog — one reboot or a git clean erases the record**

**Evidence:** git status in lexa-hub: `?? docs/QA_SESSION_REPORT_2026-07-16.md` (untracked). The report's §13 says 'copy anything worth keeping into the repo' — never done: all 20 qa-run logs, QA_CAMPAIGN_FINDINGS.md, the pf/adv/evrule captures, and the health logs live only under /tmp/claude-1000/.../scratchpad, and this machine wipes /tmp on reboot (lexa-hub CLAUDE.md's own build note: 'arm64 wolfSSL sysroot (/tmp — wiped on reboot!)'). `grep -rn -i "soc-dither|boundary.dither|hold.bias|pagination" docs/standards-buildout/00_PROGRESS.md docs/*.md` (excluding the untracked report) returns zero hits — findings B/C/D/E are tracked in no board, backlog, or task file in either repo. Combined with the config-drift probe's finding that all 65+ session commits are unpushed, the entire campaign's record is one disk failure or reboot away from partial loss.

**Proposed fix:** Immediately: `git add docs/QA_SESSION_REPORT_2026-07-16.md`, copy QA_CAMPAIGN_{SUMMARY,FINDINGS}.md + the load-bearing capture logs into csip-tls-test/docs/qa-artifacts/, and file findings B–E into 00_PROGRESS.md / a backlog with owner+severity.

### CC-9 [medium/process]
**Bench left with enforce_aus_limits:true against the report's own revert instruction, and with the new two-sided PF code live under the exact config (advanced_der:on, reconciler.adv:active) in which the report says the PF axis is unjudgeable**

**Evidence:** Report §11 table: 'enforce_aus_limits | hub.json | true | I flipped this on for AUS coverage — revert to false for the pre-campaign default' — the instruction is written but the value was left true, so the demo hub now runs the WP-11 GenLimW/LoadLimW cascade that the pre-campaign demo never had (a behavior change to the standing demo, not just a QA setting). Simultaneously §11 leaves advanced_der:"on" + reconciler.adv:"active" with the freshly deployed 29e9552 lexa-modbus binary, while §2.2's own caveat says fixed_pf is only observable with advanced_der:off — i.e. the bench's standing configuration can neither exercise nor detect a regression in the newest deployed reconciler change (see CC-2). The config-drift probe covered redeploy-wipes-values; this is the complement: the values as LEFT diverge from both the pre-campaign demo state and the report's own instructions. Verified against the report text; on-device state not re-verified (read-only mandate, no SSH).

**Proposed fix:** Decide the demo's intended state explicitly (AUS on or off), set it, and record it in the committed bench profile the config-drift probe proposed; treat 'revert X after' notes as blocking wrap-up steps.

### CC-10 [low/process]
**Load-bearing pre-session dependency unaudited: lexa-proto 60bdb1b (chunked >125-register SunSpec reads) underlies the PF fix's model-701 measurements and both repos' pins, yet no probe reviewed it**

**Evidence:** The 14-probe digest covers commits e0864c9, 29e9552, fbcaca0, 3e907f2, and cf5d2b7 — not lexa-proto 60bdb1b, which the session report §1 lists as load-bearing context ('chunk SunSpec model reads >125 registers — the P0 "model 701 unreadable" bug'). lexa-hub git log: `da33264 fix(proto): bump lexa-proto -> 60bdb1b (sunspec chunks model reads >125 regs)`. 29e9552's two-sided convergence verdicts are computed from Parse701 measurements that only exist because of 60bdb1b's chunked reads — a subtle chunking bug (offset/scale-factor tearing across chunk boundaries) would surface as exactly the PF/var measurement noise the band-dither findings describe, and the config-drift probe already established this SHA exists on no remote. Absence verified (no probe in the digest names 60bdb1b); the risk itself is hypothetical.

**Proposed fix:** One targeted review of lexa-proto 60bdb1b's chunk-boundary arithmetic (scale factors and multi-register points straddling the 125-register split) plus a register-map fixture test, before treating PF/var measurement values as trustworthy inputs to convergence hardening work.

### CC-11 [low/test-blindspot]
**Entire campaign ran on the Yocto dev-kit's anonymous, ACL-less broker — the TASK-013/AD-008 MQTT auth/ACL boundary has never been exercised under fault load, and cannot be on this bench**

**Evidence:** lexa-hub CLAUDE.md (Current bench deployment / DEVKIT caveats): the dev kit's Yocto mosquitto has 'anonymous broker, no mosquitto_passwd/ACL on the box', and the config-drift probe confirmed deploy-hub-pi.sh aborts on Yocto at mosquitto_passwd. Every mqtt-family scenario in the soak (mqtt-broker-restart, mqtt-storm, mqtt-stale-retained, mqtt-malformed-control — all present in soak-batch files) therefore ran against an anonymous broker: the per-service credential connect path (mqttutil.ConnectAuth with real creds), ACL-denied publish handling, and the qa-inject user boundary have zero bench mileage. The product default (WS-1: allow_anonymous false + ACL) is a different broker posture than anything the campaign tested. Verified from CLAUDE.md + soak batch composition; no scenario output could contradict it since the broker cannot enforce auth.

**Proposed fix:** Run one mqtt-family batch against the STANDBY Pi's full auth+ACL broker (or add mosquitto with auth to the dev-kit image), specifically asserting reconnect-with-credentials during mqtt-broker-restart and an ACL-denied publish surfacing as an error metric, before the WS-1 default is relied on in production.
